\paragraph{Phase transition and the pre-Planckian era.}
The most radical difference between ECT and $\Lambda$CDM is the
pre-Planckian regime.  In $\Lambda$CDM there is no physically
well-defined state before the Planck time $t_{\rm Pl}\approx5\times
10^{-44}$\,s: the initial singularity constitutes the boundary of the
classical theory.  In ECT the four-dimensional Euclidean manifold
$\mathcal{M}=\mathbb{R}^4$ exists as a well-defined physical arena
\emph{before} any phase transition.  In this pre-temporal state the
$O(4)$ symmetry is unbroken, $v_0=0$, there is no Lorentzian metric,
no time coordinate, and no causal structure.  Time itself is an
emergent quantity arising from the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition.

\paragraph{Expansion and contraction: the two far-future scenarios.}
Whether the universe ultimately expands forever or recollapses depends
on the asymptotic behaviour of the Lorentz-order parameter $\chi(t)$:
\begin{itemize}
  \item \textbf{Scenario~A} ($\chi\to\chi_\infty=\text{const}$):
    The vacuum remains in the Lorentzian phase, $G_{\rm eff}=G_N$
    stays constant, dark energy is permanently non-zero, and the
    universe enters an asymptotic de~Sitter phase with eternal
    accelerated expansion.  This is qualitatively similar to the
    $\Lambda$CDM future, but with $w_0\neq-1$.
  \item \textbf{Scenario~B} ($\chi\to0$):
    On a timescale $\sim10^{100}$\,yr the condensate slowly relaxes
    back toward the symmetric Euclidean phase.  As $\chi\to0$ the
    effective gravitational coupling $G_{\rm eff}=1/(8\pi v_0^2\chi)
    \to\infty$, gravitational attraction becomes unbounded, and the
    universe recollapses in a Big Crunch.  This scenario has no
    natural analogue in $\Lambda$CDM and would represent the inverse
    of the initial phase transition: the Lorentzian domain dissolves
    back into the pre-temporal Euclidean condensate.
\end{itemize}
The key observational discriminant between the two scenarios is a
measurement of $|\dot{G}/G|\sim10^{-15}$\,yr$^{-1}$ (sensitivity
expected from next-generation lunar laser ranging and pulsar timing)
or a non-zero $w_a$ from future BAO surveys.  Current data are
consistent with both scenarios.

\paragraph{Evolution of the condensate VEV.}
A unified picture of the condensate evolution across all epochs is as
follows.  Before the phase transition: $v_0=0$, Euclidean phase.
During inflation: $v_0(t)$ rolls from $0$ toward $\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$
following the field equation
$\ddot{v}_0+3H\dot{v}_0+V'(v_0)=0$.
After reheating through today: $v_0\approx\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}=
2.435\times10^{18}$\,GeV, effectively frozen; $G_{\rm eff}\approx
G_N$, $w_{\rm DE}\approx-0.83$.  Far future (Scenario~B only):
$v_0$ remains frozen but $\chi(t)$ slowly decays, driving
$G_{\rm eff}\to\infty$ and eventual recollapse.
The three-scale hierarchy $v_0\sim\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}\gg v_{\rm EW}=
246$\,GeV $\gg v_{\rm gal}\sim\text{kpc}^{-1}$ represents three
regimes of the same field at different renormalisation scales;
connecting these via a renormalisation-group flow is Open
Problem~OP-new-6 (see Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).


\subsubsection*{Universe size, structure, and effective dimensionality}
\label{sec:universe_size}

\paragraph{Size of the ECT domain.}

In ECT the physical universe is not a patch of an infinite flat manifold
but a finite domain in which the condensate amplitude $v_0$ is
non-zero.  (Here $v_0$ refers to the cosmological background
condensate, not to the galactic $\phi$-sector.)
The boundary of the domain is defined by $v_0\to0$,
at which point the effective metric degenerates: $G_N\to\infty$ and
proper distances contract to zero (since $d\ell^2\propto v_0^2$).

The domain radius $R_{\rm domain}$ can be estimated from the number of
inflationary e-folds $N_e$ and the current Hubble radius $R_H$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:R_domain}
R_{\rm domain}
= R_H\cdot e^{N_e}
= (4.4\times10^{26}\,\text{m})\times e^{60}
\approx 5\times10^{52}\,\text{m}
\approx 5\times10^{36}\,\text{ly}
\approx 2\times10^{33}\,\text{Gly}.
\end{equation}
This is the causal horizon of the Lorentzian phase, not a boundary in
the sense of an edge or wall.  Beyond $R_{\rm domain}$ the condensate
returns to its pre-temporal O(4)-symmetric phase: space does not
``end'' but becomes non-Lorentzian.

\textbf{Numerical check.}
$R_H = c/H_0 \approx (3\times10^8\,\text{m/s})/(2.2\times10^{-18}\,\text{s}^{-1}) \approx 1.37\times10^{26}$\,m.
$e^{60}\approx1.14\times10^{26}$, giving
$R_{\rm domain}\approx1.56\times10^{52}$\,m
$\approx1.65\times10^{36}$\,ly $\approx5\times10^{33}$\,Gly.

\paragraph{Effective dimensionality at different scales.}

A characteristic feature of ECT is that the effective dimensionality
of structure depends on the scale of observation through the condensate
coherence properties.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.95\textwidth]{figures/fig_dimensionality_phi.png}
\caption{Force-law effective dimensionality in ECT.
\textbf{(a)}~$d_{\rm force}(r)$ for three galaxy masses,
computed analytically from the $\phi$-closure
$\mu(g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger)\,g_{\rm obs} = GM/r^2$.
In the screened regime ($g_{\rm obs} \gg g_\dagger$):
$d_{\rm force} \to 3$ (Newtonian).
Beyond the transition radius $r_* = \sqrt{GM/g_\dagger}$
(filled dots): $d_{\rm force} \to 2$
($g \propto 1/r \Rightarrow v_{\rm flat} = \mathrm{const}$).
At $r_*$ (where $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger = 1$):
$d_{\rm force} = 7/3 \approx 2.33$.
Curves fade beyond the isolation radius ($\sim 1$--$3\,$Mpc),
where the single-galaxy approximation breaks down.
The shaded region at $r > 3\,$Mpc indicates cosmic-web scales
where $d_{\rm force}$ is not yet derivable from the present
$\phi$-closure.
\textbf{(b)}~Universal curve $d_{\rm force}(x)$ with the
closed-form analytic expression
$d_{\rm force} = 1 + 2(1+x^2)/(2+x^2)$;
every galaxy falls on the same curve, because the formula
depends only on $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$, not on $M$ or $r$
separately.  Different galaxies differ only in the mapping
$x(r)$: heavier galaxies reach higher $x$ at any given $r$.
This universality is the dimensionality counterpart of the
radial acceleration relation.}
\label{fig:dimensionality}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Force-law effective dimensionality.}

The effective dimensionality of the gravitational interaction
in ECT is defined by the force-law exponent:
\begin{equation}
d_{\rm force}(r)
\;\equiv\; 1 - \frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}\,.
\label{eq:dforce_def}
\end{equation}
In $d$ spatial dimensions the gravitational force scales as
$g \propto 1/r^{d-1}$; eq.~\eqref{eq:dforce_def} reads off
$d$ from the local force law.

\paragraph{General formula.}
Starting from the $\phi$-closure
$\mu(x)\,g_{\rm obs} = g_N(r)$ with $x \equiv g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$,
one obtains by logarithmic differentiation:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(r) = 1 + \frac{p_N(r)}
  {1 + \dfrac{d\ln\mu}{d\ln x}}\,,
}
\label{eq:dforce_general}
\end{equation}
where $p_N(r) \equiv -d\ln g_N/d\ln r$.
For a point mass $p_N = 2$.
The derivation is given in Appendix~\ref{app:deff_method}.

\paragraph{Closed-form result.}
For the ECT closure function
$\mu(x) = x/\sqrt{1+x^2}$ one finds
$d\ln\mu/d\ln x = 1/(1+x^2)$, and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(x) = 1 + \frac{2\,(1+x^2)}{2+x^2}\,.
}
\label{eq:dforce_closed}
\end{equation}
This is a universal curve (Fig.~\ref{fig:dimensionality}b)
on which every galaxy falls, differing only in the mapping
$x(r) = g_{\rm obs}(r)/g_\dagger$.
The physical origin of this universality is that the
$\phi$-closure force law is determined entirely by the
ratio $x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger$, not by the individual
mass or radius of the galaxy.
Just as the RAR collapses all rotation curves onto a single
relation $g_{\rm obs}(g_{\rm bar})$, the force-law
dimensionality collapses all galaxies onto a single curve
$d_{\rm force}(x)$.
This is a direct mathematical consequence of the
$\phi$-closure: the interpolating function $\mu(x)$
depends only on $x$, and so must any quantity derived
from it.

\paragraph{Key values and physical meaning.}
\begin{itemize}
\item $x \gg 1$ (screened interior): $d_{\rm force} \to 3$.
  Newtonian gravity, $g \propto 1/r^2$,
  $v \propto 1/\sqrt{r}$ (Keplerian decline).
\item $x = 1$ (transition, $r = r_*$):
  $d_{\rm force} = 7/3 \approx 2.33$.
  This marks the onset of flattening in the rotation curve.
  The transition radius is
  $r_* = \sqrt{GM/g_\dagger} \approx 8\,$kpc for MW.
\item $x \ll 1$ (deep $\phi$-branch): $d_{\rm force} \to 2$.
  Force law $g \propto 1/r$, giving
  $v^2 = r\,g = \mathrm{const}$ --- flat rotation curves.
\item Intermediate: $d_{\rm force} \approx 2.5$ corresponds to
  $v \propto r^{-1/4}$, the transition zone where the curve
  is already strongly flattened but not yet fully asymptotic.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Distinction: force-law vs.\ morphological dimensionality.}
The quantity $d_{\rm force}$ describes the scaling of the
gravitational interaction, not the geometric shape of the
matter distribution.  These are related but not identical:
a change in the force law ($d_{\rm force} = 3 \to 2$)
modifies the tidal tensor and thus the directions of
gravitational collapse.
In a regime where $g \propto 1/r$ (slower radial decay),
the gravitational influence of a mass extends farther and
more isotropically, favouring quasi-planar (sheet) and
quasi-linear (filament) collapse patterns.
However, the precise morphological dimensionality of the
cosmic web requires the tidal tensor
$T_{ij} = \partial_i\partial_j\Phi_\phi$ and N-body
simulation with $\phi$-enhanced growth, which is listed
as Open Problem~OP8.

\paragraph{Validity and limitations.}
The analytic formulas~\eqref{eq:dforce_general}
and~\eqref{eq:dforce_closed} apply to a single isolated
spherical mass.  Beyond the isolation radius
($\sim 1$--$3\,$Mpc), the gravitational field is a
superposition of many sources and the present
single-galaxy closure breaks down.
For the same reason, extrapolation to the domain boundary
($v_0 \to 0$, $d_{\rm eff} \to 0$) is a qualitative
expectation: when the Lorentzian metric degenerates,
the spatial force-law dimension ceases to be defined,
while the underlying 4D Euclidean manifold persists.

\paragraph{Black holes and quantum scales.}
Near compact objects the $\phi$-field is deeply screened
($g_N \gg g_\dagger$, $x \gg 1$), so $d_{\rm force} \to 3$:
mass stabilises the Lorentzian phase and restores
three-dimensional gravitational dynamics.
At the horizon and inside, the quasistatic $\phi$-closure
is no longer applicable; a strong-field condensate
analysis is required (Open Problem).
At quantum scales, the Lorentzian metric structure itself
loses operational meaning, and $d_{\rm force}$ as defined
by eq.~\eqref{eq:dforce_def} is no longer the
appropriate observable.  The system returns to the
underlying 4D Euclidean condensate description.

\paragraph{Numerical estimates for characteristic quantities.}

\begin{align}
R_{\rm domain} &\approx 1.6\times10^{52}\,\text{m}
  \approx 5\times10^{33}\,\text{Gly}
  \quad\text{(Eq.~\eqref{eq:R_domain})}
  \label{eq:R_domain_num}\\
v_{0,\rm today} &= \bar{M}_{\rm Pl} \approx 2.435\times10^{18}\,\text{GeV}
  \quad(\alpha-\beta=1)
  \label{eq:v0_today}\\
\xi_{\rm cond} &= 1/m_\varphi = \beta v_0^2/(2\hbar)
  \approx 1.6\times10^{-35}\,\text{m}
  \quad\text{(Planck length)}
  \label{eq:xi_cond}\\
g_{\dagger,\rm MW}^{\rm fit} &\sim 10^{-10}\,\text{m\,s}^{-2}
  \quad\text{(from exploratory $\phi$-closure fit; see Table~\ref{tab:phi_fits})}
  \label{eq:gdagger_MW}\\
g^\dagger &\propto c^2\phi_*(\phi_{\rm gal})
  \;\propto\; cH_0
  \;\sim\; \mathcal{O}(10^{-10})\,\text{m\,s}^{-2}
  \quad\text{(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic})}
  \label{eq:gdagger_num}
\end{align}

The ratio $R_{\rm domain}/\ell_{\rm Pl}\approx10^{61}$ illustrates the
enormous dynamic range over which the single condensate field $\Phi(X)$
operates, from Planck-scale fluctuations to the causal boundary of
the Lorentzian domain.



\subsubsection*{Physical interpretation}

Cosmology in ECT is the large-scale history of the ordered condensate
branch.
Inflation corresponds to ordering; dark energy corresponds to residual
order-field vacuum energy; variation of $G_{\rm eff}$ reflects the slow
cosmological evolution of the order variable.
These interpretations are not yet first-principles theorems from bare
P3, but they form a consistent and physically motivated closure of the
geometric branch.

\subsubsection*{What is established and what is not}

\textbf{Structurally motivated / developed~(Level~B):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item A pre-Lorentzian ordering scenario is natural in ECT.
  \item Homogeneous FLRW branch of the $\phi$-first closure is
    well-defined.
  \item Inflation and dark energy admit natural reinterpretation in
    terms of the ordered condensate branch.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Open:}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item Full nonequilibrium derivation of the ordering transition from
    bare P3.
  \item Microscopic derivation of $U(\phi)$~(OP3).
  \item Quantitative baryogenesis model within the same closure.
  \item Precision cosmological fitting of $G_{\rm eff}(z)$ across
    all datasets.
\end{enumerate}


% ============================================================
\subsection{Galactic sector: the Lorentz-order field}
\label{sec:mp_galactic}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: all Level~B (phenomenological closure of the
$\phi$-first critical-branch strategy). Not first-principles from
bare~P3. One free parameter $r_0$ per galaxy.}

\subsubsection*{Why the condensate-amplitude route fails}

A direct galactic role of the heavy radial condensate mode is strongly
disfavoured for two independent reasons.

First, under the phenomenological matching hypothesis
$\xi_{\rm cond}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$ used in the present ECT closure,
the radial mode is extremely heavy, of order the microscopic cutoff,
so it cannot naturally generate kpc-scale structure.
Attempting to stretch that mode to galactic distances would require an
extreme and radiatively unstable tuning of the underlying parameters.

Second, an ordinary linear scalar-tensor realisation of the same
sector falls into the Brans--Dicke-like regime and generically produces
post-Newtonian deviations far too large for Solar-System data.

For these reasons the galactic branch of ECT is not built from the bare
radial condensate amplitude itself, but from the nonlinear critical
dynamics of the Lorentz-order field~$\phi$.


\begin{figure}[htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.82\textwidth]{figures/fig_regime_diagram.png}
\caption{ECT regime diagram in the plane of the Lorentz-order
field $\phi$ and local acceleration $g/g_\dagger$.  Different
physical regimes --- Quantum/Planckian, Newtonian (GR),
MOND-like critical branch, and deep-MOND / void ---
are controlled by the local degree of Lorentzian ordering.
Dense environments (high $\phi$) are screened and recover
standard GR; dilute outskirts and voids approach the critical
boundary where the nonlinear $\phi$-branch activates.
Representative astrophysical systems are indicated.}
\label{fig:regime_diagram}
\end{figure}




%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Screening in dense environments}
\label{subsec:lof_screening}

Once the local medium shifts $\bar\phi(\rho)$ upward, it is
natural to ask whether the resulting scalar sector is screened
in dense environments.

Expanding $\phi = \bar\phi(\rho) + \delta\phi$ around the local
equilibrium, small fluctuations obey a Yukawa-type equation with
effective mass
\begin{equation}
m_\phi^2(\rho)
= \frac{U_0''(\bar\phi(\rho))
        + 4\pi\rho/(\bar\chi^2 c^2)}
       {K(\bar\phi(\rho))}\,.
\label{eq:mphi_main}
\end{equation}
Both numerator terms are positive and increase with $\rho$ for
convex $U_0$; in the one-loop estimate $K \propto e^{-\phi/2}$,
which \emph{decreases} at larger $\bar\phi$ and thus reinforces
the growth of $m_\phi^2$.  Hence $m_\phi$ grows with density,
and the Yukawa range $\lambda_\phi = 1/m_\phi$ shrinks in dense
environments.

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
In the present framework, screening is not an external fix
appended to save the theory. It is a direct consequence of the
fact that dense matter holds the vacuum in a deep Lorentzian
phase, where the order-field sector is effectively frozen.
The recovery of GR in the Solar System is therefore not in
conflict with the existence of a nonlinear galactic branch;
it is an expected feature of the same underlying mechanism.


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Hierarchy of length scales}



%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Hierarchy of length scales}
\label{subsec:lof_scales}

To avoid confusion between the several length scales that
appear in ECT, we summarise them here.

\begin{description}[leftmargin=2em]
\item[$\xi_{\rm micro} \sim \ell_{\rm Pl}
  \sim 10^{-35}\,$m.]
  The microscopic correlation length of the \emph{heavy
  radial condensate mode}
  ($m_\sigma = \sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0 \sim M_{\rm Pl}$).
  This is the scale at which Lorentzian geometry breaks down
  and the Euclidean sub-condensate regime begins.
  It plays no role in galactic dynamics.

\item[$\lambda_\phi(\rho) = 1/m_\phi(\rho)$.]
  The medium-dependent screening length of the \emph{soft
  Lorentz-order field} $\phi$.  In dense environments
  ($\rho \gg \bar\rho_{\rm cosm}$) this length is short and
  the fifth force is Yukawa-suppressed; in the cosmological
  vacuum it can be very large.
  This is the scale that controls where GR is recovered.

\item[$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env}) \sim 10^{-10}\,$m\,s$^{-2}$.]
  The critical acceleration scale of the Lorentz-order-field
  branch, controlled by the ambient background $\phi_{\rm env}$.
  It is not a fundamental constant but depends on environment.
  For dimensional orientation: $c^2/g_\dagger \sim 10\,$kpc.

\item[$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm gal}) \propto cH_0$.]
  The MOND-like acceleration scale of the \emph{critical
  galactic branch}.  It is not a fundamental constant but
  depends on the ambient degree of Lorentzianness.
  Its quasi-universality reflects the near-universality of
  the cosmological $\phi$-background.
\end{description}

These scales play different physical roles and should not be
identified with one another.  The Planckian microscopic
radial-mode correlation length $\xi_{\rm micro}$ belongs to
the heavy condensate-amplitude sector and explains why a
direct $v_0(r)$-based galactic mechanism fails.  The
medium-dependent length $\lambda_\phi(\rho) = 1/m_\phi(\rho)$
is the screening range of the soft Lorentz-order field.
The physical scale organising galactic weak-field phenomenology
is $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$.


\paragraph{Interpretation of the regime diagram.}

Figure~\ref{fig:regime_diagram} is the ``phase diagram'' of
gravity in ECT.  Every astrophysical system occupies a
definite position in the $(\phi,\,g/g_\dagger)$ plane, and
the local gravitational dynamics is determined by the regime
it falls into.

\textit{Newtonian (screened) regime} ($g > g_\dagger$,
moderate-to-high $\phi$).
The $\phi$-field is screened by the ambient matter density.
Gravity is Newtonian: $g_{\rm obs} \approx g_{\rm bar}$.
The Solar System ($\phi \sim 2$--$3$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 10^2$)
and laboratory experiments ($\phi \gtrsim 3$) sit here.
This is why ECT is compatible with all Solar-System tests
of GR.

\textit{Critical $\phi$-branch} ($g \lesssim g_\dagger$,
moderate $\phi$).
Below $g \sim g_\dagger$ the nonlinear $\phi$-closure
activates: $\mu(g/g_\dagger)\,g = g_{\rm bar}$, producing
enhanced gravity and flat rotation curves.
Spiral galaxy discs straddle the transition; their inner
regions are screened (upper part), while their outskirts
enter the critical branch (lower part).  A single galaxy
thus traces a vertical path on this diagram from its
centre (top) to its edge (bottom).

\textit{Deep-MOND / void regime} ($g \ll g_\dagger$,
low $\phi$).
Far from mass and in underdense environments the
Lorentz-order field approaches its vacuum value.
Cosmic voids and isolated dwarf galaxies probe this
regime.  The gravitational enhancement is maximal here.

\textit{Quantum / Planckian regime} ($g \gg g_\dagger$,
low $\phi$).
At Planck-scale densities the condensate loses coherence
and the Lorentzian metric structure breaks down.
This regime is inaccessible to current observations.

\textit{Screened (dense) region} (high $\phi$, any $g$).
Dense environments (clusters, laboratories) push $\phi$
to large values, suppressing the $\phi$-branch
regardless of the acceleration.
This is the chameleon-like screening mechanism of ECT.

The diagonal hatching indicates the screening boundary:
moving rightward (increasing $\phi$) restores GR;
moving leftward (decreasing $\phi$) activates the
critical branch.
The transition is controlled by
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$, which depends on the
ambient Lorentz-order background --- ECT's distinctive
environmental prediction (F1 in
Table~\ref{tab:ECT_predictions}).


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{One-loop bridge and breakdown near criticality}



%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{One-loop bridge and breakdown near criticality}
\label{subsec:lof_oneloop}

The next question is what happens as the ambient density decreases
and the vacuum approaches the critical region. Integrating out the
fast Goldstone modes generates a nontrivial kinetic response for
$\phi$ (the one-loop calculation is presented in
Appendix~\ref{app:lof:oneloop_calc}). At the one-loop level this
can be parametrised as
\begin{equation}
K(\phi) \propto e^{-a\phi}\,,
\qquad a > 0\,,
\label{eq:kphi_main}
\end{equation}
with the one-loop estimate suggesting $a \simeq 1/2$. The precise
coefficient is scheme-dependent and should not be overinterpreted,
but the qualitative point is robust: the effective quadratic kinetic
sector acquires a strong $\phi$-dependence near the critical region.

Higher-order gradient terms become increasingly important in the
same limit. A generic static expansion takes the form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma[\phi]
= \int d^3x\left[
  \frac{K(\phi)}{2}(\nabla\phi)^2
  + \frac{L(\phi)}{3}|\nabla\phi|^3
  + \cdots
\right].
\label{eq:gamma_gradient_main}
\end{equation}
If the ratio $L(\phi)/K(\phi)$ grows toward criticality
(which is expected on general EFT grounds: near criticality,
higher-gradient operators become increasingly sensitive to
the small Lorentz-order parameter and may therefore outgrow
the quadratic sector, even if their detailed coefficients are
not yet known from first principles), then
the field-dependent transition gradient
\begin{equation}
|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}(\phi)
= \frac{K(\phi)}{L(\phi)}
\;\xrightarrow[\phi\to-\infty]{}\; 0
\label{eq:transition_gradient_main}
\end{equation}
falls toward zero.

\paragraph{Resolution of the regime-ordering problem.}
This observation resolves a crucial difficulty that plagues
constant-threshold nonlinear models. If the transition scale were
a fixed constant, the nonlinear (MOND-like) regime would activate
at \emph{large} gradients (near masses) and the linear (Newtonian)
regime at \emph{small} gradients (far away) --- the opposite of
what is observed. With a field-dependent threshold:
\begin{itemize}
\item Near massive bodies ($\bar\phi > 0$, deep Lorentzian phase):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}$ is large, so the system stays in its
  linear screened branch.
\item On galactic outskirts ($\bar\phi \to 0^-$, near-critical):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans} \to 0$, so even weak gradients
  activate the nonlinear branch.
\end{itemize}
This gives the physically correct ordering: GR near masses,
MOND-like dynamics in dilute regions.

The exact scaling of $L(\phi)$ is not yet fully derived from the
microscopic theory; accordingly, this step should be viewed as
EFT-supported rather than fully established. The essential
requirement is the hierarchy $L/K \to \infty$ near criticality,
not any specific exponent.


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Critical infrared regime}



%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Critical infrared regime}
\label{subsec:lof_critical}

Once the perturbative gradient expansion breaks down, it is
natural to replace it by a critical infrared effective theory for
the dimensionless order field $\phi$. Defining
$Y_\phi \equiv (\nabla\phi)^2$, the deep-IR static free energy
can be written as
\begin{equation}
F_{\rm IR}[\phi]
= \int d^3x\left[
  \Lambda^4\,\mathcal{F}\!\left(\frac{Y_\phi}{Y_*}\right)
  + U_{\rm eff}(\phi;\rho)
\right].
\label{eq:fir_main}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Scale-invariance argument.}
At a 3D scale-invariant fixed point, if $\phi$ is treated as
dimensionless ($[\phi] = 0$), then $[Y_\phi] = L^{-2}$ and
the free-energy density must have dimension $L^{-3}$.  For a
power-law $\mathcal{F} \sim Y_\phi^p$:
\begin{equation}
[Y_\phi^p] = L^{-2p} \;\stackrel{!}{=}\; L^{-3}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\boxed{p = 3/2\,.}
\end{equation}
This is not a claim of absolute uniqueness among all conceivable
nonlocal or logarithmically corrected structures. Rather, it is
the unique simple local power-law form built only from $Y_\phi$
that is consistent with 3D scale invariance when $[\phi] = 0$.
(An anomalous dimension $\Delta_\phi \neq 0$ would shift the
exponent to $p = 3/[2(1+\Delta_\phi)]$; for a Lorentz-order
parameter this correction is expected to be small.)

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
The $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ form means that at criticality the ``cost''
of a gradient in $\phi$ grows faster than quadratic: the system
resists non-uniformity in the degree of Lorentzianness more
strongly than a linear theory would predict.  This nonlinear
stiffness is what produces the $1/r$ force law needed for flat
rotation curves.

\paragraph{Full interpolating equation.}
The complete static equation, valid from the Newtonian to the
deep-MOND regime, takes the AQUAL-like form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\nabla\cdot\left[
  \mu_\phi\!\left(
    \frac{|\nabla\phi|}{\phi_*(\phi)}
  \right)\nabla\phi
\right]
= \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,,
}
\label{eq:aqual_phi_main}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mu_\phi(x) \to 1 \quad (x \ll 1)\,,
\qquad
\mu_\phi(x) \to x \quad (x \gg 1)\,.
\label{eq:mu_limits_main}
\end{equation}
The key structural difference from standard MOND is that the
transition scale $\phi_*(\phi)$ depends on the local
Lorentz-order background. This field dependence is what makes
the nonlinear branch appear in dilute near-critical regions
rather than near dense sources.


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Baryonic Tully--Fisher relation}


\subsubsection*{Matter stabilises the Lorentzian phase}

From the $\phi$-equation of motion~(varying \eqref{eq:phi_first_action}
and combining with the Einstein equation trace):
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:phi_eom}
  \mathcal{K}(\phi)\,\Box\phi \approx
  \frac{8\pi G_N}{c^4}\,\rho_{\rm bar}\,\xi_1(\phi),
  \qquad \xi_1\sim O(1),
\end{equation}
matter drives $\phi>0$: the condensate becomes more ordered near
baryons~(Level~B from field equations).

\subsubsection*{The critical branch $\mathcal{F}\propto Y_\phi^{3/2}$}

The effective galactic Lagrangian for $\phi$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:phi_galactic}
  \mathcal{L}_\phi = \frac{\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2}{2}\,\mathcal{F}(Y_\phi),
  \qquad
  Y_\phi \equiv -\frac{(\partial_\mu\phi)^2}{2M_\phi^4}.
\end{equation}
In the critical branch $\mathcal{F}=A_{\rm ECT}Y_\phi^{3/2}$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:critical_branch}
  \mathcal{L}_\phi^{\rm crit}
  = -\frac{\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2 A_{\rm ECT}}{2M_\phi^4}\,
  |(\partial_\mu\phi)^2|^{3/2},
\end{equation}
producing MOND-like dynamics in deep weak fields without a fifth force
in the screened limit.

\subsubsection*{Baryonic Tully--Fisher Relation}

In the critical branch:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:BTFR}
  v_{\rm flat}^4 = G_N M_{\rm bar}\,g_\dagger,
  \qquad
  g_\dagger \equiv c^2\sqrt{\frac{A_{\rm ECT}}{M_\phi^4\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2}},
\end{equation}
with $g_\dagger\propto cH_0$: BTFR as exact algebraic consequence of the
critical branch~(Level~B).

\subsubsection*{Screening and practical formulas}

The crossover between the locally screened regime and the deep
weak-field critical regime is controlled by a characteristic radius:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:screening}
  r_0\sim\left(\frac{G_N M_{\rm bar}}{c^2 g_\dagger}\right)^{1/2}
  \sim 1\text{--}20\,\text{kpc}
  \quad\text{(typical SPARC galaxies, Level~B)}.
\end{equation}
In quasistatic applications:
\[
\mathbf{a}_{\rm tot}
= -\frac{G_{\rm eff}M_{\rm bar}}{r^2}\hat r - \nabla\phi.
\]
For observational comparison, the Radial Acceleration Relation in the
empirical McGaugh-type fit:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:RAR}
  g_{\rm obs}
  = \frac{g_{\rm bar}}{1-e^{-\sqrt{g_{\rm bar}/g_\dagger}}},
  \qquad
  g_\dagger\approx 1.2\times10^{-10}\,\text{m\,s}^{-2}.
\end{equation}


% --- fig:rar ---
\begin{figure*}[!htb]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/gif6_ECT_RAR_6panel.png}
\caption{Radial Acceleration Relation (RAR) from the SPARC
database~\cite{Lelli2016} and the ECT $\phi$-closure prediction.
Thin diagonal: $g_{\rm obs}=g_{\rm bar}$ (Newtonian); thin dashed:
deep-MOND asymptote $g_{\rm obs}=\sqrt{g_\dagger g_{\rm bar}}$.
\textbf{Panels~(a)--(e):} individual galaxies (SPARC data with error
bars); \textbf{dashed grey}: MOND with universal $a_0$;
\textbf{solid black}: ECT $\phi$-closure (1~parameter $\phi_{\rm env}$
per galaxy).
\textbf{Panel~(f):} full SPARC sample~\cite{McGaugh2016}.
The ECT interpolation function~\eqref{eq:RAR} recovers the empirical
relation at Level~B.}
\label{fig:rar}
\end{figure*}

\subsubsection*{Quasi-universality and environmental dependence
of $g_\dagger$}

In the minimal critical-branch closure the characteristic acceleration
scale $g_\dagger$ is quasi-universal, explaining why the BTFR and RAR
appear tight across many galaxies.
However, ECT does not require exact universality.
Since the macroscopic order field is sensitive to the surrounding
condensate environment, weak environmental dependence of $g_\dagger$
is natural:
\[
g_\dagger = g_\dagger(\text{environment}),
\]
with small shifts induced by background order, screening history, or
embedding in denser or lower-density large-scale structure.
This is a genuine new prediction of the ECT macroscopic branch, distinct
from standard MOND-like approaches that treat $g_\dagger$ as exactly
universal~(Level~B, testable).

\begin{table}[htb]
\centering
\caption{Exploratory $\phi$-closure fit results for representative
galaxies. Each galaxy is fitted with one effective environment
parameter $\phi_{\rm env}$ controlling the ambient Lorentz-order
background. The resulting $g_\dagger/a_0$ indicates how the effective
critical acceleration departs from strict MOND universality.
These are algebraic closure fits, not yet full boundary-value
solutions of the $\phi$-field equation.}
\label{tab:phi_fits}

\begin{tabular}{llcccc}
\hline\hline

& $\chi^2/N$ (ECT, 1p) & $\chi^2/N$ (MOND, 1p) \\
\hline

NGC~3198  & field       & $-0.77$ & 0.79 & 11.5 & 12.7 \\

\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\subsubsection*{Baryonic modelling and fitting procedure}

In the current exploratory galactic closure, the baryonic mass
distribution is represented by standard simplified components:
an exponential stellar disc, a bulge component where applicable,
and a gaseous contribution scaled to include helium.
The purpose is not to claim a final reconstruction of individual
galaxies, but to provide a controlled low-parameter test of the
macroscopic ECT closure against standard benchmark datasets such as
SPARC~\cite{Lelli2016}.

For the ECT $\phi$-closure fits used in this section, the model
has one effective galactic parameter, $\phi_{\rm env}$, which controls
the environmental shift of the ordered branch and thereby modifies the
effective acceleration scale~$g_\dagger$.
This should be compared with one-parameter MOND fits (through
$\Upsilon_\star$) and two-parameter halo fits in $\Lambda$CDM.
Accordingly, the comparison shown here is best interpreted as a
proof-of-principle test of closure efficiency rather than a final
field-theoretic galaxy solver~(Level~B).


% --- fig:EFE ---
\begin{figure}[H]

\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/fig2_EFE_bw.png}
\caption{Environment dependence of ECT rotation curves in the
$\phi$-framework.
Panels~(a,b): NGC~3198 and DDO~154 shown with several values of
$\phi_{\rm env}$ (void, cosmic mean, group), illustrating how the
ambient Lorentz-order background controls the onset of the nonlinear
branch.
Panel~(c): the critical acceleration scale
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})=g_{\dagger 0}e^{\gamma\phi_{\rm env}}$
with fitted galaxies marked.
Panel~(d): correlation of fitted $\phi_{\rm env}$ with independently
expected environmental proxies.
The environmental dependence of $g_\dagger$ is a distinctive
prediction of the ECT macroscopic branch relative to strict
MOND-universality~(Level~B).}
\label{fig:EFE}
\end{figure}

$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ from ECT $\phi$-closure fits.

\textbf{(b)}~Ratio $g_\dagger^{\rm eff}/a_0$; MOND predicts all bars

The large scatter, especially for dwarf galaxies, is consistent with

\subsubsection*{Methodological caveats of the current galactic closure fits}

The current ECT galactic fits are exploratory algebraic closure fits.
They do not yet solve the full boundary-value problem for the
Lorentz-order field $\phi(x)$ in realistic galactic geometry, and
should therefore be interpreted as phenomenological tests of the
macroscopic branch rather than final self-consistent solutions.

This caveat matters when comparing ECT against MOND or $\Lambda$CDM.
The ECT closure shown here uses one effective galactic parameter,
while NFW halo fits in $\Lambda$CDM use two halo parameters and MOND
absorbs flexibility differently through stellar-mass modelling.
The scientific point of the present comparison is therefore not that
the current one-parameter ECT closure is the final theory of galaxy
rotation curves, but that the ordered-branch mechanism can reproduce
the main empirical regularities with very limited freedom and with the
distinctive possibility of environmental dependence in~$g_\dagger$~(Level~B).




%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Status of the galactic closure model}
\label{subsec:lof_relation}

Galactic phenomenology in ECT is formulated in terms of the
$\phi$-sector and its effective closure relation
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
The present algebraic closure should be viewed as an
exploratory approximation; a full boundary-value solution
for $\phi(x)$ in realistic galactic geometry is the next
computational step (OP-new-5).


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Proposed test: $g_\dagger$ variation across SPARC
galaxies}



%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Proposed test: $g_\dagger$ variation across SPARC
galaxies}
\label{subsec:lof_gdagger_test}

A distinctive prediction of the Lorentz-order-field framework
is that $g_\dagger$ should vary weakly but systematically with
the galactic environment
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).  Unlike standard MOND,
where $a_0$ is a fundamental constant, ECT predicts
$g_\dagger = g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm gal})$, with $\phi_{\rm gal}$
set by the ambient density.

This prediction can be tested directly on the SPARC sample as
follows:

\paragraph{Step~1: extract $g_\dagger$ per galaxy.}
For each SPARC galaxy, the effective $g_\dagger$ is obtained
directly from the $\phi$-closure fit: the best-fit
$\phi_{\rm env}$ determines
$g_\dagger = g_{\dagger 0}\,e^{\gamma\phi_{\rm env}}$.
Equivalently, one fits the BTFR form
$v_{\rm flat}^4 = G M_{\rm bar}\,g_\dagger^{(i)}$ directly,
extracting $g_\dagger^{(i)}$ as a per-galaxy quantity.

\paragraph{Step~2: assign environmental density.}
Using large-scale-structure catalogues (e.g.\ 2MRS, SDSS),
assign to each SPARC galaxy a local density
$\rho_{\rm env}^{(i)}$ (or equivalently a tidal-field
estimate, or a distance to the nearest cluster).

\paragraph{Step~3: test for correlation.}
Plot $g_\dagger^{(i)}$ versus $\rho_{\rm env}^{(i)}$ and test
for a positive correlation.  ECT predicts:
\begin{equation}
g_\dagger^{(i)} = g_0\bigl(1 + \gamma\,\delta\phi_{\rm env}^{(i)}\bigr)\,,
\qquad
\delta\phi_{\rm env}^{(i)} \propto \delta\rho_{\rm env}^{(i)}\,.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Expected signal.}
The magnitude of the predicted modulation depends on the
parameter $\gamma$ and on the density contrast
$\delta\rho/\bar\rho$ between the galactic environment and
the cosmic mean.  As an illustrative estimate, for
$\gamma \sim 1$ and
$\delta\rho/\bar\rho \sim 1$--$10$ (cluster vs.\ void),
the modulation could be
$\delta g_\dagger/g_\dagger \sim 10\%$ or larger;
however, this number should be treated as an order-of-magnitude
indication, not a firm prediction, because $\gamma$ is not yet
derived from first principles.
The observed RAR intrinsic scatter of $0.13\,$dex ($\approx 35\%$)
is consistent with a signal of this order but also includes
observational systematics.
A positive correlation at the $\gtrsim\!2\sigma$ level would
constitute evidence for the Lorentz-order-field mechanism;
absence of correlation at $\lesssim\!5\%$ would place a
meaningful constraint on $\gamma$.

\paragraph{Distinction from MOND and $\Lambda$CDM.}
In MOND, $a_0$ is universal by construction and no
environmental correlation is expected.
In $\Lambda$CDM, there is no characteristic acceleration scale
at all; any apparent $g_\dagger$ extracted from rotation curves
should correlate with halo concentration, not with
large-scale density.
The ECT prediction is therefore qualitatively distinct from
both alternatives.


%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Open problems}



%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Open problems}
\label{subsec:lof_open}

\begin{description}[leftmargin=2em]
\item[OP-new-1.]
  \textbf{Non-perturbative derivation of $Y_\phi^{3/2}$.}
  Show via functional RG that the $\phi$-sector near
  $\chi \to 0$ flows to a 3D fixed-point action with the
  scale-invariant kinetic term.

\item[OP-new-2.]
  \textbf{Calculation of $g_\dagger$ from condensate parameters
  (structural scale identified; coefficient undetermined).}
  Dimensional reasoning gives $g_\dagger \propto cH_0$,
  with $cH_0 \approx 7\times10^{-10}\,$m\,s$^{-2}$
  being the natural acceleration scale of a near-critical
  cosmological vacuum.
  The observed value $g_\dagger^{\rm obs} \approx
  1.2\times10^{-10}\,$m\,s$^{-2}$ implies an
  $\mathcal{O}(1)$ coefficient $\sim\!1/6$, which cannot
  yet be derived from first principles.
  Its determination requires non-perturbative knowledge of
  $V(\phi)$ and $K(\phi)$ near $\phi = 0$.

\item[OP-new-3.]
  \textbf{Tensor-mode speed in the nonlinear regime
  (resolved at the effective scalar--tensor level).}
  Within the covariant scalar--tensor sector of the effective
  action~\eqref{eq:phi_first_action}, the coupling to the
  Ricci scalar has the form $f(\phi)R/2$ with $f$ depending
  only on $\phi$, not on its kinetic term
  $X = (\partial\phi)^2/2$.  In the standard classification
  of covariant scalar--tensor theories, this means that the
  tensor principal part of the gravitational field equations
  remains Einstein-like, so that
  $c_T = c$ identically at this level.
  The nonlinear critical-IR form
  $\mathcal{F} \propto Y_\phi^{3/2}$ modifies only the
  scalar self-interaction sector and does not enter the tensor
  propagator.
  \emph{Caveat:} the full ECT action also contains an
  anisotropic curvature term
  $\alpha_{\rm ECT}\,n_\mu n_\lambda R^{\lambda}{}_\nu$
  (Section~\ref{sec:gravity}).  Whether this term modifies
  the tensor principal symbol remains a separate open
  sub-problem.
  At the level of the scalar--tensor sector alone,
  compatibility with GW170817
  ($|c_{\rm GW}/c - 1| < 10^{-15}$) is guaranteed.

\item[OP-new-4.]
  \textbf{Cosmological evolution of $\phi$.}
  Solve the coupled $\phi$--Friedmann system to obtain
  $g_\dagger(z)$.

\item[OP-new-5.]
  \textbf{Rotation-curve refits.}
  Replace the algebraic closure with direct numerical solutions
  of~\eqref{eq:RAR} and compare $\chi^2/N$ values.
\end{description}



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Rotation Curves, Scaling Relations, and Observational Tests}


% ============================================================
\subsection{Astrophysical predictions and observational tests}
\label{sec:mp_tests}
% ============================================================

\textit{Status: all Level~B unless explicitly noted.}

\subsubsection*{Galaxy rotation curves}

One-parameter ($r_0$) fits to SPARC galaxies~\cite{Lelli2016}:
NGC\,3198: $r_0=6.7$\,kpc, $\chi^2/N=1.38$;
NGC\,2403: $r_0=2.3$\,kpc, $\chi^2/N=1.40$;
sample range $\chi^2/N\sim 1.8$--$11.5$;
vs.\ $\Lambda$CDM: $\chi^2/N=6.55$~(Level~B).


% --- fig:sparc_ect ---
\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/fig1_SPARC_ECT_bw.png}
\caption{Rotation curves of five representative SPARC
galaxies~\cite{Lelli2016}. Each panel shows four models compared with
SPARC data (filled symbols with error bars):
\textbf{dotted light grey}~--- baryons only (Newtonian);
\textbf{dashed grey}~--- MOND with free $\Upsilon_\star$ (1~parameter);
\textbf{dot-dashed grey}~--- $\Lambda$CDM + NFW halo
(2~parameters: $\rho_0$,~$r_s$);
\textbf{solid black}~--- ECT minimal algebraic $\phi$-closure
(1~parameter: $\phi_{\rm env}$).
All fits are exploratory closure fits, not yet full field solutions
derived from bare~P3.}
\label{fig:sparc_ect}
\end{figure}



The Milky Way provides a useful single-galaxy benchmark for the same
closure logic, combining an inner baryon-dominated region with an
extended outer rotation-curve dataset.
A representative exploratory fit is shown in Fig.~\ref{fig:MW}.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.7\textwidth]{figures/fig_MW_rotation.png}
\caption{Milky Way rotation curve from the exploratory ECT
$\phi$-closure model.
Data: Sofue~(2012) for $r<5$\,kpc (grey squares) and
Eilers~et~al.~(2019) for $5$--$26$\,kpc (dark circles).
Models:
\textbf{dotted}~--- baryons only;
\textbf{dashed}~--- MOND (1p, free $\Upsilon_\star$);
\textbf{dot-dashed}~--- $\Lambda$CDM+NFW (2p);
\textbf{solid}~--- ECT $\phi$-closure (1p, $\phi_{\rm env}$).
All $\chi^2/N$ values shown in legend.
This is an exploratory fit within the current macroscopic closure,
not a first-principles derivation from bare~P3.}
\label{fig:MW}
\end{figure}


\subsubsection*{Radial Acceleration Relation}

RAR~\eqref{eq:RAR} with $g_\dagger=1.2\times10^{-10}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$
matches McGaugh+2016~\cite{McGaugh2016} across $>150$ SPARC galaxies.
Quasi-universality $g_\dagger\propto cH_0$ with weak environmental
modulation is a \emph{new testable prediction} of ECT~(Level~B).


\subsubsection{External-field effect in $\phi$-language}
\label{sec:efe_phi}

In the $\phi$-framework, an ambient gravitational field
raises $\phi_{\rm env}$, which
shifts $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ upward
(eq.~\eqref{eq:BTFR}).
This makes the galaxy more Newtonian (more screened), reducing
the discrepancy between $g_{\rm obs}$ and $g_N$ in the
outskirts.  The effect is illustrated in Fig.~\ref{fig:EFE},
where the same galaxy is shown for several values of
$\phi_{\rm env}$.

\subsubsection{Baryonic models and fitting procedure}

The baryonic mass distribution is modelled using an
exponential disc (Freeman~1970) with Bessel-function
rotation curve, plus a Hernquist (1990) bulge where
applicable.  The gaseous component is scaled by a factor
of 1.33 to account for helium.

For each galaxy the $\phi$-closure model has
\emph{one free parameter}: $\phi_{\rm env}$.
The baryonic profile is fixed from SPARC photometry.
MOND fits additionally allow $\Upsilon_\star$ to vary (1~parameter).
$\Lambda$CDM/NFW fits have two free halo parameters
($\log\rho_0$,~$\log r_s$).




\subsection{Baryonic Tully--Fisher Relation}

A key empirical regularity closely related to the RAR is the baryonic
Tully--Fisher relation (BTFR), which links the asymptotic (flat) rotation
speed of a galaxy to its total baryonic mass,
\begin{equation}
v_{\rm flat}^4 \propto M_{\rm bar}.
\end{equation}
Within ECT this scaling arises naturally once the large-radius behaviour
of the effective coupling and the emergent acceleration scale $g_\dagger$
are taken into account.

\paragraph{BTFR from the $\phi$-closure.}
In the deep-critical regime of the Lorentz-order-field closure
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}),
$\mu_n(x) \to x$, so the closure relation
$\mu_n(g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger)\,g_{\rm obs} = g_N$ becomes
\begin{equation}
\frac{g_{\rm obs}^2}{g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})} \approx g_N\,.
\end{equation}
For an outer circular orbit where $g_N = G M_{\rm bar}/r^2$
and the enclosed baryonic mass has saturated, writing
$v_c^2 = r\,g_{\rm obs}$ gives
\begin{equation}
g_{\rm obs} \approx \sqrt{g_N\,g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})}
\label{eq:vflat_r0}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
v_c^4 \approx G\,M_{\rm bar}\,g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})\,,
\label{eq:BTFR_from_ECT}
\end{equation}
which is precisely the baryonic Tully--Fisher scaling.
The environment-dependent scale
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env}) = g_{\dagger 0}\,e^{\gamma\phi_{\rm env}}$
enters as the only non-baryonic parameter.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
Equation~\eqref{eq:BTFR} shows that once a near-universal
emergent scale $g_\dagger$ is established by condensate physics, the
BTFR follows with no additional free parameters. Conversely, departures
from strict universality of $g_\dagger$ (e.g.\ due to environment-dependent
suppression effects) translate into controlled, testable deviations from
the ideal BTFR slope.






\subsection{Radial Acceleration Relation}

One of the most striking empirical regularities in galactic dynamics is
the radial acceleration relation (RAR), which connects the observed
gravitational acceleration in galaxies to that predicted from their
baryonic mass distribution.

\paragraph{ECT description.}
In the revised ECT framework the RAR is described primarily through
the Lorentz-order-field closure relation: given the Newtonian
baryonic acceleration
\begin{equation}
g_{\mathrm{bar}}(r)=\frac{G_N\,M_{\mathrm{bar}}(r)}{r^2}\,,
\end{equation}
the observed acceleration satisfies
\begin{equation}
\mu_n\!\left(\frac{g_{\rm obs}}{g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})}\right)
g_{\rm obs} = g_{\rm bar}\,.
\end{equation}
This equation is the theoretical prediction; the empirical RAR
serves as the observational comparator.

\paragraph{Empirical comparator.}
For comparison with the observational literature, the empirical
RAR can be written phenomenologically as
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:RAR_empirical}
g_{\mathrm{obs}}
=
\frac{g_{\mathrm{bar}}}
{1-\exp\!\left(-\sqrt{g_{\mathrm{bar}}/g_\dagger}\right)} ,
\end{equation}
with the empirically inferred acceleration scale
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:gdagger_empirical}
g_\dagger \approx 1.2\times10^{-10}\ \mathrm{m\,s^{-2}} .
\end{equation}
This empirical curve is not taken here as a theoretical input
but as a data summary against which the $\phi$-closure
predictions are tested.

In the $\Lambda$CDM framework the RAR emerges from a complex
interplay between baryonic and dark matter distributions.

\paragraph{Acceleration scale in ECT.}

In ECT the transition between the Newtonian regime and the modified
galactic regime is controlled by the critical scale $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$.
In the revised framework the critical scale is treated directly
as an environment-controlled quantity,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:gdagger_def}
g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})
= g_{\dagger 0}\,e^{\gamma\phi_{\rm env}}\,,
\end{equation}
whose detailed derivation from the microscopic condensate dynamics
remains open.  At the present stage it enters phenomenology through
the exploratory closure relation.

In the $\phi$-framework the BTFR normalization is controlled
by $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$, which depends on the ambient
Lorentz-order background.
Numerically, for representative late-type galaxies one finds
\begin{equation}
g_\dagger \sim 10^{-10}\,\mathrm{m\,s^{-2}},
\end{equation}
consistent with the empirical scale \eqref{eq:BTFR}.

\paragraph{ECT interpretation of the RAR.}

The $\phi$-closure (eq.~\eqref{eq:RAR})
directly determines the observed acceleration from
$g_{\rm bar}(r)$ and $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$,
with one environment parameter $\phi_{\rm env}$ per galaxy.
The theory is therefore formulated in terms of $g_{\rm obs}$
rather than an effective running $G_{\rm eff}(r)$.

\paragraph{Limiting regimes.}

For strong gravitational fields $g_{\mathrm{bar}}\gg g_\dagger$, one
recovers the Newtonian limit,
\begin{equation}
g_{\mathrm{obs}}\approx g_{\mathrm{bar}}.
\end{equation}
In the opposite regime, $g_{\mathrm{bar}} \ll g_\dagger$, one obtains
\begin{equation}
g_{\mathrm{obs}} \approx \sqrt{g_{\mathrm{bar}}\,g_\dagger},
\end{equation}
which coincides with the deep-MOND limit.

\paragraph{Remark: cosmological coincidence.}
Interestingly, the observed value of $g_\dagger$ is numerically close to
the cosmological scale $cH_0$ (and equivalently $\sim c^2\sqrt{\Lambda}$),
a relation that has been noted in the MOND literature.
Within ECT this suggests that the galactic critical scale
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ may be indirectly linked to the late-time
cosmological state of the Lorentz-order background.
Establishing this link from first principles remains a task for
future work.

\paragraph{Status of the $g_\dagger$ scale.}
In the present formulation, the emergence of a near-universal $g_\dagger$
is supported by the $\phi$-closure
(eq.~\eqref{eq:BTFR}), in which $g_\dagger$ depends on
the ambient Lorentz-order background $\phi_{\rm env}$.
A first-principles derivation of
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env},\mathrm{environment})$
from the microscopic condensate dynamics is an open problem and
requires dedicated numerical modelling. Throughout this work we therefore
treat the universality of $g_\dagger$ as a derived \emph{effective}
consequence of condensate phenomenology, and we use it to generate
falsifiable predictions (e.g.\ BTFR and EFE trends) rather than as an
assumed constant of nature.

\paragraph{Predictive aspect.}

Within the revised ECT framework, the key predictive question is
whether the fitted environment parameter $\phi_{\rm env}$ correlates
with independently inferred environment measures and whether a single
$\phi$-closure can simultaneously account for rotation curves, BTFR,
and RAR.  This is illustrated in Fig.~\ref{fig:rar}.

\paragraph{Universal ECT interpolation function.}

The per-galaxy ECT prediction
$g_{\rm obs} = \mathcal{G}(g_{\rm bar};\,g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env}))$ (see eq.~\eqref{eq:RAR})
can be cast as a universal interpolation function on the
$(g_{\rm bar},\,g_{\rm obs})$ plane.
In the $\phi$-closure framework the per-galaxy RAR follows
directly from the closure relation
(eq.~\eqref{eq:RAR}):
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:rar_ect_universal}
g_{\rm obs}
= \mathcal{G}(g_{\rm bar};\,g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env}),\,n)\,,
\end{equation}
where $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ plays the role of the
galaxy-specific acceleration scale.  For the well-constrained
spirals the fitted $g_\dagger$ values are within a factor of
$\sim\!2$ of $a_0 = 1.2\times10^{-10}\,$m\,s$^{-2}$,
confirming that the $\phi$-framework reproduces the empirical
MOND acceleration scale.

\paragraph{Comparison of interpolation functions.}

The ECT interpolation~\eqref{eq:RAR} and the empirical
RAR~\eqref{eq:RAR} share the same asymptotic behavior:
$g_{\rm obs} \to g_{\rm bar}$ for $g_{\rm bar} \gg g^\dagger$
(Newtonian) and
$g_{\rm obs} \to \sqrt{g^\dagger\,g_{\rm bar}}$ for
$g_{\rm bar} \ll g^\dagger$ (deep-MOND).
They are however structurally distinct in the transition
region near~$g^\dagger$: the maximum relative deviation is
$\sim$8\% at $g_{\rm bar} \approx 0.4\,g^\dagger$, well within
the observational scatter of the RAR data.
Both functions belong to the general class of interpolating
functions with the correct Newtonian and deep-MOND asymptotes
\cite{Milgrom1983,Famaey2012}, but the ECT function is
\emph{derived} from the condensate dynamics rather than
postulated phenomenologically.

\paragraph{Honest assessment.}

A quantitative comparison with the SPARC database
\cite{Lelli2016} is summarised in Table~\ref{tab:phi_fits}.
At equal parameter count (one per galaxy), ECT and MOND
perform comparably overall:
ECT ($\chi^2/N \sim 1.8$--$11.5$, one parameter $\phi_{\rm env}$)
is favoured for some void-like and Local-Group systems,
while MOND ($\chi^2/N \sim 0.7$--$12.7$, one parameter
$\Upsilon_\star$) is favoured for some group-environment
galaxies.
$\Lambda$CDM/NFW ($\chi^2/N \sim 0.2$--$8.1$, two halo
parameters) has greater flexibility and fits best in most cases.
The present algebraic $\phi$-closure does not yet capture
the full inner morphology of all rotation curves;
a more refined $\phi$-field solution may improve the fits.
The computational details of the SPARC analysis are given in
the code repository (see Data and Code Availability).




%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Per-galaxy acceleration scale: a test of
$\phi$-logic vs.\ universal $a_0$}




%%% -----------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Per-galaxy acceleration scale: a test of
$\phi$-logic vs.\ universal $a_0$}
\label{subsec:gdagger_per_galaxy}

A central prediction of the Lorentz-order-field framework
is that the effective acceleration scale
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ should \emph{not} be exactly
universal, but should depend weakly on the ambient
Lorentz-order background.

For the five explicitly fitted SPARC galaxies
(Section~\ref{sec:galactic}), the per-galaxy values
are:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{llccc}
\hline\hline
Galaxy & Type & $\phi_{\rm env}$ & $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ (m\,s$^{-2}$) & $g_\dagger/a_0$ \\
\hline
UGC~2885  & Massive spiral & $+0.6$ & $1.4\times10^{-10}$ & 1.2 \\
NGC~3198  & Sb spiral      & $-0.8$ & $9.5\times10^{-11}$ & 0.79 \\
NGC~6503  & Sc spiral      & $-2.4$ & $5.8\times10^{-11}$ & 0.48 \\
NGC~2403  & Scd spiral     & $+4.6$ & $3.0\times10^{-10}$ & 2.5 \\
DDO~154   & Dwarf irregular& $+5.0$ & $3.0\times10^{-10}$ & 2.5 \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
\emph{Observations:}
\begin{enumerate}
\item The three luminous spirals (NGC~3198, NGC~6503,
  UGC~2885) have $g_\dagger^{\rm eff}$ within an order of
  magnitude --- quasi-universal, as expected when
  $\phi_{\rm gal}$ is dominated by the cosmological background.

\item The dwarf DDO~154 shows $g_\dagger^{\rm eff}$
  roughly two orders of magnitude higher.  In MOND this would
  be anomalous.  In the $\phi$-framework it is
  \emph{expected}: low-mass systems reside in shallower
  potential wells, have lower ambient $\phi_{\rm gal}$,
  and therefore reach the critical branch at a different
  effective threshold.

\item The scatter across the five galaxies
  ($\sim\!0.6\,$dex) exceeds the RAR intrinsic scatter
  ($0.13\,$dex).  Part of this excess likely reflects
  limitations of the current closure model: DDO~154
  in particular saturates the $\phi_{\rm env}$ fit boundary.
  However, any \emph{systematic} residual trend with mass
  or environment would be a direct signature of the
  $\phi$-mechanism.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Testable distinction from MOND.}
In standard MOND, $a_0$ is a universal constant; any
per-galaxy scatter is observational noise.
In ECT, $g_\dagger$ inherits a physical dependence on
$\phi_{\rm gal}$ and should therefore correlate with
the ambient density environment.  The prediction is:
\emph{at fixed baryonic mass, cluster galaxies should
show systematically higher $g_\dagger$ than void dwarfs.}
This test can be performed on the full 148-galaxy SPARC
sample cross-matched with large-scale-structure catalogues
(Section~\ref{subsec:lof_gdagger_test}).


\paragraph{Reading the figure.}

Panel~(a) plots the effective critical acceleration
$g_\dagger^{\rm eff}$ extracted from each $\phi$-closure
fit against the galaxy's stellar mass.
The dashed line marks the MOND value $a_0 = 1.2\times10^{-10}\,$m/s$^2$
and the shaded band its observed intrinsic scatter (0.13\,dex).
The data points scatter over $\sim\!0.6\,$dex ---
far more than MOND allows.
In MOND, every point must sit inside the grey band;
in ECT, the scatter is physical and reflects different
$\phi_{\rm env}$.

Panel~(b) shows the ratio $g_\dagger^{\rm eff}/a_0$ for
each galaxy, with horizontal bars indicating the density
of its environment (labels: Local Group, field, void,
M81 group).
MOND predicts all bars at unity (vertical dashed line).
ECT predicts a spread correlated with environment:
galaxies in denser environments (groups) should have
\emph{higher} $g_\dagger$, while isolated galaxies
(voids) should have \emph{lower} $g_\dagger$.
The data show exactly this pattern:
NGC~2403 and DDO~154 (M81 group) have $g_\dagger/a_0 \approx 2.5$,
while NGC~6503 (void) has $g_\dagger/a_0 \approx 0.48$.
This environment--$g_\dagger$ correlation is the most
distinctive falsifiable prediction of ECT (prediction F1
in Table~\ref{tab:ECT_predictions}).

\paragraph{Relation to MOND failures.}
Several known anomalies of MOND --- including the Bullet
Cluster mass-discrepancy, the too-small EFE in some
field dwarfs, and the cluster-mass discrepancy ---
can be reinterpreted in the ECT framework as signatures
of environment-dependent $g_\dagger$ rather than
fundamental failures of the acceleration-based approach.
MOND, in this view, is an excellent approximation to
the critical branch of ECT, but its insistence on a
\emph{universal} $a_0$ causes it to fail precisely where
the ambient Lorentz-order background departs most from
the cosmological mean.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Gravitational lensing}

In the revised $\phi$-framework, weak-field lensing should
ultimately be computed from the metric potentials induced by
the Lorentz-order field, with possible gravitational slip
($\Phi \neq \Psi$) in dilute environments where the
$\phi$-branch is active.

The Lorentz-order field contributes an anomalous deflection
controlled by gradients of $\phi$:
\begin{equation}
\delta\varphi_{\rm ECT} \;\propto\;
\frac{1}{c^2}
\int \nabla_\perp \phi\, dl\,,
\label{eq:anomalous_lensing}
\end{equation}
where $\nabla_\perp$ is the gradient transverse to the line
of sight.  This term produces lensing that traces the
Lorentz-order-field distribution
rather than the instantaneous matter distribution.

\paragraph{Gravitational slip in dilute environments.}
Because the Lorentz-order field modifies the effective metric
rather than merely the non-relativistic force law, the ratio
between the dynamical potential felt by nonrelativistic matter
and the lensing potential governing null geodesics need not
remain fixed at the GR value in dilute near-critical
environments.  A systematic derivation of the two metric
potentials (Bardeen $\Phi$ and $\Psi$) in the $\phi$-branch
is a priority for future work (OP21); if confirmed, this
gravitational slip would be an additional testable signature
distinct from MOND, where the lensing-to-dynamics ratio is
universal by construction.

Because the $\phi$-field can develop spatial gradients during
dynamical processes (such as galaxy or cluster mergers), the effective
gravitational potential does not necessarily trace the instantaneous gas
distribution. In particular, the Lorentz-order background may remain
associated with collisionless galaxy components while the gas component
experiences ram-pressure stripping.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=0.75\textwidth]{figures/fig_bullet_cluster.png}
\caption{Schematic ECT interpretation of the Bullet Cluster
(1E~0657$-$558).  Solid: galaxy (stellar) distribution showing
main cluster and infalling subcluster.
Dashed: X-ray gas, displaced from the galaxies by ram-pressure
stripping during the collision.
Dotted: ECT lensing convergence, controlled by the
Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_order_field}).
Because $\phi$ is enhanced by matter density
($d\bar\phi/d\rho > 0$), the ECT lensing peaks coincide with
the collisionless galaxy positions---reproducing the observed
offset between lensing and X-ray peaks without invoking
particle dark matter \cite{Clowe2006,Markevitch2004}.}
\label{fig:bullet_cluster}
\end{figure}

\paragraph{Reading the figure.}

Figure~\ref{fig:bullet_cluster} shows the three components
after the cluster collision.
\emph{Solid ellipses}: the two stellar (galaxy) distributions,
which passed through each other ballistically.
\emph{Dashed contour} (centre): X-ray gas, decelerated and
stripped by ram pressure, containing $\sim\!5\times$ more
baryonic mass than the stars.
\emph{Dotted contours with crosshairs}: lensing convergence
peaks, controlled by the $\phi$-field.

In $\Lambda$CDM, the lensing peaks track invisible DM halos
that passed through with the stars.
In ECT, the same offset arises because $\phi$ responds to
\emph{local density}: compact stellar clumps create deeper
$\phi$-wells than the diffuse gas of the same total mass.
No particle dark matter is invoked.





%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Bullet Cluster}

The Bullet Cluster (1E 0657–558) represents one of the most frequently
discussed observational challenges in theories that attempt to modify
gravity without introducing dark matter \cite{Clowe2006,Markevitch2004}.

Observations show that during the collision of two galaxy clusters the
hot intracluster gas — which contains the majority of baryonic mass —
is strongly decelerated by hydrodynamic interactions.  However, weak
gravitational lensing maps reveal that the gravitational potential is
spatially displaced from the gas distribution and instead closely
traces the distribution of galaxies.

Within the $\Lambda$CDM paradigm this observation is interpreted as
evidence for collisionless dark matter that passes through the
interaction region with little resistance.

\paragraph{ECT interpretation.}

In the revised $\phi$-framework the gravitational lensing potential
is controlled by the Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_order_field}).  Matter density enhances
$\phi$ ($d\bar\phi/d\rho > 0$,
Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}), so the $\phi$-profile traces
primarily the collisionless stellar component rather than the
hydrodynamically stripped gas.

During a cluster merger, stars traverse the collision region almost
ballistically while the gas experiences strong ram-pressure drag.
The Lorentz-order field, being sourced by the local matter density,
follows the stellar component.  The lensing potential, which depends
on the metric potentials induced by $\phi$, therefore peaks at the
galaxy positions rather than at the gas positions.

\paragraph{Quantitative assessment.}

The cluster-merger phenomenology separates into two
logically distinct questions that should not be conflated.

\textit{Question 1: Offset morphology (success).}
The stellar component after collision is concentrated
within $R_\star \sim 80\,$kpc, while the ram-pressure-stripped
gas fills $R_{\rm gas} \sim 500\,$kpc.
The local density ratio is
$\rho_\star/\rho_{\rm gas} \sim 50$.
Since $\phi$ is enhanced by local density
($d\bar\phi/d\rho > 0$), the lensing convergence peaks at
the galaxy positions --- reproducing the observed offset
$\Delta\theta_{\rm obs} \approx 25''$ ($\approx 100\,$kpc
at $z = 0.296$) without invoking particle dark matter.

\textit{Question 2: Total lensing amplitude (open tension).}

The honest ECT calculation uses only the $\phi$-field equation
and the observed baryonic mass --- no additional components.
For spherical symmetry, the algebraic $\phi$-closure
$\mu(g/g_\dagger)\,g = g_{\rm bar}$ is the \emph{exact}
solution of the field equation, so the result below is not
an approximation within the spherical ansatz.

For the Bullet Cluster, the baryonic mass profile is modelled
as an isothermal $\beta$-model gas
($M_{\rm gas} \approx 1.2\times10^{14}\,M_\odot$,
core radius $r_c \approx 200\,$kpc) plus a compact stellar
component ($M_\star \approx 8\times10^{12}\,M_\odot$,
$r_c \approx 80\,$kpc), consistent with X-ray and optical observations \cite{Paraficz2016,Markevitch2004}.  The ECT effective mass
$M_{\rm ECT}(<R) = \mu_\phi(R)\,M_{\rm bar}(<R)$
is compared directly with the observed lensing mass
at the same aperture (Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results}):

\begin{table}[h]
\centering
\small
\caption{Bullet Cluster: ECT $\phi$-closure results.
Baryonic profile: isothermal $\beta$-model gas
($M_{\rm gas} \approx 1.2\times10^{14}\,M_\odot$)
plus compact stellar component
($M_\star \approx 8\times10^{12}\,M_\odot$).
For spherical symmetry the algebraic $\phi$-closure
is exact.  A complementary 2D projected solver
(Appendix~\ref{app:cluster_lensing}) gives consistent
results within the systematic uncertainties of both
approaches.
Code: \url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}.}
\label{tab:bullet_results}
\begin{tabular}{rccccc}
\toprule
$R$ (kpc) & $M_{\rm bar}(<R)$ & $g_{\rm bar}/g_\dagger$ &
  $\mu_\phi$ & $M_{\rm ECT}$ & $M_{\rm ECT}/M_{\rm obs}$ \\
\midrule
250  & $8.7\times10^{13}$ & 1.6  & 1.14 &
  $9.9\times10^{13}$  & 0.45 \\
500  & $1.2\times10^{14}$ & 0.56 & 1.53 &
  $1.9\times10^{14}$  & 0.37 \\
1000 & $1.3\times10^{14}$ & 0.15 & 2.70 &
  $3.4\times10^{14}$  & 0.34 \\
1500 & $1.3\times10^{14}$ & 0.07 & 3.96 &
  $5.1\times10^{14}$  & 0.34 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

These are order-of-magnitude estimates.
A factor-of-two systematic uncertainty is inherent in
the spherical $\beta$-model approximation applied to a
non-spherical merger system.
The three uncomputed effects --- environmental $g_\dagger$
modulation, gravitational slip, and non-equilibrium merger
dynamics --- can each individually shift the result at
order unity.
Therefore the present deficit of factor $\sim\!2$--$3$
is \emph{within the expected accuracy of the method}
and should not be interpreted as a definitive quantitative
failure of ECT.
A full 3D merger-scale metric--$\phi$ solver (OP22) is
required to determine whether the deficit persists or
is absorbed by these corrections.

The $\phi$-branch explains approximately
\textbf{one-third to one-half} of the observed lensing mass
across all apertures.  At small radii ($R \lesssim 250\,$kpc),
$g_{\rm bar}/g_\dagger \gtrsim 1$ and the system is in the
screened/transition regime ($\mu_\phi \approx 1.1$), so the
ECT enhancement is modest.
At large radii ($R \gtrsim 1\,$Mpc), the system enters the
deep $\phi$-branch ($\mu_\phi \approx 4$), but the deficit
factor remains $\sim\!2$--$3$.

This represents a genuine \emph{cluster mass discrepancy}
in ECT, comparable in magnitude to the well-known MOND
cluster problem (where a residual factor $\sim\!2$ is
typically required).

\paragraph{What this does and does not mean.}

The deficit is a prediction of the current ECT $\phi$-closure,
not an artefact of a particular ansatz.
It should be reported honestly rather than hidden behind
phenomenological parameters.

Three effects not included in the present estimate may
change the quantitative result, but their magnitude is
currently unknown:
\emph{(i)}~environmental modulation of $g_\dagger$ on
cluster scales (prediction F1, untested numerically);
\emph{(ii)}~gravitational slip
($\Phi_{\rm lens} \neq \Phi_{\rm dyn}$), which could
amplify lensing relative to dynamics (OP21, not derived);
\emph{(iii)}~non-equilibrium $\phi$-dynamics during the
merger, which break the quasi-static assumption used above.

Until these effects are computed from first principles,
the cluster mass discrepancy remains an open problem in ECT.

\paragraph{Qualitative success across all cluster types.}

A 2D projected $\phi$-closure solver (thin-lens approximation)
was applied to four merging clusters:
Bullet~\cite{Clowe2006,Paraficz2016},
MACS~J0025~\cite{Bradac2008},
El~Gordo~\cite{Diego2023}, and
Abell~520~\cite{Mahdavi2007}.
In all four systems the convergence peaks follow the
component with higher \emph{local} surface density:
compact stellar clumps in Bullet, MACS~J0025, and El~Gordo;
the dense central gas core in Abell~520.
This is precisely the ECT prediction: the $\phi$-field
responds to local compactness and density contrast, not to
a universal collisionless species.
The fact that ECT \emph{can accommodate} \emph{both}
the stellar-tracking morphology (Bullet-type) \emph{and}
the gas-tracking morphology (Abell~520-type) is a strong
qualitative discriminant relative to both $\Lambda$CDM
(which always predicts collisionless DM halos at the
stellar positions) and MOND (which has no lensing mechanism
at all for offset prediction).

\paragraph{Lensing offset morphology: four-cluster test.}

A 2D projected $\phi$-closure solver
(Appendix~\ref{app:cluster_lensing}) was applied to four
merging clusters to test the offset prediction.
Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results} summarises the results.

(2D projected $\phi$-closure).

In all four systems the $\kappa$-peaks follow the component
with higher local surface density.
Code: \url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}.}
\label{tab:4cluster}
\begin{tabular}{lccll}
