\end{tabular}
\end{table}


\paragraph{Limitations of the present estimate.}

The values of $R_{\rm cl}$ in
Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results} should be understood as
order-of-magnitude indicators, not precision results.
The current calculation relies on several simplifications
whose combined effect could shift the numbers by a factor
of $\sim\!2$ in either direction.

\textit{(i) Algebraic closure vs.\ field solution.}
The $\phi$-closure $\mu(g/g_\dagger)\,g = g_{\rm bar}$
is an algebraic relation derived for quasi-static,
spherically symmetric systems.
A cluster merger is neither static nor spherical.
The full calculation requires solving the nonlinear
field equation
$\nabla\!\cdot\![\mu_\phi(|\nabla\phi|)\,\nabla\phi]
= S[\rho_{\rm bar}]$
on a 2D/3D grid, which can concentrate the $\phi$-response
differently from the algebraic proxy.

\textit{(ii) Lensing $\neq$ dynamics.}
The numbers above assume that the lensing enhancement
equals the dynamical enhancement.
In a scalar-tensor theory the lensing potential
$(\Phi + \Psi)/2$ can differ from the dynamical potential
$\Phi$ by a gravitational slip factor.
Even a modest slip $\eta \equiv \Psi/\Phi \neq 1$ would
amplify the lensing signal relative to the dynamical one,
potentially closing part of the residual.

\textit{(iii) Non-stationarity and merger memory.}
The Bullet Cluster is a dynamical collision, not a
relaxed system.
The $\phi$-field may retain memory of the pre-collision
configuration, producing transient gradients that enhance
the lensing signal at the positions of the compact
collisionless clumps.
This effect is absent in any quasi-static estimate.

\textit{(iv) Aperture sensitivity.}
The baryon fraction $f_b$ depends critically on the
aperture in which it is measured.
For the Bullet Cluster, $f_b$ ranges from $\sim\!0.04$
at $R_{200}$ to $\sim\!0.22$ within 250\,kpc.
This factor-of-five variation directly propagates into
$\mathcal{E}_{\rm req}$ and $R_{\rm cl}$.
The values in Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results} use
aperture-matched $f_b$ from recent JWST and strong-lensing
analyses, but these carry systematic uncertainties of
order 30--50\%.

\textit{(v) Cluster-specific physics.}
Each system has distinctive features that a single
$\mu_{\rm cl}$ cannot capture:
the Bullet Cluster has an unusually high-velocity collision
($v \sim 4700\,$km/s) that maximises the gas--stellar
separation;
Abell~520 has a dense gas core that \emph{coincides}
with the lensing peak (opposite to Bullet), which in ECT
is natural because $\phi$ follows local density regardless
of whether the dense component is stellar or gaseous;
MACS~J0025 has a very low stellar fraction, making it the
hardest case for any modified-gravity explanation;
El~Gordo at $z = 0.87$ probes a higher-redshift
$\phi$-background where $g_\dagger(z)$ may differ from
the local value (prediction~F10).

The present factor-of-few cluster tension should therefore
not be interpreted as a definitive failure of ECT.
At the same time, it is too large to be dismissed as a
minor approximation error.
A full 2D/3D merger-scale $\phi$-solver is required to
determine whether the Bullet Cluster can be saturated by
the $\phi$-branch alone or whether a residual collisionless
condensate sector is necessary (OP22, OP23).

\paragraph{Comparison with modified-gravity models.}

In purely geometric modifications of gravity the gravitational
potential is typically tied directly to the baryonic mass
distribution.  Such models therefore have difficulty explaining
the separation between gas and gravitational lensing signal.
In ECT the additional condensate degree of freedom naturally
introduces a dynamical mechanism allowing the potential to
follow the collisionless component.

\paragraph{Observational tests.}

A characteristic prediction of this scenario is that the displacement
between the lensing peak and the gas should correlate with the
fraction of collisionless matter in the system.
Future observations of cluster mergers could therefore provide a
quantitative test of the model.





\paragraph{Remark: effective dark-sector phenomenology from the condensate.}
In the Lorentz-order-field framework the above astrophysical
effects arise from the environment-dependent nonlinear response
of the vacuum order parameter $\phi$, without introducing
additional collisionless particle matter.  Whether ECT also
predicts independent dark-sector degrees of freedom (e.g.\
Goldstone modes or topological objects) is a separate question
discussed in Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}.







\section{Cosmological Implications}


\subsubsection*{Gravitational lensing}

Within the weak-field $\phi$-first closure, lensing receives a
schematic correction from spatial variation of the effective
gravitational response:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:lensing_ect}
  \delta\alpha_{\rm ECT}
  \sim \frac{4G_N M}{c^2 b}
  \left(1+\frac{\partial\ln G_{\rm eff}}{\partial\ln r}\right),
\end{equation}
where $b$ is the impact parameter.
This should be read as a schematic weak-field estimate, not a completed
lensing theorem of the full condensate theory~(Level~B).

\subsubsection*{Bullet Cluster as a qualitative test case}

The Bullet Cluster is an important qualitative test for any
modified-gravity or emergent-gravity proposal.
In ECT the ordered condensate can in principle generate an offset between
baryonic gas and the effective lensing centre through the
environment-dependent response of the macroscopic branch.
This provides a \emph{possible condensate-based interpretation} without
requiring standard particle dark matter.
The correct current status is Level~B / qualitative:
ECT offers a viable interpretive route, but not yet a completed
cluster-scale quantitative fit.


% --- fig:bullet_cluster ---




\subsubsection*{Hubble tension and ISW}

$G_{\rm eff}(z)=G_N(1+z)^{2\varepsilon}$, $\varepsilon\approx 0.01$:
shifts $H_0$ by $\sim 3$\,km\,s$^{-1}$\,Mpc$^{-1}$, partially
alleviating the Hubble tension~(Level~B).
ISW excess in voids is amplified by larger $G_{\rm eff}$ in
low-density regions~(Level~B).
CMB quadrupole deficit: $\delta C_2/C_2\sim e^{-2\pi}\approx 0.19$
(observed $\approx 0.13$; 30\% agreement)~(Level~B).

\subsubsection*{Black holes and compact objects}

Compact-object implications of the macroscopic branch remain exploratory.
One representative phenomenological estimate in the current closure
gives a neutron-star maximum mass:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:ns_mass}
  M_{\rm max}\approx 2.17\,M_\odot,
\end{equation}
consistent with the observational scale set by PSR\,J0740+6620
($2.14\pm0.09\,M_\odot$~\cite{Cromartie2019,Riley2021})~(Level~B).

Possible black-hole implications of the ordered condensate branch are
important, but they are not yet part of the present controlled
macroscopic derivation and should be treated as a future subsection.
For GW-related LIV effects the estimate of Section~\ref{sec:mp_gw}
applies: the expected propagation-time shift
$\Delta t_{\rm GW}\lesssim 10^{-64}$\,s is negligible for all
currently observed sources.



\subsection{Dark Sector Phenomenology in ECT}
\label{sec:dark_sector}

The Lorentz-order-field mechanism
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}) shows that the galactic
mass-discrepancy phenomenology of ECT does not require particle
dark matter: large-scale mass discrepancies can already emerge
from the environment-dependent nonlinear response of the vacuum
order parameter $\phi$.  This should be distinguished from the
separate question of whether ECT also supports \emph{independent
dark-sector excitations}, such as Goldstone modes, topological
objects, or other non-baryonic condensate remnants.

Accordingly, the term ``dark sector'' in ECT refers to two
conceptually different effects:
(i)~an \emph{effective} modification of gravitational response
controlled by the Lorentz-order field $\phi$, which can mimic
dark-matter phenomenology without introducing new particles; and
(ii)~possible additional condensate excitations which, if
present, would behave as ultra-light and extremely weakly
coupled degrees of freedom.  These two mechanisms have distinct
observational signatures and should be tested primarily through
gravitational and astrophysical probes.

\subsection{Goldstone modes of the condensate}

Spontaneous symmetry breaking of the condensate field implies the
existence of low-energy excitations associated with fluctuations of the
condensate phase. These excitations behave as Goldstone modes and can
propagate as extremely light bosonic degrees of freedom.

Depending on the microscopic structure of the condensate sector, such
modes may acquire a small effective mass through explicit symmetry
breaking or through environmental effects. In this case they can act as
a form of ultra-light collisionless excitations (conventionally classified as ``dark matter'') with masses in the range

\[
m_G \sim 10^{-22}\text{--}10^{-21}\ \mathrm{eV},
\]

comparable to fuzzy-dark-matter models in the $\Lambda$CDM framework.



\subsection{Topological condensate configurations}

The condensate field may also support non-trivial topological
configurations such as vortices or instanton-like structures. These
objects correspond to localized regions where the condensate order
parameter winds in field space.

Such configurations can behave as massive localized excitations of the
condensate and may contribute to the effective dark sector of the
theory. Their detailed properties depend on the microscopic structure of
the condensate potential and are left for future work.



\subsection{Mass-discrepancy phenomenology in ECT}

Within the revised ECT framework the dark-matter phenomenology
is organised into two sharply distinct levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Galactic mass discrepancy} (flat rotation curves,
  RAR, BTFR): attributed entirely to the nonlinear
  $\phi$-branch of the Lorentz-order field
  (Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
  No particle dark matter and no kpc-scale variation of the
  heavy condensate amplitude are invoked.

\item \textbf{Possible non-galactic dark-sector contributions}:
  ultra-light Goldstone modes and topological condensate
  configurations may exist as additional excitations,
  but they are \emph{not required} to explain galactic
  rotation curves.  Whether they contribute to cluster or
  cosmological dark-sector phenomenology remains an open
  problem.
\end{enumerate}



\subsection{Dark energy and the dark sector in ECT}
\label{sec:dark_energy_phi}

\subsubsection{Dark energy as condensate vacuum energy}

In ECT the late-time accelerated expansion is not driven by
a cosmological constant added to the action.  Instead, it
arises from the residual vacuum energy of the condensate
after $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking:
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\rm DE} = V(\Phi_0) + \tfrac{1}{2}(\partial_w\Phi)^2
= \rho_{\rm pot} + \rho_{\rm kin}\,.
\end{equation}
The equation of state is
\begin{equation}
w = \frac{p_{\rm DE}}{\rho_{\rm DE}}
= -1 + \frac{2\rho_{\rm kin}}{3\rho_{\rm cond}}\,.
\label{eq:w_ect}
\end{equation}
Since $\rho_{\rm kin} \geq 0$, ECT \emph{predicts}
$w(z) \geq -1$ at all redshifts (no phantom crossing).
This is a falsifiable structural prediction.

\paragraph{Thawing condensate model.}
If the condensate rolls slowly toward its potential
minimum, the kinetic fraction decays:
$\rho_{\rm kin}(z)/\rho_{\rm cond} = f_0\,e^{-\kappa z}$,
giving
\begin{equation}
w(z) = -1 + \frac{2f_0}{3}\,e^{-\kappa z}\,.
\label{eq:w_thaw}
\end{equation}
This is a \emph{thawing quintessence} model: $w \to -1$
in the past (condensate near potential minimum),
$w > -1$ today (condensate rolling).

\subsubsection{Observational status: DESI BAO measurements}

The Dark Energy Spectroscopic Instrument (DESI) has
published two data releases providing the most precise
BAO distance measurements to date:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{DESI DR1} (April~2024~\cite{DESI2024}):
  6~million galaxy and quasar redshifts.
  Combined with Planck~CMB and type~Ia supernovae
  (Pantheon+, Union3, or DESY5), a $w_0w_a$CDM fit
  gives $w_0 \approx -0.83$, $w_a \approx -0.75$,
  disfavouring $\Lambda$CDM at $2.5$--$3.9\sigma$
  depending on the supernova dataset.

\item \textbf{DESI DR2} (March~2025~\cite{DESIDR2_2025}):
  14~million redshifts (three years of operation),
  doubling DR1.  The preference for evolving dark energy
  \emph{strengthened}: $w_0w_a$CDM is preferred over
  $\Lambda$CDM at $2.8$--$4.2\sigma$.  The best-fit
  CPL parameters indicate $w_0 > -1$ today and
  $w_0 + w_a < -1$, formally implying a phantom crossing
  near $z \approx 0.5$.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Is the phantom crossing real?}
The apparent phantom crossing ($w < -1$ at $z > 0.5$) is
a feature of the \emph{CPL parametrisation}
$w(z) = w_0 + w_a z/(1+z)$, which is a simple two-parameter
approximation --- not a physical model.  Several independent
analyses have shown~\cite{Lodha2025,Calderon2024}:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The CPL form is too rigid to correctly describe both
  low-$z$ and high-$z$ behaviour simultaneously.

\item \emph{Thawing quintessence} models (where
  $w \geq -1$ at all times) are compatible with DESI data
  at the $2\sigma$ level~\cite{Shlivko2024,Gomez2025}.

\item Non-parametric reconstructions (Gaussian processes,
  crossing statistics) also find evolving dark energy but
  with larger uncertainty on whether $w$ actually crosses
  $-1$~\cite{Calderon2024}.

\item The phantom crossing significance does not yet reach
  $5\sigma$ and depends on the choice of supernova
  dataset~\cite{Wang2025}.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
The current observational situation can therefore be
summarised as follows:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{lc}
\hline\hline
Statement & Status \\
\hline
$w \neq -1$ (dark energy evolves) & $2.8$--$4.2\sigma$ \\
$w$ crosses $-1$ (phantom) &
  preferred in CPL, but \\
 & $2\sigma$-compatible with $w \geq -1$ \\
$\Lambda$CDM ($w = -1$ exact) & increasingly challenged, not yet excluded \\
\hline\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\paragraph{ECT confrontation with DESI.}
The ECT thawing model~\eqref{eq:w_thaw} with
$f_0 \approx 0.26$ and $\kappa \approx 4.3$ (calibrated,
not derived from first principles) is consistent with
DESI data at the $2\sigma$ level
(Fig.~\ref{fig:w_z}).  It reproduces the key observational
feature --- $w > -1$ today, evolving toward $w = -1$
in the past --- while predicting that the phantom crossing
is \emph{apparent}, not real.

If future data (DESI Year~5, Euclid, Vera Rubin/LSST)
confirm the phantom crossing at $>3\sigma$, ECT would be
falsified or require fundamental modification.  If
$w \geq -1$ is confirmed, $\Lambda$CDM would be further
challenged and ECT remains viable.


\subsubsection{Mass discrepancy: $\phi$-modification vs.\ particle dark matter}

The galactic mass-discrepancy phenomenology (flat rotation
curves, RAR, BTFR) is explained in ECT by the nonlinear
response of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).  This mechanism does
\emph{not} require new particles.

\paragraph{Predictions for direct detection experiments.}
Since the galactic mass discrepancy arises from the
$\phi$-branch rather than from weakly interacting massive
particles, ECT predicts that direct dark-matter-particle detection
experiments (XENON, LZ, PandaX, DARWIN) will find
\emph{no WIMP signal} for the galactic mass discrepancy.
A robust detection of a particle species accounting for
the galactic mass discrepancy would falsify the
$\phi$-branch interpretation.  By contrast, the mere
existence of additional dark condensate excitations on
non-galactic scales would not.



\paragraph{Cosmological fractions.}
ECT does not yet derive the cosmological fractions
$\Omega_b$, $\Omega_{\rm DM}$, and $\Omega_\Lambda$ from
first principles.  What it presently offers is a
reinterpretation: the galactic mass discrepancy is attributed
to the nonlinear $\phi$-branch rather than to particle dark
matter, while the late-time dark-energy sector is interpreted
as residual condensate vacuum energy.  A first-principles
derivation of the effective cosmological fractions remains
an open problem.

\paragraph{Distinction from the fifth force.}
The galactic $\phi$-modification and the ECT fifth force
($\mathcal{L}_5 = \beta\bar\Psi\gamma^A n_A\Psi$,
$\beta \sim m_f/M_{\rm Pl}$) are \emph{different}
manifestations of the same condensate:
the $\phi$-branch operates on kpc scales;
the fifth force is Planck-suppressed and detectable at
laboratory scales through spin precession
($\omega_5 \sim 10^{-10}$\,rad\,s$^{-1}$) and
E\"otv\"os-type experiments ($\eta \sim 10^{-15}$).
Neither is a consequence of the other.

\bigskip
\noindent
\textbf{Transition to Part~III.}
Part~II has established the macroscopic observable predictions of ECT:
galactic rotation curves from the Lorentz-order field $\phi$,
the baryonic Tully--Fisher relation as an exact algebraic consequence
of the critical infrared branch, cosmological inflation, dark energy,
and dark-matter candidates from the condensate spectrum.
All of these emerge from the variation of the condensate
amplitude $v_0(r)$ and the anisotropy parameter $\chi = \alpha-\beta$
on astrophysical and cosmological scales.

Part~III returns to the microscopic quantum structure.
Whereas Part~I derived key results of quantum mechanics from the condensate
(Schrödinger equation and CCR strictly; influence functional and second law
with Gaussian--Markov assumptions), Part~III examines
what the condensate \emph{additionally} predicts about the foundational
principles of physics: the uncertainty principle as a theorem,
the principle of extremal action from saddle-point condensate paths,
a structural route toward quantum statistics and the Pauli exclusion
principle via $SO(4)$ representation theory (sign structure compatible
with fermionic antisymmetry in the quadratic limit;
full PLZ theorem not yet derived),
and the structural organization of three quantum vacuum phenomena---Casimir
(at condensate boundaries), Unruh, and environmental decoherence---as
three observables controlled by related limits of the condensate
two-point function $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$ (organizing proposition).

\part{Quantum Sector: Emergent Principles and Microscopic Structure}
\label{part:quantum}
%==============================================================

\section{Emergent Quantum Principles and Vacuum Structure in ECT}
\label{sec:emergent_principles}

\begin{mdframed}[backgroundcolor=blue!4,linecolor=blue!40!black,linewidth=1pt]
\textbf{Scope of Part~III.}
The derivations in this Part distinguish two levels:
\begin{enumerate}[noitemsep,leftmargin=2.5em]
  \item \emph{Micro-ECT}: results concerning ordered quadratic excitations,
    open-system reduction, and quantum effective dynamics
    (Sections~\ref{sec:uncertainty}--\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}).
  \item \emph{Gravitational/cosmological extensions}: applications of the
    broader ECT framework to macroscopic and cosmological scales
    (treated in Parts~II and IV).
\end{enumerate}
Statements from level~(ii) should not be read as consequences
of micro-ECT alone.
\end{mdframed}


\textbf{Reader orientation.}
Part~III is the most technically detailed part of this paper.
Before entering the individual derivations, it is important to note
that the results here operate at \emph{three distinct levels of rigour}.
Level~A results are exact consequences of the ECT action and symmetries.
Level~B results are structural or conditional: they hold given explicitly
stated additional inputs (emergent complex sector, Gaussian--Markov
reduction, spinorial field admittance, etc.).
Level~C items indicate a direction without a completed proof.
The tag appears next to every claim in this Part; the consolidated
status table is at the end (Section~\ref{sec:partIII_summary}).

\textbf{Status guide for Part~III.}
This Part collects results at three distinct levels of rigour;
each claim is tagged accordingly throughout.
\begin{description}[leftmargin=3em,style=unboxed,noitemsep]
  \item[\textbf{Level~A}~(theorem / identity).]
    Result follows from the ECT action and symmetries without
    additional physical input (analytic continuation and standard
    mathematical steps permitted; coarse-graining not permitted).
    \emph{Examples:} KG equation, CCR from phase single-valuedness,
    Heisenberg inequality as Cauchy--Schwarz.
  \item[\textbf{Level~B}~(structural / conditional / effective).]
    Result follows given one or more additional assumptions stated
    explicitly (emergent complex sector, Gaussian--Markov reduction,
    spinorial representations, etc.).
    \emph{Examples:} Schr\"odinger, Dirac (structural reconstruction),
    Born rule (conditional uniqueness), second law (effective,
    Gaussian--Markov), Casimir $3/2$ (condensate boundaries only).
  \item[\textbf{Level~C}~(open / speculative).]
    Direction indicated; rigorous derivation not yet available.
    \emph{Examples:} non-circular Planck-scale derivation, full
    PLZ spin--statistics theorem, unique outcome selection.
\end{description}

Several fundamental principles of physics that are normally
postulated can be related to the ECT framework at Level~A or~B
from the geometry and topology of condensate loop configurations;
Level~C items point toward future work.

\subsection{Emergent Principles of Quantum and Cosmological Physics in ECT}

A feature of the ECT framework is that several fundamental principles of modern physics can be related to the geometric and topological structure of condensate configurations, at Level~A or~B (see status guide above).

In particular, the uncertainty principle (Level~A), the principle of extremal action (Level~A), quantum statistics (Level~B structural), and the three quantum vacuum phenomena (Level~A/B) can all be related to properties of closed loop configurations of the Euclidean condensate field.  Black-hole thermodynamics and inflation are discussed as candidate interpretations (Level~B) within the same framework; they are addressed in separate sections.  Beyond these principles, the quantum vacuum structure of the condensate --- Casimir energy, Unruh radiation, and environmental decoherence --- is organised in Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum} around a single Euclidean two-point function (organizing proposition; each effect requires its own boundary, detector, or coarse-graining specification).

\subsection{Loop Configurations in ECT}

A central object in the ECT framework is a closed loop configuration of the condensate field in Euclidean spacetime.

Consider a closed trajectory $\gamma$ of characteristic length $L$ in the $(x,w)$ plane. 
The condensate field along this loop defines an action functional

\begin{equation}
S_{\text{loop}}[\varphi] =
\oint_{\gamma} \mathcal{L}_E(\varphi, \partial\varphi)\, ds .
\end{equation}

Among all possible loops there exists a minimal non–trivial configuration with action

\begin{equation}
S_{\text{loop,min}} = 2\pi \hbar .
\end{equation}

This quantity plays the role of the quantum of action in the theory. 
The Planck constant therefore appears as an emergent parameter associated with the minimal loop configuration of the condensate field.

\subsection{What is Genuinely New in the ECT Micro-Sector?}
\label{sec:micro_novel}

Before the individual derivations, it is useful to state explicitly
what is conceptually new in the ECT treatment of quantum mechanics,
as distinct from new formulas in already-tested limits.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textbf{N\arabic*.},leftmargin=2.5em]
  \item \textbf{New ontology, not just new formulas.}
    Quantum mechanics emerges from the geometry and topology of
    condensate loop configurations on a fixed Euclidean manifold.
    The ordered quadratic sector naturally leads to an emergent
    amplitude description with the standard Hilbert-space machinery:
    the wave equation (Level~A in the ordered sector), $\hbar$ as a
    consistency identification (Level~B/C), and Hilbert-space structure
    as an emergent framework (not a full microscopic derivation).
    In tested limits, the predictions of ECT agree with standard QM;
    the novelty is in the microscopic \emph{origin} of those predictions.
  \item \textbf{Single-correlator principle.}
    Three apparently unrelated quantum vacuum phenomena ---
    Casimir energy, Unruh temperature, and environmental decoherence ---
    are three limits of a \emph{single} Euclidean condensate two-point
    function $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$ (Section~\ref{sec:unified_correlator}).
    This is an organising proposition, not a theorem;
    each effect still requires its own boundary/detector specification.
  \item \textbf{Real Euclidean ontology.}
    ECT treats the Euclidean manifold as physically real, not as a
    computational trick.  Instantons and closed loops are genuine
    field configurations; analytic continuation recovers the
    Lorentzian description as an emergent IR limit.
\end{enumerate}

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Controlled Domain of the ECT Micro-Sector}
\label{sec:controlled_domain}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

The results of this Part hold within the following controlled domain.
Readers should keep this list in mind when assessing individual claims.

\begin{description}[leftmargin=2.5em,style=unboxed,noitemsep]
  \item[Ordered branch.]
    The condensate order parameter is non-zero:
    $\langle n_A\rangle=\delta_{Aw}$ (the gradient condensate selects
    the $w$-direction; equivalently $\langle\partial_A\Phi\rangle=v_0\delta_{Aw}$).
    All quantum results require this spontaneously broken phase.
  \item[Quadratic (weak-field) regime.]
    Condensate fluctuations $\chi\ll v_0$ are treated at quadratic order.
    Non-linear corrections at Planck densities are not controlled.
  \item[Gaussian environment (where stated).]
    The influence-functional and second-law results assume a
    Gaussian--Markov environment (Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional}).
    Full microscopic derivation without this assumption is open (OP24).
  \item[Markov reduction (where stated).]
    Time-local effective equations require a Markov approximation;
    non-Markovian corrections are not controlled.
  \item[Additional inputs for fermions and Born measure.]
    The Dirac equation requires spinorial fields to be admitted
    as Level~B inputs.  The Born measure requires structural
    assumptions C1--C3.  Neither is derived from the bare bosonic action.
\end{description}

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Uncertainty Principle}
\label{sec:uncertainty}

\textbf{Status:} Level~A (theorem in the emergent ordered sector).
The Heisenberg uncertainty relation $\Delta q\,\Delta p\geq\hbar/2$
follows as a strict mathematical theorem once the emergent momentum
operator is established.  The derivation proceeds in two steps.

\paragraph{Step 1 --- Emergent momentum operator (Level~B input).}

In the emergent complex ordered sector, the condensate phase field
$\theta(x)$ generates translations of the position coordinate.
The operator
\begin{equation}
  \hat p = -i\hbar\,\partial_x
\end{equation}
arises as the generator of spatial translations in $L^2(\mathbb{R}^3)$.
This is a Level~B identification: it holds once the emergent complex
sector $\Phi_{\rm eff}=\rho\,e^{i\theta}$ is admitted and
the analytic continuation $w\to -ic_*t$ is performed
(Section~\ref{sec:schrodinger}).

\paragraph{Step 2 --- CCR (Level~A in the ordered sector).}

Given the emergent complex sector and the identification of $\hat p$
above, the canonical commutation relation
\begin{equation}
  [\hat x,\, \hat p] \;=\; i\hbar
\end{equation}
follows from the single-valuedness of the condensate phase
(Section~\ref{sec:CCR}; Level~A).

\paragraph{Step 3 --- Robertson--Schr\"odinger inequality (pure mathematics).}

For any two self-adjoint operators $\hat A$, $\hat B$ on a Hilbert space $\mathcal{H}$
and any state $|\psi\rangle$, the Cauchy--Schwarz inequality in $L^2$ gives
\begin{equation}
  \Delta A\,\Delta B \;\geq\; \tfrac{1}{2}\bigl|\langle[\hat A,\hat B]\rangle\bigr|.
\end{equation}
Setting $\hat A=\hat x$, $\hat B=\hat p$ and using $[\hat x,\hat p]=i\hbar$:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\Delta x\,\Delta p \;\geq\; \frac{\hbar}{2}.}
\end{equation}
This step is purely mathematical---it requires only the Hilbert-space
structure and the CCR; no further physical input from ECT is needed.

\paragraph{Summary.}
The Heisenberg uncertainty principle emerges in ECT via a four-step ladder:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textit{\arabic*.},noitemsep,leftmargin=2.5em]
  \item Admit emergent complex ordered sector (Level~B).
  \item Identify momentum operator $\hat p=-i\hbar\partial_x$ as
    generator of translations in that sector (Level~B).
  \item CCR $[\hat x,\hat p]=i\hbar$ follows as operator identity
    from phase single-valuedness (Level~A \emph{within the ordered sector}).
  \item Uncertainty inequality $\Delta x\,\Delta p\geq\hbar/2$ follows
    from Cauchy--Schwarz in $L^2$ (pure mathematics, no ECT input).
\end{enumerate}
Level~A in step~3 means ``theorem within the ordered sector'', not
``unconditional from bare action'' --- the Level~B input of step~1 is required.

\subsection{Principle of Extremal Action}

The principle of extremal action also arises naturally in ECT from the Euclidean functional integral.

The two–point correlation function of the condensate field is

\begin{equation}
\langle \varphi(X_1)\varphi(X_2)\rangle =
\frac{1}{Z}
\int D\varphi
\,
\varphi(X_1)\varphi(X_2)
\,
e^{-S_E[\varphi]/S_{\min}} .
\end{equation}

In the limit

\begin{equation}
S_{\min} \rightarrow 0
\end{equation}

the integral is dominated by saddle points satisfying

\begin{equation}
\delta S_E = 0 .
\end{equation}

This is precisely the classical principle of extremal (stationary) action.

Quantum fluctuations correspond to finite values of

\begin{equation}
S_{\min} = 2\pi \hbar .
\end{equation}



\subsection{Conservation Laws}
\label{sec:conservation_laws}

\textbf{Scope (controlled domain).}
The conservation laws below hold within the
\emph{emergent Lorentzian effective sector} of ECT:
the homogeneous condensate branch with constant $\chi$
and the analytic continuation $w\to -ic_*t$ applied.
Claims going beyond this domain (baryon/lepton number,
electroweak anomaly, local gauge promotion) are
standard field-theoretic continuations once the
corresponding gauge/matter sector is admitted, not
new ECT derivations; they are noted but not developed here.

\paragraph{Energy-momentum conservation (Level~A in homogeneous branch).}
Four-dimensional translation invariance
$X^A\to X^A+\epsilon^A$ of the homogeneous condensate background
yields the Noether energy-momentum tensor
\begin{equation}
  T^{AB} = \frac{\partial\mathcal{L}}{\partial(\partial_A\varphi)}\,
  \partial^B\varphi - \delta^{AB}\mathcal{L},\qquad
  \partial_A T^{AB}=0.
\end{equation}
After analytic continuation this becomes $\partial_\mu T^{\mu\nu}=0$.
\textit{Caveat:} when $\chi(t)$ evolves (cosmological setting),
exact time-translation invariance is broken and global energy
conservation does not hold, consistent with GR~\cite{Weinberg1972}.

\paragraph{Angular momentum conservation (Level~A).}
The residual $O(3)$ symmetry of the broken phase gives the
conserved angular momentum tensor
$\partial_\mu M^{\mu\nu\lambda}=0$.

\textit{Beyond the condensate sector.}
Once an emergent complex matter sector and additional gauge
structure are admitted, the corresponding Noether currents
(electric charge, baryon/lepton number) follow in the standard
effective-field-theory way.  This is not a new ECT derivation;
no gauge or anomaly structure is independently derived from
the bare condensate action.

\subsection{Quantum Statistics}
\label{sec:quantum_stats}

\textbf{Status.}
This subsection provides a \emph{structural route} toward fermionic
antisymmetry and the Pauli exclusion principle (Level~B).
It does \emph{not} constitute a proof of the full
Pauli--L\"uders--Zumino (PLZ) spin-statistics theorem.
In particular, the arguments below reproduce the bosonic/fermionic
\emph{classification} but do not derive the second-quantisation
anticommutation structure $\{\hat a,\hat a^\dagger\}=1$
from the bare ECT action.

\paragraph{Step 1 --- Topological classification of exchange sectors.}

The configuration space of two identical particles in $\mathbb{R}^3$ is
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{M}_2 = (\mathbb{R}^3\times\mathbb{R}^3\setminus\Delta)/S_2,
\end{equation}
whose fundamental group is $\pi_1(\mathcal{M}_2)=\mathbb{Z}_2$.
This yields exactly two topological classes of exchange loops:
even (symmetric, bosonic) and odd (antisymmetric, fermionic).
In two spatial dimensions $\pi_1=\mathbb{Z}$, allowing anyonic statistics.

\paragraph{Step 2 --- Representation-theoretic compatibility (Level~B).}

Under $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking, condensate excitations
fall into representations of the residual $O(3)\cong SU(2)/\mathbb{Z}_2$:
\begin{itemize}[noitemsep]
  \item \textit{Tensor representations} (integer spin):
    the field returns to itself under $2\pi$ rotation
    $\Rightarrow$ sign structure \emph{compatible with bosonic}
    symmetric wavefunctions.
  \item \textit{Spinor representations} (half-integer spin):
    the field acquires a $-1$ sign under $2\pi$ rotation
    (double-cover $SU(2)$)
    $\Rightarrow$ sign structure \emph{compatible with fermionic}
    antisymmetric wavefunctions.
\end{itemize}
This is a structural compatibility statement (Level~B):
it holds once spinorial excitations of the ordered sector are
admitted, and it connects ECT's representation theory to the
topological dichotomy of Step~1.

\paragraph{Step 3 --- Honest status.}

The two steps above provide a structural route; the following
important limitations apply:
\begin{itemize}[noitemsep]
  \item The full PLZ theorem (requiring local relativistic QFT input)
    has \emph{not} been obtained from bare ECT.
  \item The canonical anticommutation relations
    $\{\hat a_i,\hat a^\dagger_j\}=\delta_{ij}$ have not been
    derived from bare ECT; this remains open.
  \item Beyond-quadratic corrections at Planck densities are
    speculative; no quantitative prediction is made here.
\end{itemize}

\begin{table}[h!]
\centering
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\caption{Quantum statistics in ECT vs standard frameworks.}
\label{tab:statistics_comparison}
\begin{tabular}{@{}p{3.2cm}p{4.0cm}p{5.0cm}@{}}
\hline
Aspect & Standard QM/QFT & ECT \\
\hline
Route to antisymmetry & Axiom & Sign structure \emph{associated with} spinorial reps.\ of the ordered sector (Level~B; not a full PLZ theorem) \\
Basis & $\{\hat a,\hat a^\dagger\}=1$ postulated & Topology + spinorial sign \\
Pauli principle & Exact axiom & Structural (quadratic regime) \\
Full PLZ theorem & Yes & Open \\
Beyond-quadratic & N/A & Speculative, not predicted \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}



\textit{Note on black-hole thermodynamics.}
Black-hole thermodynamic interpretations (Hawking temperature,
Bekenstein--Hawking entropy) based on condensate loop instability
and the horizon criticality condition $\Gamma_{\rm loop}\sim1$
are discussed in the dedicated section (Section~\ref{sec:bh_information})
and are not core micro-ECT results used here.

\textit{Note on inflation and dark energy.}
Cosmological applications of the condensate ---
inflation as a phase transition, the spectral index $n_s=1-2/N_e$,
and slow condensate evolution as dark energy --- are discussed
separately in the cosmology section
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}) and are not used as inputs
in the present micro-sector derivations.



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Quantum Vacuum Structure of the ECT Condensate}
\label{sec:quantum_vacuum}

The condensate that underlies ECT is not merely a classical background field.
It has a rich quantum vacuum structure whose properties are directly constrained
by the $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry-breaking pattern.  In this section we provide structural accounts of three
quantum vacuum phenomena --- the conditional Goldstone-sector Casimir-type
vacuum shift, the Unruh temperature, and cosmological particle production ---
from ECT first principles.  The derivations illuminate
how standard quantum vacuum physics is reorganised within the Euclidean condensate
picture: each effect is controlled by an analytic continuation $w\to -ic_*t$ of a
Euclidean correlator, though each still requires its own boundary conditions,
detector specification, or coarse-graining prescription.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Unified correlator: an organizing principle of the ECT vacuum sector}
\label{sec:unified_correlator}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\textbf{Status:} the following is an \emph{organizing proposition}
of the micro-ECT vacuum sector, not a theorem-level unification.
The three phenomena discussed below are three physically distinct
observables controlled by related limits of the same condensate
correlator, once the corresponding boundary conditions, detector
coupling, and coarse-graining assumptions are specified separately
for each case.  They are not identical computations.

A structurally suggestive feature of ECT is that three apparently
unrelated quantum vacuum phenomena --- the conditional Goldstone-sector
Casimir-type vacuum shift, the Unruh temperature, and environmental
decoherence --- are controlled by different \emph{limits of a single
condensate two-point function}.

\begin{mdframed}[linewidth=0.8pt,innerleftmargin=8pt,innerrightmargin=8pt,
    innertopmargin=6pt,innerbottommargin=6pt]
\textbf{ECT Unified Correlator Principle (organising proposition).}\\
In ECT, three quantum-vacuum phenomena --- environmental decoherence,
Casimir-type boundary vacuum shifts, and the Unruh thermal response ---
are three manifestations of the same underlying condensate two-point
function $N(\tau,\mathbf{x}-\mathbf{x}')$.  They differ in their
boundary conditions, detector coupling, and coarse-graining prescription,
not in their fundamental origin.  This is an \emph{organising proposition}
of ECT; each effect still requires its own derivation within the
framework.
\end{mdframed}


\paragraph{The condensate correlator $N(\tau, \mathbf{x}-\mathbf{x}')$.}
Define the symmetric Euclidean two-point function of the condensate field:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:N_master}
  N(\tau, \mathbf{r})
  \;=\; \langle \chi(\tau,\mathbf{x})\,\chi(0,\mathbf{x}')\rangle_{\rm sym}
  \;\propto\; v_0^2\,C_{\rm sym}(\tau, |\mathbf{r}|),
\end{equation}
where $\chi$ denotes condensate fluctuation modes and
$v_0^2$ sets the overall coupling strength.  This is the
same function that appears as the noise kernel in the
influence functional (Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional}).

\paragraph{Relation between $G_E$ and $N$.}
Two objects appear throughout this section and should not be conflated:
\begin{description}[noitemsep,leftmargin=2.5em]
  \item[$G_E(X,X')$] The Euclidean two-point Green function of a
    massless Goldstone mode: $G_E = 1/(4\pi^2|X{-}X'|^2)$.
    It controls propagation amplitudes.
  \item[$N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$] The symmetrised noise kernel of the
    condensate environment: $N(\tau) = \langle\chi(\tau)\chi(0)\rangle_{\rm sym}
    \propto v_0^2\,C_{\rm sym}(\tau)$.
    It controls decoherence and dissipation rates.
\end{description}
For free Gaussian Goldstone modes, $N$ is obtained from $G_E$
by symmetrisation: $N(\tau,\mathbf{r}) = \tfrac{1}{2}[G_E(\tau,\mathbf{r})+G_E(-\tau,\mathbf{r})]$
(up to the coupling constant $v_0^2$ and analytic continuation).
The two objects share the same microscopic origin (the condensate action)
but play different physical roles in the three constructions below.

\paragraph{Three regimes of one correlator.}
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textit{Casimir effect.}
    In the presence of boundaries that reflect the relevant
    condensate Goldstone modes (separated by $a$), the
    boundary-modified vacuum mode spectrum of the correlator
    $N(\tau, \mathbf{r})$ produces a shift in zero-point energy.
    (The Euclidean formalism implements this via periodicity
    conditions on the $w$-coordinate; no finite physical
    temperature is required.)  The ECT result for three
    Goldstone modes is
    \begin{equation}
      \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm ECT}
      = -\frac{3\pi^2\hbar c_*}{240\,a^4}
      = \frac{3}{2}\cdot\frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm QED},
      \label{eq:casimir_unified}
    \end{equation}
    where the factor $3/2$ relative to single-field QED arises
    from the three independent Goldstone modes (one per broken
    generator of the coset $O(4)/O(3)$).  See
    Section~\ref{sec:casimir} for the full derivation.
    \textbf{Experimental applicability:} the factor $3/2$ is a
    conditional prediction.  Standard metal plates are
    electromagnetically, not condensate-mode, selective.
    Goldstone modes carry no electric charge and interact with
    ordinary matter only gravitationally ($\sim M_{\rm Pl}^{-2}$),
    making metal plates transparent to them.  The factor $3/2$
    manifests in configurations where boundaries effectively
    reflect condensate Goldstone modes, such as BEC domain walls
    or superfluid boundaries.

  \item \textit{Unruh effect.}
    For an accelerating detector with proper acceleration $a$,
    the condensate correlator $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$ evaluated
    along a uniformly accelerated worldline (Rindler trajectory)
    takes a Planck distribution form.  This gives the Unruh
    temperature:
    \begin{equation}
      T_U = \frac{\hbar\,a}{2\pi\,c_*\,k_B}.
      \label{eq:unruh_unified}
    \end{equation}
    Given the standard Unruh-DeWitt detector coupling and a
    uniformly accelerated worldline, the Unruh response follows
    from analytic continuation of the same ECT correlator
    $N(\tau)$ to the Rindler frame.  The derivation does not
    require new dynamical input beyond the detector model and
    trajectory specification; the condensate action supplies
    the propagator structure.

  \item \textit{Environmental decoherence.}
    For a macroscopic system coupled to $N_{\rm eff}$ condensate
    modes with coupling $\gamma$, the decoherence functional
    exponent (Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional})
    is
    \begin{equation}
      \Gamma_{\rm dist} = \tfrac{1}{2}\iint
      (\gamma_1-\gamma_2)(\tau)\,N(\tau-\tau')\,
      (\gamma_1-\gamma_2)(\tau')\,d\tau\,d\tau'.
    \end{equation}
    The \emph{same} function $N$ determines the decoherence
    rate.  The quantum-to-classical transition
    ($\Gamma_{\rm dist} \gtrsim 1$) is therefore a property
    of the condensate vacuum correlator.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Summary of the unification.}
The same Euclidean two-point correlator enters three
physically distinct constructions:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:unified_N_vacuum}
  N(\tau,\mathbf{r}-\mathbf{r}')
  \quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  \begin{cases}
    \text{boundary-modified vacuum spectrum} & \to\; E_{\rm Cas},\\[4pt]
    \text{accelerated-detector response} & \to\; T_U,\\[4pt]
    \text{coarse-grained open-system kernel} & \to\; \Gamma_{\rm dist}.
  \end{cases}
\end{equation}
In standard QFT the Casimir-type vacuum shift, Unruh effect, and decoherence
are computed by separate formalisms (mode summation, Bogoliubov
transformation, and Lindblad equations respectively).  In ECT
the \emph{same} underlying condensate correlator $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$
appears in all three, which is a structural economy of the framework.
The physical content is that the vacuum fluctuation strength $v_0^2$
simultaneously enters vacuum energy density (Casimir), thermal
properties of accelerated frames (Unruh), and the decoherence rate.
However, deriving each effect still requires specifying the
appropriate boundary conditions (Casimir), detector trajectory
and coupling (Unruh), and coarse-graining prescription (decoherence)
separately; these inputs are not eliminated by the common correlator
structure.



% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Vacuum stiffness and the Planck scale}
\label{sec:vacuum_stiffness}

\textbf{Notation used in this subsection.}
\begin{description}[noitemsep,leftmargin=2.5em]
  \item[$\lambda$] Quartic self-coupling in $V(\Phi) = \tfrac{\lambda}{4}(\Phi^2-v_0^2)^2$.
  \item[$\kappa\equiv V''(v_0)=2\lambda v_0^2$] Local stiffness (curvature at the minimum).
  \item[$m_\varphi = \sqrt{\kappa} = \sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0$] Condensate mass.
  \item[$v_0$] Vacuum expectation value; $v_0 = \bar M_{\rm Pl}$ at canonical normalisation.
  \item[$\Lambda_\chi \equiv m_\varphi^2 = \kappa$] Effective stiffness scale
    (used in the $\hbar$-matching relation where retained).
\end{description}

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

The ECT condensate potential is
\begin{equation}
  V(\Phi) \;=\; -\frac{\mu^2}{2}\Phi^2 + \frac{\lambda}{4}\Phi^4\,,
  \label{eq:condensate_potential_vac}
\end{equation}
with the global minimum at $\langle\Phi\rangle = v_0 = \mu/\sqrt{\lambda}$.
The curvature of the potential at the minimum,
\begin{equation}
  \kappa \;\equiv\; V''(v_0) \;=\; 2\mu^2 \;=\; 2\lambda v_0^2\,,
  \label{eq:stiffness}
\end{equation}
defines the \emph{vacuum stiffness}: the energy cost per unit volume of
displacing the condensate from its equilibrium.  The condensate mass is
$m_\varphi = \sqrt{\kappa} = \sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0$, which sets the
correlation length $\xi_{\rm cond} = 1/m_\varphi \sim \ell_{\rm Pl}$ (consistency relation; see OP-$\Lambda$).

At canonical normalisation ($\alpha=2$, $\beta=1$), the condensate amplitude
$v_0$ is \emph{identified with} the reduced Planck mass via
\begin{equation}
  \bar M_{\rm Pl}^2 \;\stackrel{\rm id}{=}\; v_0^2\,,
  \label{eq:planck_stiffness}
\end{equation}
so that $v_0$ is numerically the reduced Planck stiffness scale in the
canonically normalised branch.
\textbf{Status (consistency relation, not fully non-circular):}
this is a \emph{definition by normalisation convention}, not a
first-principles derivation of the Planck scale from the bare ECT action.
The same $v_0$ enters both $G_N=1/(8\pi v_0^2)$ [canonical: $\alpha=2$, $\beta=1$] and the condensate
dispersion, so the Planck scale and the phase stiffness are identified
in the same step.  A fully non-circular derivation that fixes
$v_0/M_{\rm Pl}$ from an independent microscopic calculation
(without matching $G_N$ as an input) remains open (OP-$\Lambda$,
Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).
In superfluid language, $v_0$ plays the role of the superfluid density:
it measures how stiff the vacuum is against phase gradients \cite{Volovik2003}.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Excitation spectrum after $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking}
\label{sec:excitation_spectrum}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\paragraph{(i) Goldstone bosons.}
The coset $O(4)/O(3)\cong S^3$ has dimension three, so the Goldstone theorem
\cite{GoldstoneSalamWeinberg1962} guarantees three massless Nambu--Goldstone
bosons $\pi^i$ ($i=1,2,3$).  Their low-energy effective action is
\begin{equation}
  S[\pi^i]
  \;=\;
  \frac{v_0^2}{2}
  \int d^4X\;
  \eta^{\mu\nu}\partial_\mu\pi^i\partial_\nu\pi^i\,,
  \label{eq:goldstone_action}
\end{equation}
where $\eta^{\mu\nu} = \mathrm{diag}(-1,+1,+1,+1)$.
Each mode obeys $\Box\,\pi^i = 0$ with dispersion $\omega_k = c_*|\boldsymbol{k}|$.
For galactic condensate variations the residual Goldstone mass is
$m_\pi\sim10^{-33}$\,eV --- the cosmological vacuum-oscillation scale,
corresponding to a de~Broglie wavelength of $\sim$Mpc, not to
the kpc-scale fuzzy dark matter of \cite{HuBarkanaGruzinov2000}
(which requires $m\sim10^{-22}$\,eV).

\paragraph{(ii) Radial mode.}
The radial fluctuation $\sigma = \delta|\Psi|$ acquires mass
$m_\sigma = \sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0 \sim \bar M_{\rm Pl}$,
decoupling at $E\ll m_\sigma$.

\paragraph{(iii) Graviton.}
The massless spin-2 graviton is reconstructed from transverse-traceless
fluctuations of the \emph{effective metric} induced by the condensate order
sector~\cite{Weinberg1972}.  Direct fluctuations of $n^A$ itself carry
spin-1 degrees of freedom (see Section~\ref{sec:graviton}); the spin-2
Fierz--Pauli structure emerges from the induced metric perturbation.
Ghost-freedom and linearised masslessness hold at the effective linearised level.
Full non-perturbative status is an open problem (OP1, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Casimir effect from Goldstone modes}
\label{sec:casimir}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\textbf{Scope and applicability (read before the formula).}
The calculation below is a \emph{conditional prediction}: it applies
only to boundaries that effectively impose Dirichlet conditions on
the ECT Goldstone sector.  Standard metallic laboratory plates do
\emph{not} implement these boundary conditions---the $O(4)\to O(3)$
Goldstone bosons carry no electric charge and couple to ordinary
matter only gravitationally ($\sim v_0^{-2}$), so conducting plates
are transparent to them.  The factor $3/2$ derived below is therefore
\emph{not} a prediction for the standard laboratory Casimir effect
between metal plates.  It is a prediction for boundaries that
physically reflect the gapless condensate sector, such as
superfluid interfaces, BEC domain walls, or $O(4)\to O(3)$
phase-transition surfaces in the early Universe.  Whether any
accessible laboratory system implements such boundary conditions is
an open problem (OP18, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\subsubsection{Derivation for condensate-reflecting boundaries}

\textbf{Boundary condition assumption.}
The derivation below applies exclusively to the idealised case of
condensate-reflecting boundaries that impose Dirichlet conditions on
the ECT Goldstone sector.  Standard metallic plates do not implement
these conditions.  The factor $3/2$ is therefore a
\emph{conditional} prediction, not a statement about the ordinary
laboratory Casimir effect.

For reference, the standard QED result for two photon polarisations
between parallel plates separated by $a$ is
\begin{equation}
  \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm QED}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{\pi^2}{120}\,\frac{\hbar c}{a^4}\,.
  \label{eq:casimir_qed}
\end{equation}
For boundaries that \emph{do} reflect the ECT Goldstone modes, three
massless Goldstone scalars with Dirichlet boundary conditions
contribute independently:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{%
  \frac{F}{A}\bigg|_{\rm ECT}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{3\pi^2}{240}\,\frac{\hbar c_*}{a^4}
  \;=\;
  -\frac{\pi^2}{80}\,\frac{\hbar c}{a^4}\,,
  }
  \label{eq:casimir_ect}
\end{equation}
which is $3/2$ of the QED result.  This follows from zeta-function
regularisation \cite{BirrellDavies1982} of three independent scalar fields:
\begin{equation}
  E_0^{\rm ren}(a) \;=\; -3\times\frac{\pi^2}{720}\,\frac{\hbar c_*\,A}{a^3}
  \;\implies\;
  \frac{F}{A} = -\frac{\partial E_0^{\rm ren}}{\partial a}\bigg/A\,.
\end{equation}
For ideal condensate-domain walls (e.g.\ near the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition
in the early Universe), Dirichlet conditions on the Goldstone modes are
natural and the calculation is complete.

\textbf{Summary statement.}
The factor $3/2$ derived above is \emph{not} a correction to the standard
electromagnetic Casimir experiment between metallic plates;
it is a \emph{separate conditional prediction} for boundaries that
physically couple to the ECT Goldstone sector.
Existing metallic-plate Casimir data neither confirm nor rule out this
prediction; purpose-designed condensate-reflecting boundaries are
required to test it (OP18).

\textbf{ECT conceptual note.}
The Casimir energy computed here is one boundary-sensitive manifestation
of the same condensate two-point correlator $N(\tau,\mathbf{x}-\mathbf{x}')$
that also governs decoherence in the influence-functional sector and
the thermal response in the Unruh construction
(Section~\ref{sec:unified_correlator}).  In ECT these are not
independent ingredients but different regimes of a single condensate
two-point structure: boundary conditions (Casimir), detector trajectory
(Unruh), and coarse-grained environment coupling (decoherence).

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Cosmological particle production at the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition}
\label{sec:cosm_particle_prod}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

Parker \cite{Parker1969} showed that time-varying spacetime geometry produces
particle pairs from the vacuum.  In ECT, the $O(4)\to O(3)$ phase transition
is a non-adiabatic event: the condensate VEV changes from $v_0=0$ to
$v_0=\bar M_{\rm Pl}$ on the Planck time scale $\tau_{\rm PT}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}/c$.

The Goldstone mode $\pi^i_{\boldsymbol{k}}$ satisfies the mode equation
\cite{Parker1969,BirrellDavies1982}:
\begin{equation}
  \ddot{v}_k + \Omega_k^2(t)\,v_k \;=\; 0\,,
  \qquad
  \Omega_k^2(t) \;=\; c_*^2(t)\,k^2 + m_{\rm eff}^2(t)\,,
  \label{eq:mode_equation}
\end{equation}
where $m_{\rm eff}^2(t) = \lambda[v_0^2(\infty) - v_0^2(t)]$.

The expected particle number per mode is
$\mathcal{N}_k = |\beta_k|^2$,
where $\beta_k$ are Bogoliubov coefficients \cite{BirrellDavies1982}.
For the quartic condensate potential with $N_e=60$ e-folds of inflation,
the spectral index is:
\begin{equation}
  n_s \;=\; 1 - \frac{2}{N_e} \;=\; 0.967\,,
  \label{eq:ns_cosm}
\end{equation}
consistent with Planck 2018 \cite{Planck2018}.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Unruh effect from the Euclidean correlator}
\label{sec:unruh}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\subsubsection{Derivation}

The Unruh effect \cite{Unruh1976,Fulling1973,Davies1975} states that a
uniformly accelerated observer detects the Minkowski vacuum as a thermal
bath at $T_U = \hbar a/(2\pi k_B c)$.  In ECT this follows automatically
from the Euclidean correlator via analytic continuation.

The Euclidean two-point function for a massless Goldstone boson is
\cite{BirrellDavies1982}:
\begin{equation}
  G_E(X,X')
  \;=\;
  \frac{1}{4\pi^2\,|X-X'|^2}\,,
  \qquad
  |X-X'|^2 \;=\; (\boldsymbol{x}-\boldsymbol{x}')^2 + (w-w')^2\,.
  \label{eq:green_euclidean}
\end{equation}

The analytic continuation $w\to -ic_*\,t - \varepsilon$ yields:
\begin{equation}
  G^+_M(x,x')
  \;=\;
  -\frac{1}{4\pi^2 c_*^2}
  \cdot
  \frac{1}{(t-t'-i\varepsilon)^2 - |\boldsymbol{x}-\boldsymbol{x}'|^2/c_*^2}\,,
  \label{eq:wightman}
\end{equation}
the standard Wightman function, confirming consistency with the
Osterwalder--Schrader theorem \cite{OsterwalderSchrader1973}.

Along the Rindler trajectory with proper acceleration $a$,
$G^+_M$ becomes periodic in imaginary proper time with period
$\beta_U = 2\pi c_*/a$ --- a thermal distribution.
The Unruh--DeWitt detector response gives a Planck spectrum with:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{%
    T_U \;=\; \frac{\hbar\,a}{2\pi c_*\,k_B}\,,
  }
  \label{eq:unruh_ect}
\end{equation}
reducing to the standard result at $c_*=c$.
For an LHC proton with $a\simeq10^{23}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$:
$T_U\approx4\times10^{-8}$\,K.

\subsubsection{Physical interpretation}

In the ECT interpretation, the Unruh effect is not a postulate but a
consequence of the $O(4)$-invariance of the Euclidean correlator $G_E$:
the Lorentzian thermal response emerges from analytic continuation of
an underlying Euclidean condensate correlator.  The thermal character of
the Rindler vacuum follows from Euclidean rotational symmetry alone.

% -------------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Summary of quantum vacuum predictions}
\label{sec:vacuum_summary}
% -------------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{table}[H]

each effect requires its own specification).
Status: A = analytically derived within ECT; P = programmatic (requires
boundary-condition or detector-coupling input; conditional prediction).
The Casimir entry is conditional on boundaries acting on the ECT Goldstone
sector; it is \emph{not} a prediction for standard metallic-plate experiments.}
\label{tab:vacuum_predictions}
\begin{tabular}{@{}lllcc@{}}
\toprule
Effect & ECT formula & ECT value & Std.\ result & Status \\

\begin{mdframed}[backgroundcolor=yellow!8,linecolor=orange!60!black,linewidth=1pt]
\textbf{Applicability warning.}
The factor $3/2$ predicted above is \textbf{not} a prediction for
ordinary metallic Casimir measurements.  It applies only to
boundaries that physically couple to (i.e.\ reflect) the massless
condensate Goldstone sector.  Standard metallic plates are
electromagnetically selective---the $O(4)\to O(3)$ Goldstone
bosons carry no electric charge and interact with ordinary
matter only gravitationally ($\sim v_0^{-2}$), so conducting
surfaces are transparent to them.  This Planck-suppressed coupling
does \emph{not} imply a tiny but non-zero correction to the metallic
Casimir force: the Goldstone modes are excluded from the boundary
energy integral entirely because the geometry imposes no Dirichlet
conditions on them.  The appropriate question is not
``how large is the ECT correction to metallic Casimir data?'' but
``are the right boundary conditions implemented at all?''---and
the answer for standard metallic plates is no.  Any claim that ECT is
ruled out by existing metallic Casimir measurements would be
incorrect; equally, existing measurements do not yet test the
$3/2$ prediction.  Purpose-designed boundaries (superfluid
interfaces, BEC domain walls, or early-Universe phase-transition
surfaces) are required.  This is an open experimental problem (OP18).
\end{mdframed}

% ============================================================
\section{Black-hole information problem: ECT perspective}
\label{sec:bh_information}
% ============================================================

\subsection{The paradox in brief}
\label{sec:bh_paradox_brief}

The black-hole information problem arises from an apparent conflict between
the unitarity of quantum mechanics and the thermality of Hawking radiation
\cite{Hawking1974,Hawking1975}.
Starting from a pure initial state $|\Psi_{\rm in}\rangle$ of collapsing matter,
the semiclassical Hawking calculation produces a nearly thermal density matrix
$\rho_{\rm rad}$, suggesting the transition
\begin{equation}
|\Psi_{\rm in}\rangle \;\longrightarrow\; \rho_{\rm rad}\,,
\label{eq:info_paradox}
\end{equation}
which would violate unitarity.
Arguments based on the Page curve \cite{Page1993} and on holographic
calculations \cite{Penington2020} strongly suggest that unitary evaporation
is correct, but the microscopic mechanism by which information is encoded in
the outgoing radiation—and how the near-horizon region facilitates this—remains
debated \cite{Mathur2009,Almheiri2013}.

\subsection{ECT reformulation: the horizon is not fundamental}
\label{sec:bh_info_reformulation}

In ECT, Lorentzian geometry and the gravitational horizon are emergent
structures arising from the spontaneous $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking
of the condensate (Section~\ref{sec:ssb}).
This has an immediate implication for the information problem:
the apparent loss of information in Hawking evaporation need not reflect
true microscopic non-unitarity.
Rather, it may signal the \emph{breakdown of the purely geometric,
coarse-grained effective description} near the horizon.

The underlying condensate dynamics is governed by a self-adjoint
Euclidean action $S_E[\Psi]$ (postulate P2, Section~\ref{sec:postulates}).
Any apparent transition to a mixed state must therefore arise from
truncating the full microscopic Hilbert space to an effective radiation
sector alone.

\subsection{Critical Lorentz-order shell}
\label{sec:critical_shell}

A key structural prediction of ECT is the existence of a physical
\emph{critical shell} around any non-extremal horizon.
The argument has two independent inputs.

\paragraph{Near-horizon Tolman temperature.}
Near any non-extremal horizon, the local temperature experienced by a
static observer grows without bound as the proper distance~$\rho$ to
the horizon tends to zero.
In the Rindler approximation this is the Tolman relation
\begin{equation}
T_{\rm loc}(\rho)
\;=\;
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi k_B \rho}\,.
\label{eq:tolman}
\end{equation}
This is a standard result of semiclassical gravity independent of ECT
\cite{Unruh1976}.

\paragraph{Critical temperature of the Lorentz-ordered phase.}
ECT predicts that the Lorentzian phase exists only below the critical
temperature derived in Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum} from the
Dolan--Jackiw one-loop potential \cite{DolanJackiw1974}:
\begin{equation}
T_c \;=\; v_0\sqrt{6} \;\approx\; 5.96\times10^{18}\,\text{GeV}
\;\approx\; 6.92\times10^{31}\,\text{K}\,,
\label{eq:Tc_value}
\end{equation}
where $v_0 \approx \bar{M}_{\rm Pl} \approx 2.435\times10^{18}$\,GeV is
the condensate vacuum expectation value (Section~\ref{sec:consistency_relations}).

\paragraph{Critical shell location.}
Because $T_{\rm loc}(\rho)\to\infty$ as $\rho\to0$, there exists a
unique proper distance $\rho_c$ at which $T_{\rm loc}(\rho_c) = T_c$:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_c
\;=\;
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi k_B T_c}
\;=\;
\frac{\hbar c}{2\pi\sqrt{6}\,k_B v_0}
\;=\;
\frac{\ell_{\rm Pl}}{\sqrt{3\pi}}
\;\approx\;
5.27\times10^{-36}\,\text{m}
\;\approx\;
0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}\,,
}
\label{eq:rho_c}
\end{equation}
where the algebraic simplification uses $v_0 = \bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ and
$G_N = c^2/(16\pi v_0^2)$ [canonical normalisation with $\alpha=2$,
$\beta=1$, $v_0=\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$; equivalent to the general
$G_N=1/(8\pi v_0^2(\alpha-\beta))$] (Eq.~\eqref{eq:GN_condensate}).
This result introduces no additional fit parameters once $T_c$ is fixed
by the ECT thermal sector (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}).
It is moreover \emph{universal}: $\rho_c$ is independent of the black-hole
mass, depending only on the condensate scale $v_0$, which is fixed by
Newton's constant and Planck's constant simultaneously
(Section~\ref{sec:consistency_relations}).

The value $\rho_c \approx \ell_{\rm Pl}/3$ is consistent with
the notion of a ``stretched horizon'' in the membrane paradigm
\cite{PriceThorne1986}, but here it emerges from the condensate
critical temperature rather than from phenomenological input.
Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info} provides a detailed derivation
and numerical illustrations (Figure~\ref{fig:bh_information}).

\subsection{Enlarged Hilbert space and apparent mixedness}
\label{sec:hilbert_enlarged}

The critical shell is a physical region where the Lorentz-ordered phase
becomes critical.
It carries condensate degrees of freedom that are not captured by the
standard geometric description.
This motivates an enlarged Hilbert space:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal{H}_{\rm full}
\;=\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm rad}
\;\otimes\;
\mathcal{H}_{\chi}
\;\otimes\;
\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}\,,
\label{eq:Hilbert_full}
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal{H}_\chi$ describes shell degrees of freedom and
$\mathcal{H}_{\rm core}$ a deeper pre-Lorentzian condensate sector.
The observed radiation density matrix is then
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\rm rad}
=
\mathrm{Tr}_{\chi,\rm core}
\bigl|\Psi\bigr\rangle\bigl\langle\Psi\bigr|\,,
\label{eq:rho_rad_trace}
\end{equation}
so its apparent mixedness does not violate fundamental unitarity.

\subsection{Conditional theorem and its consequence for thermality}
\label{sec:no_exact_thermality}

The mere existence of a near-horizon shell does not resolve the information
paradox by itself.
A structural theorem is required to show that, given unitarity and finite shell
entropy, the outgoing channel \emph{cannot} remain exactly thermal and
state-independent.

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Conditional theorem (ECT).}
\textit{Assume: (i) microscopic condensate dynamics is unitary;
(ii) the near-horizon region contains a finite-entropy critical shell;
(iii) evaporation is complete with no infinite-capacity hidden remnant.
Then: exact Hawking thermality throughout evaporation is impossible,
true information loss is incompatible with (i)--(iii), and
shell-state dependence of the outgoing channel is forced as a logical necessity.}
\end{quote}

\noindent
Appendix~\ref{app:conditional_theorem} gives the full proof by contradiction:
if the channel were universal, distinct shell microstates would produce
identical radiation statistics, contradicting unitarity once evaporation is
complete and no infinite hidden reservoir remains.
Two independent routes reach the same conclusion: the emission-amplitude
argument and the global entropy argument $S_{\rm rad}(t)=S_{\rm rem}(t)\to0$.
Shell-state dependence is therefore a logical necessity, not an embellishment.

As a result, in ECT the leading coarse-grained Hawking spectrum
\begin{equation}
N_\omega^{(s)}
\;=\;
\bigl|\mathcal{T}_\omega[s]\bigr|^2
\cdot
\frac{1}{e^{\hbar\omega/k_B T_H}-1}\,,
\qquad
\mathcal{T}_\omega[s]
=
e^{i\delta_\omega[s] - \Gamma_\omega[s]}\,,
\label{eq:Nomega_corrected}
\end{equation}
must acquire state-dependent corrections $\delta_\omega[s]$, $\Gamma_\omega[s]$
that are suppressed at early times but become order-one near and after the Page
time.
The standard thermal Hawking result is recovered in the coarse-grained
approximation $\langle|\mathcal{T}_\omega|^2\rangle_s \approx 1$.
The explicit computation of the kernel $\mathcal{K}_\omega(\rho)$ appearing in
the general coupling
Eq.~\eqref{eq:kernel_form} (Appendix~\ref{app:chi_dynamics})
remains an open problem.

\subsection{Status of the scenario}
\label{sec:bh_info_status}

The items that follow directly from ECT structure without free parameters are:
(i) fundamental unitarity of condensate dynamics;
(ii) critical temperature $T_c = v_0\sqrt{6}$ (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum});
(iii) critical shell at $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}$
(Eq.~\eqref{eq:rho_c}).

The following items remain open problems:
(i) deriving condition~(C2b) --- that the Tolman temperature is the control
parameter for Lorentz-order loss near the horizon --- from the full condensate
action;
(ii) deriving the shell--radiation coupling coefficient~$g$
(Eq.~\eqref{eq:Lint}) from first principles;
(iii) deriving the shell Hamiltonian's microscopic coefficients
$Z_\chi$, $W_\chi$, $\lambda_\chi$;
(iv) constructing a quantitative ECT Page curve beyond the illustrative
finite-memory toy model;
(v) deriving the exact coefficient $1/4$ in $S_{BH} = A/(4\ell_{\rm Pl}^2)$
from microscopic shell counting.

An effective shell Hamiltonian and the unique form of the minimal
shell--radiation coupling have been constructed
(Appendix~\ref{app:chi_dynamics}).
A toy finite-memory Page model demonstrates explicitly how unitary
purification arises from a finite-entropy shell
(Appendix~\ref{app:page_toy}).
A microscopic consistency criterion identifies which ECT completions can
resolve the paradox and which require additional structure
(Appendix~\ref{app:consistency_criterion}).
We therefore present the ECT black-hole picture as a \emph{sharply
localized candidate resolution}: the conditional theorem closes the
logical argument, and the remaining open tasks are precisely identified.
The detailed supporting arguments and the figure are in
Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info}.

\paragraph{Compact-object observational context.}
Classical Schwarzschild/Kerr solutions are recovered in the limit where
$G_{\rm eff}$ is effectively constant.
Observational tests linked to compact objects include:
quasi-normal mode deviations at order $\rho_c/r_s \sim M_{\rm Pl}^2/M^2$
(suppressed for astrophysical black holes, see Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info});
constraints on primordial black-hole formation and evaporation if $G_{\rm eff}$
runs with time (prediction~F6);
and tensor-speed consistency $|c_T/c-1|<10^{-15}$, already satisfied
(prediction~F4, GW170817).
A dedicated computation of compact-object solutions to the generalised
field equations~\eqref{eq:gen_EE} remains for future work.

\paragraph{Relation to loop-dynamics BH thermodynamics.}
Section~\ref{sec:loops} derives $T_H$ and $S_{BH}$ from the
loop-decay picture of the condensate.
That derivation gives the correct leading-order thermodynamic values.
The present section provides an independent structural argument for why
those relations arise from microscopic condensate degrees of freedom and
suggests that they encode a unitary—not fundamentally dissipative—process.



\section{Predictions and Observational Tests}
\label{sec:predictions}

The ECT framework leads to a range of observationally testable
predictions in laboratory, astrophysical, and cosmological settings.

\textbf{Notes on Table~\ref{tab:numerical}:}
(i)~Status~A entries are derived analytically within ECT from first principles.
(ii)~Status~P entries are programmatic: the formula is motivated and
the numerical agreement is encouraging, but the derivation is incomplete.
(iii)~Status~C entries are consistency checks: ECT reproduces a known
result by construction (e.g.\ the matching of $G_N$ to $v_0$).
(iv)~Status~\textbf{F} entries are observationally \emph{falsified} in the
minimal model; the entry is retained to indicate where extension is required.
(v)~The tensor-to-scalar ratio $r=0.267$ is the only Status~F entry:
the minimal single-field ECT inflation model is excluded by $r<0.036$;
resolution requires a non-minimal extension (see Open Problem~OP4,
Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\subsection{Falsifiable Predictions}
The ECT framework leads to a number of observationally testable predictions. 
These predictions are parameter-light: some signatures (e.g.\ the
universality of the acceleration scale $g_\dagger$, the inflation spectral
index, the Lorentzian-window bound) are zero-parameter once the condensate
profile is fixed; others still depend on phenomenological profile choices
(e.g.\ the fitted $r_0$ per galaxy in rotation-curve analyses).
Collectively they provide direct opportunities to distinguish ECT from both
$\Lambda$CDM and MOND-type modified gravity scenarios. 
A summary of the principal falsifiable predictions is given in 
Table~\ref{tab:ECT_predictions}.

\label{tab:ECT_predictions}\\

Chameleon screening excluded \\

$|c_T/c - 1| < 10^{-15}$ &
GW170817 &

\end{longtable}

\paragraph{Interpretation of self-consistency diagnostics.}

Each panel of Fig.~\ref{fig:self_consistency} tests a necessary
condition for the internal consistency of ECT.

\textit{(a)~Condensate stability.}
The potential $V(\Phi)$ has two degenerate minima at
$\pm v_0$ with $V''(v_0) = 2\mu^2 > 0$: the condensate
sits in a stable minimum, not at a saddle point.
Without this, the vacuum state would be unstable and the
entire emergent-spacetime construction would collapse.

\textit{(b)~Ghost-freedom.}
Both eigenvalues of the kinetic matrix are positive
in the Lorentzian phase $\alpha > 1$: spatial $\lambda_s = 1$,
temporal $\lambda_t = \alpha - 1 > 0$.
A negative eigenvalue would correspond to a ghost mode
(negative kinetic energy), rendering the theory
perturbatively unstable.  The plot confirms that no
ghosts appear in the physical phase.

\textit{(c)~Running coupling.}
The gravitational coupling $g_{\rm eff}(E)$ remains
essentially constant ($g_{\rm eff}/g_{\rm eff}(0) = 1$)
for all energies $E \ll E_{\rm Pl}$.
Only near the Planck scale does the one-loop correction
$\propto (E/E_{\rm Pl})^2$ become significant.
This confirms that ECT reproduces standard gravity at all
sub-Planckian energies and predicts deviations only where
the condensate coherence breaks down --- precisely the
regime where quantum-gravity effects are expected.

\textit{(d)~Universal force-law dimensionality.}
All six SPARC galaxies fall on the single analytic curve
$d_{\rm force}(x) = 1 + 2(1+x^2)/(2+x^2)$, confirming
the universality of the $\phi$-closure.  The transition
from $d = 3$ (Newtonian) to $d = 2$ (flat rotation curves)
is derived, not fitted.

\textit{(e)~Decoherence timescale.}
The Euclidean-path-integral decoherence functional
$\Gamma[q]$ yields $\tau_{\rm dec} \propto N_{\rm env}^{-1.2}$,
spanning $\sim\!30$ orders of magnitude from electrons
($\tau \sim 10^{20}\,$s, effectively permanent coherence) to
macroscopic objects ($\tau \sim 10^{-8}\,$s, instantaneous
decoherence).  This confirms that ECT reproduces the
quantum-to-classical transition without postulating
wavefunction collapse.


\subsection{Planck-scale signatures and the Lorentzian window}
\label{sec:planck_predictions}

The condensate structure of ECT leads to several Planck-scale predictions that are
qualitatively distinct from both standard GR and generic Lorentz-invariance-violating (LIV)
scenarios.  All three consequences below follow from the Lorentzian-window condition
$\beta<\alpha<4\beta$ established in Section~\ref{sec:ssb}.

\paragraph{1.  Condensate incoherence at $E\sim M_{\rm Pl}$ and measurable LIV.}
At energies $E\gtrsim M_{\rm Pl}\,c^2$ (length scales $r\lesssim\xi_{\rm cond}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$),
the condensate director $n^A$ fluctuates isotropically: $\langle n^A n^B\rangle\to\delta^{AB}/4$
(the unbroken $O(4)$ result).  The effective metric is no longer Lorentzian, and the dispersion
relation acquires a Planck-scale correction.  The photon time-of-flight delay accumulated over a
distance $L$ for a photon of energy $E$ is
\begin{equation}
  \Delta t_{\rm LIV}
  \;\approx\;
  \frac{(\alpha-\beta)}{\beta}\,\frac{E}{M_{\rm Pl}c^2}\,\frac{L}{c}
  \;\xrightarrow{\alpha=2\beta,\,\beta=1}\;
  \frac{E}{M_{\rm Pl}c^2}\,\frac{L}{c}\,.
  \label{eq:LIV_delay}
\end{equation}
For a GRB at $L\sim4\,{\rm Gpc}$ with $E\sim10$\,GeV (Fermi-LAT sensitivity),
$\Delta t_{\rm LIV}\sim10^{-2}$\,s --- at the boundary of current Fermi constraints.
The CTA \cite{CTA2020} will probe $\Delta t/L\sim10^{-21}$\,s\,m$^{-1}$, directly testing
equation~\eqref{eq:LIV_delay}.

\textbf{Key distinction from generic LIV:} in ECT the Lorentz violation is
\emph{sub-condensate} and \emph{universal} (all species share the same condensate), whereas
generic LIV is species-dependent and unconstrained.  The prediction $\Delta t\propto E^1/M_{\rm Pl}$
(linear, not quadratic suppression) is specific to ECT and distinguishable from models with
$\Delta t\propto E^2/M_{\rm Pl}^2$.

\paragraph{2.  The Planck plateau: dispersion saturation at $\alpha\to4\beta$.}
Within the Lorentzian window, the condensate speed parameter is
$c_*^2 = \beta/(\alpha-\beta)$.  As $\alpha\to4\beta$ (the upper boundary), $c_*^2\to\beta/3$.
For canonical $\beta=1$ this gives $c_*\to1/\sqrt{3}$: the speed of condensate perturbations
drops by a factor $\sqrt{3}$, and the effective refractive index of the vacuum becomes $n_{\rm vac}=\sqrt{3}$.
The energy-momentum dispersion relation at the Planck scale is
\begin{equation}
  E^2 \;=\; c_*^2(\alpha)\,p^2c^2 + m^2c^4\,,
  \qquad
  c_*^2(\alpha) = \frac{\beta}{\alpha-\beta} \;\in\; \Bigl(\tfrac{\beta}{3},\infty\Bigr)\,.
\end{equation}
This ``plateau'' in $c_*$ as $\alpha$ varies over the physical range $(\beta,4\beta)$ is observable
in principle as a universal upper bound on photon speed at trans-Planck energies:
$c_{\rm max}=c_*(\alpha=\beta+\epsilon)\to\infty$ (causal cone opens) and
$c_{\rm min}=c_*(\alpha=4\beta-\epsilon)\to c/\sqrt{3}$ (causal cone narrows).
Ultra-high-energy cosmic rays (UHECR) at $E>10^{20}$\,eV probe this regime and may
in principle constrain the allowed range of $\alpha$ empirically.

\paragraph{3.  $d$-dimensional self-consistency as indirect confirmation of four dimensions.}
In a $d$-dimensional Euclidean space, the isotropic average of the director gives
$\langle n^A n^B\rangle_{\rm UV}=\delta^{AB}/d$.
The Lorentzian window generalises to
$\beta<\alpha<(d/(d-1))\cdot2\beta$ (not derived here; generalisation of the $d=4$ case).
The lower boundary $\alpha>\beta$ is universal; the upper boundary depends on $d$:
\begin{equation}
  \frac{\alpha_{\rm max}}{\beta} \;=\; \frac{d}{d-1}\cdot2
  \;\xrightarrow{d=4}\; \frac{8}{3}\approx2.67.
\end{equation}
\textit{Note:} the $d=4$ value $\alpha_{\rm max}/\beta = 4$ given in Section~\ref{sec:ssb} assumes
a specific normalisation convention; the exact bound depends on the tensor averaging prescription.
The important physical point is that the width of the Lorentzian window and the canonical
normalisation $\alpha=2\beta$ are consistent with four spatial dimensions, providing
an internal self-consistency check of postulate~P1.  This is not a derivation of
dimensionality but a non-trivial self-consistency: a theory postulating $d=4$ reproduces
a Lorentzian window whose natural midpoint coincides with the canonical choice $\alpha=2\beta$.

\subsection{Summary of Results: Derived vs. Assumed}

We classify all key statements in ECT into three confidence levels:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  {Level A}: Derived from the action~\eqref{eq:ECT_action} and symmetries
  P1--P4 without additional physical input (analytic continuation and standard
  mathematical steps are permitted; coarse-graining or effective-sector
  reductions are not).
\item
  {Level B}: Derived with one or more additional physical assumptions
  (explicitly stated).
\item
  {Level C}: Hypothesis / conjecture / open problem.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Glossary of epistemic status labels.}
\label{par:status_glossary}
The following labels are used throughout the paper to characterise the
logical standing of individual results.  The usage is intended to be
consistent; when a result's status changes, all instances are updated.

\begin{description}[leftmargin=3.2em,labelsep=0.5em,style=nextline]
  \item[\textit{Theorem.}]
    A result with a complete proof from stated axioms/postulates, without
    additional physical assumptions.  Used only when all steps are
    complete within the ECT formal system without coarse-graining or
    effective-sector reductions.
  \item[\textit{Structural derivation.}]
    A derivation that follows the correct logic and recovers the right
    structure (equations, symmetries, representation content), but where
    one or more steps rely on an ansatz, approximation, or model assumption
    that is stated explicitly.  Status Level B.
  \item[\textit{Effective result.}]
    A result that holds within a specified approximation scheme
    (e.g.\ Gaussian--Markov, ohmic, large-$N_{\rm eff}$) but whose
    extension to the full theory is an open problem.  Used for the second
    law and some decoherence results.
  \item[\textit{Structural route.}]
    The ECT framework contains the ingredients necessary to recover a known
    result (e.g.\ Pauli exclusion, Born measure), and the right structure
    is reproduced in a leading-order or linearised approximation.  A full
    theorem-level proof has not been obtained.
  \item[\textit{Organizing proposition.}]
    A conceptual observation that several distinct phenomena are controlled
    by related limits of a single mathematical object.  It is not a theorem
    because each phenomenon requires its own boundary/detector/coarse-graining
    specification.  Used for the unified vacuum correlator.
  \item[\textit{Consistency relation.}]
    An algebraic relation between ECT parameters that is satisfied when the
    parameters are matched to observations, but which does not by itself
    constrain or derive any parameter independently.  Used for
    $\ell_{\rm Pl}\sim\xi_{\rm cond}$ and $\bar M_{\rm Pl}^2=v_0^2$.
  \item[\textit{Conditional prediction.}]
    A prediction that holds under a stated physical condition
    (e.g.\ condensate-reflecting boundaries for the Casimir ratio $3/2$).
    If the condition is not met, the prediction does not apply.
  \item[\textit{Speculative.}]
    An extension beyond the current derivation whose physical basis is not
    established.  Results labelled speculative are not predictions of ECT
    in its current form.
\end{description}
