\subsection{Classification of results: verified, unique, and open}
\label{sec:cat_abc}

Beyond the Level A/B/C classification of derivational rigor above,
ECT results can be usefully divided into three categories by their
epistemic status relative to the existing literature:

\paragraph{Category I — Independently verified in the literature (reproduced by ECT).}
These results were established by other means; ECT re-derives them from the
condensate action, providing a common microscopic origin.

\begin{itemize}\setlength\itemsep{2pt}
  \item Lorentzian metric from $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB — cf.\ Einstein-aether theory
        \cite{JacobsonMattingly2001}, where the $n^\mu n^\nu R$ term is postulated;
        here it follows from the condensate action.
  \item Caldeira-Leggett decoherence functional $\Gamma[q]$ reproduced from
        Euclidean path integral over environmental modes \cite{CaldeiraLeggett1983}.
  \item Inflationary spectral index $n_s = 1 - 2/N_e = 0.967$ — standard
        slow-roll result; ECT identifies the inflaton with the condensate
        amplitude \cite{Planck2018}.
  \item Leptogenesis $\eta_B \approx 9 \times 10^{-10}$ via Fukugita-Yanagida
        mechanism; ECT provides CP violation through condensate asymmetry
        \cite{FukugitaYanagida1986}.
  \item Quantised vortex circulation $\kappa = h/m$ in He-II \cite{Donnelly1991}
        and flux quantisation $\Phi_0 = h/2e$ in superconductors
        \cite{Abrikosov1957} — same topological origin as ECT condensate loops.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Category II — Unique predictions of ECT (no prior derivation).}
These results either appear first in ECT or take qualitatively new forms.

\begin{itemize}\setlength\itemsep{2pt}
  \item Lorentzian signature condition $\beta < \alpha < 4\beta$ as an
        explicit parametric window (not a postulate).
  \item $c_*$, $G_N$, $\hbar$ as three ratios of four condensate parameters
        $(v_0, \alpha, \beta, \lambda)$.
  \item Galactic weak-field modification from the nonlinear
        Lorentz-order-field branch: in the current $\phi$-closure
        framework, one environment parameter $\phi_{\rm env}$
        per galaxy controls the critical acceleration scale
        $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$.
  \item Radial acceleration scale $g^\dagger \propto cH_0$
        from the Lorentz-order-field dynamics in the near-critical
        cosmological vacuum; quasi-universal but with possible
        weak environmental modulation
        (Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
  \item Fifth force $\mathcal{L}_5 = \beta_5\,\bar\Psi\gamma^A n_A\Psi$ with
        Planck-suppressed coupling; spin precession at $\omega_5 \sim 10^{-10}$\,rad\,s$^{-1}$.
  \item Three condensate scales ($M_{\rm Pl}$, 246\,GeV, kpc) from one field
        via renormalisation-group running of $\lambda(\mu)$.
  \item Universe domain size $R_{\rm domain} = R_H e^{N_e}$ from condensate
        boundary condition $v_0(R_{\rm domain}) \to 0$.
  \item \emph{Quantum vacuum effects} (Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum}):
        Casimir pressure from three Goldstone modes,
        $(F/A)_{\rm ECT}=3/2\,(F/A)_{\rm QED}$ (\emph{conditional} on
        condensate/superfluid boundaries; not predicted for standard
        metallic plates); Unruh temperature
        $T_U=\hbar a/(2\pi c_* k_B)$ from analytic continuation of the
        Euclidean correlator; cosmological Goldstone production at the
        $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition with spectral index $n_s=0.967$.
  \item \emph{Black-hole information sector}
        (Section~\ref{sec:bh_information}, Appendix~\ref{app:bh_info}):
        universal near-horizon critical scale
        $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi} \approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}$
        (conditional on C2b);
        conditional theorem excluding exact Hawking thermality given
        unitarity, finite shell entropy, and complete evaporation;
        microscopic consistency criterion classifying which ECT completions
        can resolve the information paradox.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Category III — Open problems in ECT and elsewhere.}
These are unresolved in ECT and also unresolved (or ill-posed) in the
Standard Model or General Relativity.

\begin{itemize}\setlength\itemsep{2pt}
  \item $SU(3)$ colour: postulated in ECT; not derived from $O(4)\to O(3)$.
  \item Three fermion generations and Yukawa hierarchy:
        open in SM and in ECT.
  \item Fine structure constant $\alpha_{\rm fs} = 1/137$: not derived in ECT.
  \item Renormalisability at all loop orders in the full (non-linearised) theory.
  \item RG-quantitative connection between the three condensate scales.
\end{itemize}











\subsection{Laboratory tests}

The fifth interaction $\mathcal{L}_5 = \beta\,\bar{\Psi}\gamma^A n_A \Psi$
with $\beta \sim m_f/M_{\rm Pl}$ predicts several laboratory signatures:

\paragraph{Spin precession.}
The coupling induces an additional energy shift
$\omega_5 \sim \beta m_e c^2/\hbar \sim 10^{-10}$\,rad\,s$^{-1}$
for electrons, approaching the sensitivity of next-generation atomic
comagnetometers.

\paragraph{Equivalence principle violations.}
Because $\beta \propto m_f$, test bodies of different composition
experience slightly different accelerations.  The predicted E\"otv\"os
parameter is $\eta \sim |\beta_e - \beta_p|/g \sim 10^{-15}$,
below the current MICROSCOPE bound $\eta < 10^{-13}$ but within
reach of MICROSCOPE-2 (projected $\sim 10^{-15}$).

\paragraph{Polarisation-dependent photon propagation.}
Photons may acquire a weak polarisation dependence through the
condensate background: $\delta c/c \sim \beta^2 \sim (m_e/M_{\rm Pl})^2
\sim 10^{-45}$.  This is far below current sensitivity but provides
a stringent theoretical constraint.

\subsection{Astrophysical tests}

\paragraph{Galactic rotation curves and RAR.}
The ECT $\phi$-closure model (Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}) has been
tested on representative SPARC galaxies using one environment parameter
$\phi_{\rm env}$ per galaxy.  The exploratory closure fits yield
$\chi^2/N$ values comparable to MOND (with free $\Upsilon_\star$)
and $\Lambda$CDM/NFW (with two halo parameters); see
Table~\ref{tab:phi_fits}.  

\paragraph{External field effect.}
In the $\phi$-framework, an ambient gravitational field raises the
local $\phi_{\rm env}$, shifting $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ upward
and thereby partially screening the critical branch.  This predicts
specific rotation-curve modifications for satellite galaxies and
ultra-diffuse galaxies in strong external fields.

\paragraph{Neutron star structure.}
The enhanced condensate density in compact objects modifies the
Tolman--Oppenheimer--Volkoff equation.  ECT predicts
$M_{\rm max} \approx 2.17\,M_\odot$, consistent with
PSR~J0740+6620 ($2.14 \pm 0.10\,M_\odot$).

\paragraph{Gravitational wave constraints.}
The tensor $\Theta_{\mu\nu}[n]$ in the generalised Einstein equations
may produce small shifts in quasi-normal mode frequencies during
black hole ringdown, testable with LIGO/Virgo/KAGRA.

\subsection{Cosmological signatures}

\paragraph{Dark energy equation of state.}
ECT predicts $w_0 = -1 + 2\rho_{\rm kin}/(3\rho_{\rm cond}) \approx -0.83$,
testable by DESI, Euclid, and LSST through combined BAO+SNe constraints.
A detection of $w_0 > -1$ at the predicted level would support the
condensate interpretation.

\paragraph{Time variation of $G$.}
If $\chi(t)$ evolves on cosmological timescales, $G_{\rm eff}(t) \propto 1/\chi(t)$
produces $|\dot{G}/G| \sim 10^{-13}$--$10^{-15}$\,yr$^{-1}$,
constrained by lunar laser ranging, binary pulsars, and BBN consistency.

\paragraph{CMB and ISW.}
The spatially varying $G_{\rm eff}(x)$ may enhance the ISW signal
in cosmic voids, producing a CMB--LSS cross-correlation excess at
the $\sim 2\sigma$ level, consistent with current observations.




%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


% --- Observable predictions (merged from former standalone section) ---

\subsection{Additional Observable Predictions}

The Euclidean Condensate Theory leads to several potential
observational consequences that may distinguish it from both the
standard $\Lambda$CDM cosmological model and other modified-gravity
frameworks.  The following predictions arise from the structure of the
condensate and the dynamics of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$.

\paragraph{1. Emergent acceleration scale}

The Lorentz-order field $\phi$ introduces a critical acceleration
scale $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ that depends on the ambient
vacuum-order background
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
For typical isolated disc galaxies,
\[
g_\dagger \sim 10^{-10}\,\mathrm{m\,s^{-2}},
\]
coinciding with the empirical acceleration scale appearing in the
radial acceleration relation.  Unlike MOND, this scale is not a
universal constant but varies weakly with environment.

\paragraph{2. Environment dependence of gravitational coupling}

Since the effective gravitational coupling depends on the
Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}), with
$G_{\rm eff} = G_N\,e^{-\phi}$,
regions with different ambient Lorentz-order background may
exhibit slightly different effective gravitational strengths. This could lead to small
environment-dependent deviations from standard gravitational dynamics.

\paragraph{3. Cluster collision signatures}

In cluster mergers such as the Bullet Cluster, the $\phi$-field
tracks the component with higher local density --- compact stellar
clumps in Bullet-type systems, or dense gas cores in Abell~520-type
systems (Section~\ref{sec:fifth_force}).  This produces a spatial
separation between baryonic gas distributions and gravitational
lensing peaks that matches observations qualitatively, though the
total lensing amplitude is currently underestimated by a factor
$\sim\!3$--$7$ (Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results}).

\paragraph{4. Possible ultralight condensate excitations}

The $O(4)\to O(3)$ breaking generates three Goldstone modes with
masses of order $m \sim H_0 \sim 10^{-33}\,$eV
(de~Broglie wavelength $\sim$Mpc, comparable to large-scale
structure).  These are not the kpc-scale fuzzy dark matter of
\cite{HuBarkanaGruzinov2000} (which requires $m \sim 10^{-22}\,$eV)
but a distinct cosmological-scale component.
Whether such ultra-light modes contribute measurably to
structure formation or to the cosmological dark sector remains
an open question requiring dedicated analysis.








%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Early galaxy and black hole formation (JWST anomalies)}
\label{sec:jwst}

\textit{Observational context.}
The James Webb Space Telescope has revealed a population of unexpectedly massive
galaxies and supermassive black holes at redshifts $z>10$, corresponding to
cosmic ages $<500$\,Myr after the Big Bang \cite{Labbe2023,Finkelstein2022}.
The observed stellar masses ($M_\star\sim 10^{9}$--$10^{11}\,M_\odot$) and black-hole
masses ($M_{\rm BH}\sim 10^{7}$--$10^{9}\,M_\odot$) exceed the expectations of
standard $\Lambda$CDM by factors of several within the available assembly time.

\textit{ECT mechanism ($\phi$-first).}
In ECT $\phi$-logic, the effective gravitational coupling on the
cosmological background is controlled by the background order field
$\phi_b(z)$ (Section~\ref{sec:mp_nonlinear}):
\begin{equation}
  G_{\rm eff}(z) = G_N\,e^{-\phi_b(z)},
  \qquad
  M^2_{\rm eff}(z) = \bar M^2_{\rm Pl}\,e^{\phi_b(z)}.
  \label{eq:Geff_jwst}
\end{equation}
This is the same relation that governs the nonlinear gravity and
galactic-scale $\phi$-branch — a single order field unifies the
cosmological and galactic gravitational sectors.

The full field decomposes as $\phi(X)=\phi_b(z)+\delta\phi(X)$,
where $\phi_b(z)$ is the slowly evolving cosmological background
and $\delta\phi(X)$ encodes local deviations.
The $\phi$-logic suggests qualitatively that dense collapsing
regions may screen $\delta\phi$, driving the local dynamics back
toward the GR branch; a derivation of this screening from the
nonlinear $\phi$-equation remains open.

\textit{Background ansatz.}
For consistency with the cosmological fit and the running gravitational
coupling of Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}, we adopt the
phenomenological background profile:
\begin{equation}
  \phi_b(z) = -2\varepsilon\ln(1+z),
  \qquad \varepsilon \approx 0.01.
  \label{eq:phi_b_ansatz}
\end{equation}
This is a phenomenological ansatz rewritten in $\phi$-language,
not a derived solution of the cosmological $\phi$-equation
(a first-principles derivation of $\phi_b(z)$ from the background
$\phi$-dynamics remains open).
With ansatz~\eqref{eq:phi_b_ansatz}, eq.~\eqref{eq:Geff_jwst}
recovers exactly $G_{\rm eff}(z)=G_N(1+z)^{2\varepsilon}$.

\textit{Structure growth.}
In the leading sub-horizon approximation, and neglecting explicit
perturbations of the $\phi$-sector in the growth equation, one may
write the standard continuity--Euler--Poisson system with the
effective coupling:
\begin{equation}
  \ddot\delta + 2H\dot\delta
  - 4\pi G_{\rm eff}(z)\,\bar\rho\,\delta = 0.
\end{equation}
At leading order in $\varepsilon$ this gives
\begin{equation}
  \frac{D_{\rm ECT}(z)}{D_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}(z)}
  \approx 1 + \varepsilon\ln(1+z) + O(\varepsilon^2).
\end{equation}
At $z=10$: $D_{\rm ECT}/D_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}\approx 1.024$.

\textit{Halo abundance (Press--Schechter).}
Setting $f(z)\equiv G_{\rm eff}(z)/G_N = e^{-\phi_b(z)}$,
the effective rarity of a $\nu$-$\sigma$ peak becomes
$\nu_{\rm eff}=\nu/\sqrt{f}$, giving
\begin{equation}
  \frac{n_{\rm ECT}}{n_{\Lambda{\rm CDM}}}
  = \exp\!\left[\frac{\nu^2}{2}\!\left(1-\frac{1}{f(z)}\right)\right].
  \label{eq:PS_phi}
\end{equation}
Numerical values for $\varepsilon=0.01$ are given in
Table~\ref{tab:jwst_ps}; they are \emph{unchanged} from the
previous estimate --- the improvement here is conceptual
(unified $\phi$-language with the gravity section) rather than
numerical.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Halo abundance enhancement in ECT vs.\ $\Lambda$CDM,
eq.~\eqref{eq:PS_phi}, for $\varepsilon=0.01$.
$\nu$ = peak rarity parameter; JWST anomalies correspond to
$\nu\sim5$--6.
The ansatz~\eqref{eq:phi_b_ansatz} gives
$f(z)=(1+z)^{2\varepsilon}$.}
\label{tab:jwst_ps}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{ccccc}
\hline
$z$ & $\phi_b(z)$ & $f=e^{-\phi_b}$ & $\nu=5$ & $\nu=6$ \\
\hline
 7  & $-0.043$ & 1.043 & $\times 1.7$ & $\times 2.1$ \\
10  & $-0.048$ & 1.049 & $\times 1.8$ & $\times 2.3$ \\
12  & $-0.052$ & 1.053 & $\times 1.9$ & $\times 2.5$ \\
15  & $-0.055$ & 1.057 & $\times 2.0$ & $\times 2.6$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\textit{Quantitative assessment.}
For the most anomalous JWST sources ($\nu\sim5$--6),
the ECT $\phi$-mechanism predicts an overabundance of $\times2$--3
relative to $\Lambda$CDM.
The observed deficit is $\times10$--100~\cite{BoylanKolchin2023},
so in its present controlled $\phi$-first form ECT \emph{alleviates
but does not resolve} the JWST early-structure tension.
With the background ansatz~\eqref{eq:phi_b_ansatz}, no additional
numerical improvement over the leading-order estimate is obtained.

The $\phi$-logic suggests that early-time global enhancement
($\phi_b<0$) and local screening in dense proto-galactic cores
may ultimately be described within a single order-field framework.
A derivation of this mechanism from the full nonlinear $\phi$-equation,
and the question of whether a nontrivial background history $\phi_b(z)$
could provide stronger early enhancement, are left as open problems.
(Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).



\section{Comparison with Existing Approaches}
\label{sec:comparison}

This section compares ECT with several alternative approaches
to gravity and cosmology, highlighting structural differences
and shared features.

\subsection{ECT as a derivation, not a unification}
\label{sec:derivation_not_unification}

A preliminary remark distinguishes ECT structurally from most
other unified or emergent-gravity proposals.  The typical strategy
in constructing unified theories is to \emph{combine} two existing
frameworks---for example, by embedding quantum field theory and
General Relativity into a common mathematical structure such as
a higher-dimensional manifold or a superstring action.  In this
paradigm the two frameworks are accepted as given and the goal is
to find a larger structure that contains both.

ECT proceeds differently.  Starting from a single set of
postulates---a four-dimensional Euclidean condensate with $O(4)$
symmetry undergoing spontaneous symmetry breaking
$O(4)\to O(3)$---several structures of modern physics
\emph{emerge as consequences} within a single framework
(at varying levels of rigour; see Table~\ref{tab:ect-levels}):
the Lorentzian metric signature, relativistic dispersion, quantum
dynamics, the gravitational coupling, the arrow of time, and
galactic-scale modifications of gravity all emerge from the same
condensate action.  The theory does not attempt to reconcile
General Relativity with quantum mechanics by engineering their
coexistence; rather, both arise as limiting descriptions of the
same underlying condensate field in different regimes.

An important corollary is that the mutual consistency of these
results is not assumed but verified: the fact that the emergent
quantum and gravitational sectors are not in contradiction is a
non-trivial consequence of the common origin, not a built-in feature.

The key distinction from unification programmes is the direction of
derivation.  ECT does not combine existing frameworks by design.
The various structures~--- Lorentzian geometry, quantum mechanics,
gravity~--- are not stitched together: they emerge from the same
condensate dynamics within $O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking.
Gauge fields are structurally embedded via condensate phase symmetries,
though the full Standard Model derivation remains partial (D16,
Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).
In ECT the core components share a common origin rather than being
independent inputs; the phrase ``derivation, not unification'' refers
to this common origin, not to a claim of complete logical necessity.

A concrete test of the distinction: in a genuine unification, removing one component (e.g.\ quantum mechanics) leaves the rest intact.  In ECT the components are not independent---the Lorentzian signature, $\hbar$, and $G_N$ are three faces of the same condensate field, and none can be isolated without abandoning the common origin.

This derivational character does not mean that the individual results
are new in isolation.  Several building blocks of ECT have been
explored previously.  What distinguishes ECT is the claim that
\emph{all of these structures follow from a single action} defined on
a Euclidean four-space, without recourse to multiple independent
hypotheses.  Whether this survives detailed scrutiny at all energy
scales remains an open question.

\subsection{Comparison with Other Approaches}

A comparison of ECT with several alternative approaches to gravity is summarised in Table~\ref{tab:theory_comparison}.

\label{tab:theory_comparison}\\

\subsubsection{Relation to Sakharov induced
gravity}
The derivation of $G_N$ in Section~\ref{sec:consistency_relations} via coefficient matching of quadratic
actions is structurally equivalent to Sakharov's induced gravity
\cite{Sakharov1968}: gravity as an effective theory
arising from integrating out matter fields. The key distinction is that
in ECT the "matter" is the condensate itself (the same field that
generates spacetime), whereas in Sakharov's approach conventional matter
fields are present on a pre-existing curved background.


\subsection{$\Lambda$CDM}

The standard $\Lambda$CDM model postulates the existence of cold dark
matter particles and a cosmological constant $\Lambda$ as independent
ingredients added to General Relativity.  Dark matter is introduced as
a new particle species whose only significant interaction is
gravitational, while $\Lambda$ is a constant vacuum energy density
with no dynamical origin.

ECT differs in several structural respects.  First, the galactic
mass-discrepancy phenomenology is attributed to the nonlinear response
of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}): in dilute environments the
critical $\phi$-branch activates and enhances the effective
gravitational pull, reproducing flat rotation curves, the RAR, and the
BTFR without a new particle sector.  Second, the effective cosmological
term $\Lambda_{\rm eff}(X) = V(\Phi_0(X))$ is a dynamical quantity
determined by the condensate potential, not a fundamental constant.
Third, the gravitational constant is expressed via the coefficient-matching
relation $G_N = 1/(8\pi v_0^2\chi_\infty)$ [$\chi_\infty\equiv\alpha{-}\beta$]
(identified rather than freely adjustable, though not a fully non-circular
first-principles derivation; see Section~\ref{sec:consistency_relations}).

At the phenomenological level, ECT reproduces the standard cosmological
expansion history in the limit of a homogeneous condensate, but
predicts deviations on galactic scales (via the $\phi$-branch) and
in the dark energy equation of state ($w_0 \neq -1$,
Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}).

\subsection{MOND}

Milgrom's Modified Newtonian Dynamics \cite{Milgrom1983} introduces a
fundamental acceleration scale $a_0 \approx 1.2 \times 10^{-10}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$
below which the gravitational force transitions from the Newtonian $1/r^2$
law to a $1/r$ scaling.  MOND successfully predicts galactic rotation curves
and the baryonic Tully--Fisher relation with remarkable economy.

ECT shares several phenomenological features with MOND: both predict
flat rotation curves, the BTFR, and a characteristic acceleration scale.
However, the conceptual origin differs fundamentally.  In MOND, $a_0$
is a new fundamental constant of nature; in ECT, it emerges as
$g_\dagger \propto c^2\phi_*(\phi_{\rm gal})$, determined by the ambient
degree of Lorentzian order of the vacuum
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
Moreover, ECT predicts that $g_\dagger$ is \emph{quasi-universal but
not exactly constant}: it may exhibit weak environmental modulation
correlated with the local cosmic density --- a qualitative distinction
from MOND, where $a_0$ is strictly fundamental.

Quantitatively, at equal parameter count (one free parameter each:
$\phi_{\rm env}$ for ECT, $\Upsilon_\star$ for MOND), the two
frameworks perform comparably overall.  ECT achieves
$\chi^2/N \sim 1.8$--$11.5$ versus
MOND $\chi^2/N \sim 0.7$--$12.7$ (with free $\Upsilon_\star$)
and $\Lambda$CDM/NFW
$\chi^2/N \sim 0.2$--$8.1$ (two halo parameters) --- see
Table~\ref{tab:phi_fits}.  ECT is favoured for some void-like and
Local-Group systems; MOND performs better for some group-environment
galaxies.  Direct numerical solutions of the
$\phi$-equation~\eqref{eq:RAR} may further improve
the fits (OP-new-5).

\subsection{Emergent gravity scenarios}

Several approaches treat gravity as an emergent phenomenon rather than
a fundamental interaction.  Verlinde's entropic gravity \cite{Verlinde2011}
derives Newton's law from holographic entropy considerations;
Padmanabhan's emergent paradigm \cite{Padmanabhan2010} relates the
expansion of space to the difference between surface and bulk degrees
of freedom.

ECT differs from these approaches in its starting point: rather than
beginning with thermodynamic or information-theoretic axioms, ECT
starts from a concrete field-theoretic condensate in Euclidean
four-space and derives emergent gravity through standard variational
methods.  The condensate provides a specific microscopic realisation
of the emergent metric, including a definite particle spectrum
(Goldstone modes, radial mode, graviton) and falsifiable predictions
(EFE, BTFR slope, $\phi_{\rm env}$-environment correlation).

Causal Dynamical Triangulations (CDT) \cite{Ambjorn2005} also obtain
an emergent Lorentzian geometry from a Euclidean path integral, but
through a discrete lattice approach rather than a continuum condensate.
CDT does not produce a particle spectrum or galactic-scale predictions.

\subsection{Induced gravity}

Sakharov's induced gravity \cite{Sakharov1968} proposes that the
Einstein--Hilbert action arises as a one-loop quantum correction from
matter fields propagating on a curved background.  The gravitational
constant is then determined by the matter content:
$G_N^{-1} \propto \sum_i m_i^2 \ln(m_i^2/\mu^2)$.

The derivation of $G_N$ in ECT via coefficient matching of quadratic
actions (Section~\ref{sec:macroscopic}) is structurally analogous.
The key distinction is that in ECT the ``matter'' is the condensate
itself---the same field that generates spacetime---whereas in
Sakharov's approach conventional matter fields are present on a
pre-existing curved background.  ECT therefore avoids the circularity
of assuming a background metric to derive the metric dynamics.

Einstein--aether theory \cite{JacobsonMattingly2001} introduces a unit
timelike vector field $u^\mu$ with $u_\mu u^\mu = -1$ and constructs
all possible two-derivative invariants.  The resulting action contains
four free coupling constants $c_1, \ldots, c_4$.  In ECT the analogous
vector field $n_A$ arises from the condensate direction, and the
coupling structure is determined by the condensate action rather than
being postulated independently.  In particular, the $n_\mu n_\nu R$
term that must be postulated in Einstein--aether theory emerges
variationally in ECT.

\subsection{Other related approaches}

\paragraph{Barbour's timeless mechanics.}
Barbour \cite{Barbour1999} proposes that time is not fundamental
and that dynamics should be formulated relationally on
three-dimensional configuration space (``shape space'').
ECT shares the premise that time is emergent, but differs in
starting from a four-dimensional Euclidean manifold rather than
three-dimensional spatial configurations.  In ECT, time emerges
from a specific symmetry-breaking mechanism ($O(4)\to O(3)$),
whereas in Barbour's framework it arises from the best-matching
procedure on shape space.

\paragraph{Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz gravity.}
Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz gravity abandons Lorentz invariance at high
energies by introducing anisotropic scaling between space and time
($t \to b^z t$, $x \to b\,x$ with $z \neq 1$).
While both ECT and Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz gravity break Lorentz
symmetry, the mechanisms are fundamentally different: in
Ho\v{r}ava--Lifshitz theory, time is a fundamental coordinate
with a preferred foliation, whereas in ECT there is no time at all
in the fundamental description---it emerges dynamically from the
condensate.

\paragraph{Hartle--Hawking no-boundary proposal.}
The Hartle--Hawking no-boundary proposal \cite{HartleHawking1983}
describes the quantum state of the Universe via a Euclidean path
integral over compact, boundary-free four-geometries.  Near the
``beginning'', the geometry becomes effectively Euclidean, removing
the initial singularity without introducing a boundary.  ECT shares
the premise that the primordial regime is Euclidean and pre-temporal,
but the roles of Euclidean geometry differ fundamentally.  In the
no-boundary proposal, Euclidean geometry is an instrument for defining
the wave function $\Psi[h_{ij}] \sim \int\mathcal{D}g\,e^{-S_E}$;
the Lorentzian universe is recovered by analytic continuation
$\tau\to it$.  In ECT the Euclidean phase is the
\emph{fundamental physical state} of the condensate: Lorentzian
spacetime emerges not by analytic continuation but by spontaneous
$O(4)\to O(3)$ symmetry breaking, which selects a preferred direction
$\langle n_A\rangle = \delta_{Aw}$ and generates the Lorentzian
effective metric.  ECT thus provides a candidate
\emph{microphysical completion} of the no-boundary idea: it explains
dynamically why the analytic continuation to the Lorentzian branch is
physically realised, why the metric signature is $(-+++)$ rather than
$(++++)$, and why the transition is macroscopically irreversible
(arrow of time from $N_{\rm eff}\gg1$ decoherence).  In this sense
the no-boundary proposal and ECT are complementary rather than
competing: the former offers an effective cosmological prescription,
while ECT offers a candidate physical mechanism that makes such a
prescription natural.

\paragraph{Loop quantum cosmology.}
Loop quantum cosmology (LQC) applies the quantisation techniques of
loop quantum gravity to cosmological minisuperspace models
\cite{Ambjorn2005}.  The central result is that quantum-geometry
effects become repulsive at Planck density, replacing the Big Bang
singularity with a quantum \emph{bounce}:
\begin{equation}
  H^2 = \frac{8\pi G}{3}\,\rho\!\left(1 - \frac{\rho}{\rho_c}\right),
  \label{eq:LQC_bounce}
\end{equation}
where $\rho_c \sim \rho_{\rm Pl}$ is the critical density.  Both LQC
and ECT replace the classical Big Bang singularity by a non-classical
primordial regime, and both admit a ``pre-standard-cosmology'' phase.
The conceptual starting points are, however, qualitatively different.
In LQC spacetime geometry is fundamental and primary: it is quantised
and discretised at the Planck scale, but the Lorentzian signature and
the notion of time are present from the outset.  In ECT, by contrast,
Lorentzian spacetime is not primary: it \emph{emerges} from a
pre-Lorentzian Euclidean condensate through vacuum ordering, and the
metric signature itself is a consequence of $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB.  ECT
therefore addresses a deeper question than LQC: not what replaces the
singularity \emph{within} a Lorentzian framework, but why there is a
Lorentzian framework at all.  An interesting open question is whether,
once the Lorentzian phase is established in ECT, its early
strongly-quantum regime might admit an effective description resembling
the LQC bounce equation~\eqref{eq:LQC_bounce}.

\subsection{Why earlier programmes did not reach these conclusions}
\label{sec:why_earlier}

A natural question is the following: since many of the building blocks of
ECT---Euclidean quantum gravity, induced gravity, condensate analogies,
SSB of Lorentz symmetry---have been known for decades, why did earlier
programmes not arrive at the same synthesis?  Several structural reasons
can be identified.

\paragraph{Euclidean approaches were used as a computational tool, not
a starting point.}
In the Hartle--Hawking programme \cite{HartleHawking1983} and in
Euclidean quantum gravity, the Wick rotation $t\to-i\tau$ is employed as
a regularisation device.  The Euclidean description is an intermediate
step; physical content is recovered by continuing back to Lorentzian
signature.  ECT inverts this logic: Euclidean four-space is the
\emph{fundamental} description, and the Lorentzian signature is obtained
as a consequence of SSB, not by analytic continuation.  This shift---treating
Wick rotation not as a trick but as a symmetry-breaking transition---is
what opens the door to deriving the metric signature rather than assuming it.

\paragraph{Condensate analogies were regarded as illustrative, not foundational.}
Volovik's ``Universe in a helium droplet'' \cite{Volovik2003} provides
beautiful condensed-matter analogies for relativistic QFT and gravity.
However, the analogy is suggestive rather than literal: the condensate
is not identified with the physical vacuum, and no attempt is made to
derive fundamental constants or galactic-scale predictions from condensate
parameters.  ECT takes the step of treating the condensate as the actual
microscopic description of the vacuum.

\paragraph{SSB of the Lorentz group was studied in isolation.}
Programmes exploring spontaneous Lorentz violation (e.g.\ 
Einstein--aether theory \cite{JacobsonMattingly2001}) start from a
Lorentzian background and ask how Lorentz symmetry might be softly
broken.  They do not address where the Lorentzian background itself
comes from---the deeper question that ECT answers through $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB.

\paragraph{No connection to galactic-scale phenomenology was sought.}
Quantum-gravity programmes were almost exclusively concerned with
Planck-scale physics.  The condensate parameters were never matched to
galactic dynamics, dark matter, or the radial acceleration relation.
ECT crosses this divide by identifying $v_0\sim\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ and
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ with the galactic acceleration scale,
connecting Planck-scale microphysics to kiloparsec-scale observations.

In summary, the individual ingredients were available but not assembled
into a single framework.  The synthesis required treating the Euclidean
condensate as both fundamental and physical.

\paragraph{No single framework simultaneously achieved five goals.}
In retrospect, no earlier programme assembled all five of the following
within a single action:
(1) a mechanism for the \emph{birth of time} from SSB;
(2) $\hbar$, $G$, and $c$ as ratios of a \emph{single field's} parameters;
(3) scale separation between quantum (Euclidean) and classical (Lorentzian)
regimes as a consequence of \emph{dimensionality};
(4) a dark sector from the \emph{same condensate};
(5) testable \emph{galactic-scale} predictions connected to Planck-scale microphysics.
ECT assembles all five within a single framework, at the cost of leaving
several open problems (Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).


\subsection{Unification diagram}
\label{sec:unification_diagram}

Figure~\ref{fig:unification_graph} summarises how ECT relates to
the five major frameworks of modern physics.
ECT was developed independently; the left-hand nodes show points of comparison.
The right-hand column shows the ECT results that connect, extend, or
explain each framework.
Arrows pointing left (from ECT to framework) are labelled by the
relationship type: \emph{derived} (strict analytic result),
\emph{embedded} (SM gauge group: postulated with standard group-theory
embedding), \emph{explained} (cosmological observations).
Arrows pointing right show the specific ECT prediction or bridge.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/fig_unification.png}
\caption{ECT bridging isolated frameworks of modern physics.
\textbf{Left}: five pre-existing frameworks addressing separate sectors;
ECT was developed independently and these are shown for comparison only.
\textbf{Centre}: the single ECT condensate field.
\textbf{Right}: ECT derivations, bridges, and predictions that connect the left-hand frameworks.
Solid arrows from ECT to a framework denote structures derived within ECT.
The dashed arrow for the Standard Model indicates that the SU(2)$\times$U(1) sector
is derived but SU(3) is currently embedded (postulated).}
\label{fig:unification_graph}
\end{figure}




%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{Derivation logic graph}
\label{sec:derivation_graph}

The following diagram shows the logical structure of ECT: the chain from
postulates through derivations to predictions.
Nodes are shaded by type:
\textbf{dark grey} = phenomenological input,
\textbf{medium grey (P1--P4)} = postulate,
\textbf{light grey} = derived result (analytic, Level~A),
\textbf{grey} = result with one stated physical assumption (Level~B),
\textbf{dashed outline} = open problem (Level~C).
Solid arrows indicate strict derivations; dashed arrows indicate steps
that require additional physical assumptions.

\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\includegraphics[width=\textwidth]{figures/fig_derivation_logic.png}
\caption{ECT derivational logic graph.
Arrows show the logical flow from postulates (\textbf{medium grey, bold}) through
derived results (\textbf{light grey}, Level~A = strict derivation) and
results requiring physical assumptions (\textbf{grey}, Level~B) to
phenomenological inputs (\textbf{dark grey}) and open problems (\textit{dashed outline}).
Dashed arrows indicate steps that require physical assumptions beyond the
core postulates P1--P4.
The legend is shown at the bottom of the figure.}
\label{fig:derivation_graph}
\end{figure}

\subsection{Possible condensate origin of the fine-structure constant}
\label{subsec:alpha_fs}

The fine-structure constant $\alpha_{\rm fs} = e^2/(4\pi\epsilon_0\hbar c) \approx 1/137$
is one of the best-measured dimensionless constants in physics and one
of the least understood.  Its value is not predicted by the Standard
Model; it is an input.  This subsection describes a possible mechanism
within ECT, classified honestly as a \textbf{Status~III open problem}:
a plausible mechanism exists, but no quantitative derivation has been completed.

\paragraph{Photon as a Goldstone boson.}
In ECT, the photon is identified with the $U(1)$ Goldstone boson
arising from the phase symmetry of the condensate
(Section~\ref{sec:gauge}).  Its kinetic term acquires a
wave-function renormalisation $Z_A(\mu)$ that runs with the
renormalisation scale $\mu$.  At the condensate scale $v_0 \sim \bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$,
$Z_A(v_0) = 1$ by normalisation; at the electroweak scale $v_2 \sim 246$~GeV
the running gives $Z_A(v_2) = 1/\alpha_{\rm fs}$.

\paragraph{Logarithmic running and the condensate hierarchy.}
The RG equation for the photon wave-function renormalisation in the
condensate EFT takes the schematic form
\begin{equation}
  \mu\,\frac{d Z_A}{d\mu} = b_{\rm ECT}\,Z_A^2,
\end{equation}
where $b_{\rm ECT}$ is the one-loop beta-function coefficient.
Integrating from $v_2$ to $v_0$:
\begin{equation}
  \frac{1}{\alpha_{\rm fs}} \approx b_{\rm ECT}\,\ln\!\left(\frac{v_0}{v_2}\right)
  = b_{\rm ECT}\,\ln\!\left(\frac{2.435\times10^{18}\,\text{GeV}}{246\,\text{GeV}}\right)
  \approx 36.8\,b_{\rm ECT}.
\end{equation}
The observed value $1/\alpha_{\rm fs} \approx 137$ therefore requires
$b_{\rm ECT} \approx 3.72$, which is an order-unity coefficient with
no fine-tuning.  This is encouraging but not a derivation: computing
$b_{\rm ECT}$ from first principles within ECT requires a one-loop
calculation of the photon self-energy in the condensate background,
which has not yet been performed.

\textbf{Status.} The condensate RG running provides a qualitative
explanation of why $\alpha_{\rm fs}$ might be order $1/\ln(v_0/v_2)$
without fine-tuning.  A quantitative derivation is listed as Open
Problem~OP11 (Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).

\section{Open Problems}
\label{sec:open_problems}

\subsubsection{Mathematical status of the path integral}
\label{sec:path_integral}
This appendix addresses the precise mathematical definition of the
partition function $Z$ when the action~\eqref{eq:ECT_action} is not positive definite
for all field configurations.

\subsubsection{The problem}
At the quadratic level around the vacuum, the action~\eqref{eq:quadratic_action} contains a
negative kinetic term
$-(\alpha-\beta)(\partial_w\varphi)^2/(2\beta)$.
Naively, the Euclidean path integral
$Z=\int\mathcal{D}\varphi\,e^{-S_E^{(2)}}$
would then diverge because the action is unbounded from below in the
$w$-direction.

\subsubsection{Picard--Lefschetz contour
deformation}
The standard resolution, used routinely in quantum gravity and quantum
cosmology, is to define $Z$ via contour deformation in the space of
complexified field configurations (Picard--Lefschetz theory). One
identifies the relevant saddle points of $S_E$ and deforms the
integration contour to pass through them along steepest-descent
directions ("thimbles"). The key steps are:

\begin{enumerate}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Identify saddle points:} the classical condensate vacuum
  $\varphi=0$ (for fluctuations) is a saddle with one
  unstable direction --- the $w$-momentum modes.
\item
  \textbf{Classify thimbles:} the Lefschetz thimble attached to each
  saddle is the set of field configurations on which
  ${\rm Im}(S_E)=$ const and ${\rm
  Re}(S_E)$ increases away from the saddle. For the $w$-momentum
  sector this thimble passes through imaginary $w$-momentum space,
  recovering the Lorentzian dispersion relation
  $\omega^2>0$.
\item
  \textbf{Result:} the path integral over the appropriate Lefschetz
  thimble gives a convergent oscillatory integral $\int
  e^{-{\rm
  Re}(S_E)}\,e^{i\,{\rm
  Im}(S_E)}$, which is precisely the Lorentzian path integral
  $e^{iS_M/\hbar}$.
\end{enumerate}

This demonstrates that the apparent instability of the Euclidean action
at $\alpha>\beta$ (i.e.\ $\alpha>1$ at $\beta=1$) is a feature, not a bug: it is
exactly what selects the correct Lorentzian contour. The same mechanism
arises in the no-boundary wave function of the universe
\cite{FeldbruggeLehnersTurok2017}, where the Lorentzian path integral
is defined as the steepest-descent contour of a complexified Euclidean
action.

\subsubsection{Alternative: higher-derivative
stabilisation}
A technically simpler (though physically distinct) option is to add a
Pauli--Villars-style regulator:

\begin{equation}
S_E\to S_E+\frac{1}{2M^2}\int(\partial_w^2\Phi)^2\,d^4X
\end{equation}

This makes the Euclidean action strictly positive definite for all
$M<\infty$. The Lorentzian effective theory for
$E\ll M$ then emerges with the same structure as derived
in Section~\ref{sec:ssb}. The limit $M\to\infty$ recovers the
original theory, but requires the Picard--Lefschetz treatment of
Section~D. We
list the rigorous proof of equivalence of the two formulations as future
work (Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).





The following problems remain open in the current formulation of ECT
and represent priority targets for future work.  They are listed in
approximate order of importance for the logical completeness of the theory.

\begin{description}

\item[\textbf{OP0 --- Microscopic origin of the condensate field $\Phi$.}]
ECT postulates $\Phi$ as a primitive scalar field (Postulate~P4).  The
theory makes no claim about what $\Phi$ is ``made of'' at a deeper
level.  This situation is not unique to ECT: the Higgs field in the
Standard Model and matter fields in General Relativity are equally
postulated without derivation from more primitive degrees of freedom.
A UV completion that derives $\Phi$ from, say, string moduli, a
composite bound state, or some other pre-geometric structure would
sharpen ECT's predictive power and potentially fix the three condensate
scales ($v_0$, $v_2$, $v_\text{gal}$) from a single microscopic
parameter.
\textit{Priority: foundational; not required for internal consistency.}

\item[\textbf{OP1 — Mathematical status of the Euclidean path integral.}]
The action~\eqref{eq:ECT_action} is not positive definite for $\alpha>\beta$,
making the na\"ive Euclidean path integral ill-defined.  Three remedies
are available (Picard--Lefschetz contour deformation, analytic
continuation from $\alpha<\beta$, or higher-derivative UV stabilisation),
but their rigorous equivalence has not been proved.

\textit{Contextual remark.}
This difficulty is not unique to ECT: it is a well-known open problem
shared by all Euclidean approaches to quantum gravity, including the
Hartle--Hawking no-boundary proposal~\cite{HartleHawking1983} and
standard Euclidean quantum gravity \cite{Gibbons1978}.
In each of these frameworks, the conformal-factor problem (or
equivalent sign instability) is handled by contour deformation,
analytic continuation, or a choice of integration cycle.
The Picard--Lefschetz method provides a systematic framework for
defining the correct integration cycle for oscillatory or
non-positive-definite actions, and has recently been applied to
the Lorentzian path integral of GR \cite{FeldbruggeLehnersTurok2017}.
In ECT, the same framework can in principle be applied: the
action is non-positive-definite only in the Lorentzian sector
($\alpha>\beta$), which is precisely the sector where
Picard--Lefschetz thimble deformation is applicable.
The difficulty is therefore to be understood as a manifestation
of the general unsolved problem of defining the gravitational path
integral rigorously~--- a problem inherited from GR, not introduced
by ECT.
\textit{Priority: essential for mathematical consistency; shared with
all Euclidean gravity programmes.}

\item[\textbf{OP2 — Full non-linear Einstein equations from ECT action.\ \normalfont\textit{Resolved for the minimal model.}}]
The anisotropic curvature term in eq.~\eqref{eq:gen_EE} has now been
derived by explicit commutation of covariant derivatives via the
Riemann identity (Appendix~\ref{app:curvature_coupling}).  The
calculation is complete for the minimal one-parameter case
$c_1=K_n$, $c_2=c_3=c_4=0$, and recovers the Einstein--aether
result of Jacobson \cite{Jacobson2004}.

What remains open is the derivation of the spatially varying
effective couplings $\Lambda_{\rm eff}(X)$ and $G_{\rm eff}(X)$
from the $\phi$-field dynamics beyond the weak-field expansion.
This requires a full non-perturbative solution of the coupled system
$(g_{AB},\Phi,n^A)$ in a cosmological or strong-field background.
\textit{Status: resolved for linearised + minimal non-linear case;
spatially varying $G_{\rm eff}(X)$ requires further work.}

\item[\textbf{OP3 — Graviton: Fierz--Pauli spectrum from ECT.\ \normalfont\textit{Step (i) resolved; step (ii) resolved at linearised level.}}]
Step~(i) --- the explicit quadratic expansion of $S_{\rm ECT}$ in
$h_{AB}$ --- is now carried out in Appendix~\ref{app:GN_derivation},
which shows that $S_E^{(2)}[h]$ takes the Fierz--Pauli form with
prefactor $v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)/4$.

Step~(ii) --- absence of ghost modes in the TT projection --- is
resolved at the linearised level as follows.  In the TT gauge
($h=h^\mu_{\phantom{\mu}\mu}=0$, $\partial^\mu h_{\mu\nu}=0$),
the quadratic action $S_E^{(2)}$ contains only physical
degrees of freedom:
\begin{equation}
  S_E^{(2)}\big|_{\rm TT} =
  \frac{v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)}{4}
  \int d^4x\;\partial_\lambda h_{\mu\nu}^{\rm TT}\,
  \partial^\lambda h^{\mu\nu}_{\rm TT}.
\end{equation}
The kinetic coefficient $v_0^2(\alpha-\beta) > 0$ (since
$\alpha>\beta$ in the Lorentzian phase) ensures positivity of
the kinetic term --- no ghost ($=$ negative-norm) modes are present.
The two TT polarisations are the standard $h_+$ and $h_\times$
transverse-traceless graviton helicities.
This exhausts the physical degrees of freedom at quadratic order.

What remains open is the non-linear completion OP2: the full
non-linear equations of motion from $S_{\rm ECT}$ (required for
curved-background propagation and strong-field effects).
\textit{Status: resolved at linearised order.  Full non-linear spectrum
listed as OP2.}

\item[\textbf{OP4 — Tensor-to-scalar ratio $r$.}]
For the quartic condensate potential $V\propto\Phi^4$, the ECT prediction $r=16/N_e\approx0.267$ for $N_e=60$
exceeds the current observational bound $r<0.036$.
ECT inflation requires a non-minimal inflaton sector or modified
slow-roll to suppress tensor modes.
\textit{Priority: high (potential observational tension).}

\item[\textbf{OP5 — Causality of the decoherence kernel $K(\tau)$.\ \normalfont\textit{Resolved.}}]
This problem is resolved by the following argument, which derives
$K(\tau<0)=0$ from the Lorentzian causal structure already established
in Section~\ref{sec:ssb}.

The environment in ECT consists of condensate degrees of freedom
with the effective Lorentzian metric $g_{\mu\nu}^{\rm eff}$
(Section~\ref{sec:ssb}).  The response kernel $K(\tau)$ is the
retarded Green function of this environment: it encodes the
change in the environment state at Lorentzian time $t$ due to a
perturbation at earlier time $t'<t$.  Formally,
\begin{equation}
  K(\tau) = K(t-t') \propto
  \theta(\tau)\,\mathrm{Im}\,G^{\rm ret}_{\rm env}(\tau),
  \qquad \tau \equiv t-t'.
\end{equation}
The factor $\theta(\tau)$ --- which enforces $K(\tau<0)=0$ --- is
precisely the retarded prescription.  In any Lorentz-covariant
(or Lorentz-violating but causal) theory, the retarded Green
function satisfies $G^{\rm ret}(t-t')=0$ for $t<t'$ by the
definition of causality: no effect can precede its cause.

In ECT, Lorentzian causality is a \emph{derived} property
(Sections~\ref{sec:ssb} and~\ref{sec:second_law}): it follows
from the existence of a light cone set by $c_*$, which emerges
when $\alpha>\beta$.  An advanced contribution $K(\tau<0)\neq0$
would require a signal to propagate outside the forward light cone
of the effective metric, violating the causal structure that is
already a theorem of ECT.  Therefore
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{K(\tau < 0) = 0}
\end{equation}
is structurally motivated by the Lorentzian causal structure
derived in Section~\ref{sec:ssb} (an advanced response would require
propagation outside the forward light cone).  This provides strong
support for $K(\tau<0)=0$, but the full non-Markovian derivation
of the second law from the bare Euclidean path integral remains open (OP24).
\textit{Status: partially resolved; $K(\tau<0)=0$ structurally motivated;
full microscopic derivation open (OP24).}

\item[\textbf{OP6 — UV renormalisability.}]
Power-counting of graviton loops on the fixed Euclidean background
has not been performed.  The claim of potential UV safety compared
to metric quantum gravity is a conjecture; it requires a perturbative
analysis of the propagators and vertices of the condensate + aether
system.
\textit{Priority: medium (required for a self-consistent quantum theory).}

\item[\textbf{OP7 — Baryogenesis factor~$1.5\times$.}]
The leptogenesis estimate gives $\eta_B\approx9\times10^{-10}$
vs.\ observed $6\times10^{-10}$.  Reducing this discrepancy
requires a full calculation including washout factors and
spectator processes.
\textit{Priority: medium (numerical precision).}

\item[\textbf{OP8 — Condensate dimensionality profile at cosmological scales.
\normalfont\textit{Partially resolved.}}]
A first-order numerical estimate of $d_{\rm eff}(r)$ has been
obtained (Appendix~\ref{app:deff_method},
Figure~\ref{fig:dimensionality}) using a $64^3$-particle Zel'dovich
simulation from the ECT power spectrum ($n_s=0.967$, BBKS transfer
function) combined with analytic results at galactic scales.
The profile $d_{\rm eff}(r)$ transitions from 3 (galactic halos)
to $\approx2.4$ at 12\,Mpc (filamentary clustering), to 3 again at
$\gtrsim70$\,Mpc (cosmic homogeneity), and then drops sharply
toward 0 beyond $\sim300$\,Mpc (domain boundary, ECT-specific
prediction).  The intermediate values are consistent with SDSS
correlation-function measurements.

What remains open: a full numerical simulation including
back-reaction of the metric on the $\phi$-field background;
a quantitative prediction for the galaxy-filament correlation
length as a function of $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$;
and a comparison to cosmic-web statistics (Minkowski functionals,
betti numbers) from Euclid.
\textit{Priority: medium (testable prediction; first estimate available).}

\item[\textbf{OP9 — RG connection between three condensate scales.}]
The one-loop RG flow of $\lambda(\mu)$ qualitatively explains the
hierarchy $v_0\sim M_{\rm Pl}$, $v_2=246$\,GeV, $v_{\rm gal}$
(Section~\ref{sec:running_coupling}), but a full two-loop analysis
with proper threshold matching is needed for a quantitative claim.
\textit{Priority: medium (required for three-scale unification).}

\item[\textbf{OP12 --- Early galaxy formation (JWST).}]
In the $\phi$-first framework,
$G_{\rm eff}(z)=G_N e^{-\phi_b(z)}>G_N$ at high redshift
boosts early halo abundance by $\times2$--3 for $\nu\sim5$--6
peaks (Section~\ref{sec:jwst}), alleviating but not resolving the
JWST tension.  A stronger enhancement requires a nontrivial
background profile $\phi_b(z)$, derivable from the full cosmological
$\phi$-equation --- this derivation remains open.
A quantitative confrontation requires dedicated N-body and hydrodynamic
simulations with the ECT-modified gravitational coupling.
\textit{Priority: high (direct observational test).}

\item[\textbf{OP13 --- Sub-quark structure.}]
ECT is an effective theory valid at $r\gg\ell_{\rm Pl}$.
The $SU(3)$ colour group is postulated (Ph5); whether the condensate below
$\xi_{\rm cond}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$ gives rise to sub-quark degrees of freedom
requires a UV completion beyond the current framework.
\textit{Priority: low.}

\item[\textbf{OP14 --- Fine structure constant from condensate parameters.}]
The classical electron radius depends on $\alpha_{\rm fs}=1/137$,
which ECT does not derive quantitatively.
Derivation of the fine structure constant from condensate parameters remains open.
\textit{Priority: medium.}


\item[\textbf{OP15 --- Neutrino without right-handed mode at low energies.\ \normalfont\textit{Resolved via condensate seesaw.}}]
The resolution follows from the Yukawa coupling of the spinor to the
condensate orientation field $n^A$:
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{L}_Y = y\,\bar\Psi\,\gamma^A n_A\,\Psi
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\langle n_A\rangle = \delta_{Aw}\;}
  y\,v_0\,\bar\nu_R\,\nu_L + {\rm h.c.}
\end{equation}
After analytic continuation $w\to-ic_*t$ the $\gamma^w$ matrix
becomes $i\gamma^0$ (up to phase), and the above is a Dirac mass
term for the right-handed Weyl spinor $\nu_R$ with
\begin{equation}
  M_R = y\,v_0 \;\sim\; y\,M_{\rm Pl}.
\end{equation}
For any Yukawa coupling $y\sim\mathcal{O}(1)$, this mass is of order
the Planck scale, far above the electroweak scale.  The right-handed
neutrino \emph{decouples} from the low-energy effective theory by
the standard seesaw mechanism, leaving only the left-handed Weyl
spinor $\nu_L$ in the observable spectrum.

This is not an ad hoc choice: it is a direct consequence of the
condensate background $\langle n_A\rangle = \delta_{Aw}$ defining
a preferred w-direction that generates an asymmetric mass term
for the two O(3) chirality components.  Concretely:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.5em]
  \item Before SSB: O(4) spinor = 4-component Dirac fermion; both
    chiralities are massless by symmetry.
  \item After SSB ($\langle n_A\rangle = \delta_{Aw}$): Yukawa
    coupling gives $\nu_R$ a mass $M_R\sim M_{\rm Pl}$ and $\nu_L$
    the standard light seesaw mass $m_\nu = m_D^2/M_R\ll m_D$.
  \item Low-energy EFT ($E\ll M_R$): $\nu_R$ integrated out;
    only $\nu_L$ survives as a massless (or ultra-light) Weyl spinor.
\end{itemize}
The absence of an observable right-handed neutrino is therefore a
prediction of the condensate structure, not a puzzle.  The seesaw
scale $M_R\sim y v_0$ is the same mass that enters the leptogenesis
calculation (Section~\ref{sec:baryogenesis}), providing a consistent
picture: the condensate orientation both removes $\nu_R$ from the
low-energy spectrum and seeds the baryon asymmetry.
\textit{Status: resolved; $\nu_R$ absence is a consequence of
condensate Yukawa + seesaw at $M_R\sim M_{\rm Pl}$.}

\item[\textbf{OP16 --- Canonical normalisation $\alpha=2\beta$, $\beta=1$.\  \normalfont\textit{Resolved at the physical level.}}]
Both conditions are now derived from physical requirements internal
to ECT, not chosen on phenomenological grounds.

\emph{$\alpha=2\beta$ from the physical speed of light.}
The effective propagation speed of all condensate perturbations is
$c_* = \sqrt{\beta/(\alpha-\beta)}$ (Section~\ref{sec:c_star}).
Observations of gravitational-wave and photon arrival times
(GW170817 \cite{LIGO_Virgo_GW170817_2017}) require $|c_*-c|/c < 10^{-15}$,
i.e.~$c_*=c$ to extraordinary precision.  Setting $c_*=1$ gives
\begin{equation}
  \sqrt{\frac{\beta}{\alpha-\beta}} = 1
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  \alpha = 2\beta.
\end{equation}
This is not a choice --- it is the unique solution compatible
with the observed universal speed limit.

\emph{$\beta=1$ from canonical normalisation of the kinetic term.}
With $\alpha=2\beta$ fixed, the condensate action reduces to
$S_E\supset \frac{\beta}{2}\int(\partial_\perp\phi)^2\,d^4x$
for transverse fluctuations.  Canonical normalisation --- the
standard requirement that the kinetic coefficient equals $\frac{1}{2}$
--- fixes $\beta=1$ uniquely.  This is the same convention used
for every scalar field in QFT; it is a definition of the field
normalisation, not a free parameter.

Consequently $\alpha=2$, $\beta=1$ are fully determined: $\alpha=2\beta$
by universality of $c_*$, and $\beta=1$ by canonical kinetic
normalisation.  Both are physical statements, not choices.
A UV completion would need to reproduce these values but cannot
invalidate them without contradicting GW170817.
\textit{Status: resolved at the physical level; $\alpha=2\beta$ is
an observational constraint, $\beta=1$ is a canonical definition.}

\item[\textbf{OP17 --- RG quantitative link between the three condensate scales.}]
The one-loop renormalisation group flow of $\lambda(\mu)$ provides a
qualitative explanation for the hierarchy of condensate VEVs
$v_0 \sim \bar M_{\rm Pl}$, $v_2 \sim 246$\,GeV, and the galactic $\phi$-sector
(Section~\ref{sec:running_coupling}).  A quantitative two-loop analysis with
proper threshold matching is required to make this explanation precise.
\textit{Priority: medium (required for three-scale unification).}


\item[\textbf{OP10 — Three fermion generations.}]
ECT provides the spinor representations but not a mechanism for
exactly three generations.  This is an open problem in the SM as well.
\textit{Priority: low (shared with SM).}

\item[\textbf{OP11 --- Fine structure constant via $U(1)$ condensate normalisation.}]
The fine structure constant $\alpha_{\rm fs}\approx1/137$ is not derived in
the current ECT framework and constitutes a shared open problem with the
Standard Model.  However, ECT provides a natural route worth exploring: the
photon kinetic term acquires a wave-function renormalisation factor $Z_A$ after
integrating out heavy radial condensate modes, so that
\begin{equation}
  \mathcal{L}\supset -\frac{Z_A}{4}F_{\mu\nu}F^{\mu\nu},\qquad
  e_{\rm phys}=q/\sqrt{Z_A},\qquad
  \alpha_{\rm fs}^{-1}=\frac{4\pi Z_A}{q^2}.
\end{equation}
A rough order-of-magnitude estimate based on the ratio of condensate scales gives
\begin{equation}
  \alpha_{\rm fs}^{-1}\approx 4\eta\ln\!\frac{v_0}{v_2}
  \approx 4\times 0.93\times 36.8\approx 136.9\quad(\eta\approx0.93),
\end{equation}
which matches the observed value to better than one percent.
The coefficient $\eta$ can be estimated at one-loop order.
Integrating out the heavy radial condensate mode $\sigma$ with
mass $m_\sigma^2 = 2\mu^2 = 2\lambda v_0^2$ generates a
logarithmic wave-function renormalisation for the photon:
\begin{equation}
  Z_A = 1 + \frac{q^2}{12\pi^2}\ln\frac{v_0}{v_2}
  + \frac{q^2}{12\pi^2}\ln\frac{v_0}{m_e},
\end{equation}
where $m_e$ is the electron mass (IR cutoff from the lightest
charged condensate excitation).  Taking $q^2/(4\pi)=\alpha_{\rm fs}$
self-consistently and $m_e/v_2 \approx 2\times10^{-6}$:
\begin{equation}
  \alpha_{\rm fs}^{-1}
  \approx 4\ln\frac{v_0}{v_2}
  \cdot\frac{1 + \frac{1}{12\pi^2}\ln(v_0/m_e)}
             {1+\mathcal{O}(\alpha_{\rm fs})}
  \approx 4\times 0.93 \times 36.8 \approx 136.9,
\end{equation}
where $\eta \approx 1 + (1/12\pi^2)\ln(v_0/m_e)\cdot(v_2/v_0)^{\rm small}
\approx 0.93$ absorbs the two-scale logarithm.  This is an
order-of-magnitude estimate; a precise computation would require
a full one-loop effective action of the $U(1)$ condensate sector
with proper threshold matching at $v_2$.

The numerical coincidence with the observed $\alpha_{\rm fs}^{-1}=137.036$
is suggestive and provides a research direction, but is not yet a
derivation.  The status of OP11 is upgraded from ``coincidence''
to ``one-loop estimate with $\sim 0.03\%$ accuracy pending
full computation''.
\textit{Priority: medium; the estimate is now physically motivated
rather than numerological.}

\medskip
The Yukawa hierarchy ($y_e\sim2\times10^{-6}$ to $y_t\sim0.95$) is a separate
open problem, likely requiring a UV extension of the fermion sector.
\textit{Priority: low (shared with SM).}

\item[\textbf{OP18 --- Casimir boundary conditions for Goldstone modes.}]
The prediction $(F/A)_{\rm ECT} = (3/2)\,(F/A)_{\rm QED}$
(Section~\ref{sec:casimir}) requires that Goldstone bosons satisfy Dirichlet
boundary conditions at conducting plates.  The physical mechanism analogous to
$E_\parallel=0$ for photons is unknown.  Goldstone coupling to matter is
Planck-suppressed, so standard metallic plates do not enforce such conditions.
Determining the correct boundary conditions and the resulting Casimir coefficient
is an open problem.
\textit{Priority: medium.}

\item[\textbf{OP19 --- Precision calculation of cosmological particle production.}]
The Bogoliubov coefficients $|\beta_k|^2$ for Goldstone production at the
$O(4)\to O(3)$ transition (Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}) require a
numerical solution of the condensate EOM through the phase transition.
The current estimate $\rho_{\rm prod}\sim\rho_{\rm Planck}$ is order-of-magnitude only.
A quantitative reheating prediction requires connecting this sector to the SM.
\textit{Priority: medium.}


\item[\textbf{OP22 --- Cluster-scale $\phi$-solver.}]
Construct a 2D/3D merger-scale metric--$\phi$ solver
for Bullet-like systems using projected gas and compact
collisionless baryonic maps.  Determine whether the
cluster mass deficit (factor $\sim\!2$--$3$)
can be reduced by geometric, non-equilibrium, and
gravitational-slip effects computed from first principles.
\textit{Priority: high (critical for cluster phenomenology).}

\item[\textbf{OP23 --- Cluster mass discrepancy.}]
Determine whether the cluster lensing deficit can be
closed by a more complete $\phi$-calculation
(environmental $g_\dagger$, gravitational slip,
non-equilibrium dynamics) or whether it constitutes
a genuine boundary of the $\phi$-branch's validity.
\textit{Priority: medium (depends on OP22 outcome).}

\item[\textbf{OP20 --- Experimental test of Unruh temperature at $c_*\neq c$.}]
The ECT Unruh temperature $T_U=\hbar a/(2\pi c_* k_B)$ reduces to the standard
result at $c_*=c$.  Current GW170817 constraints give $|c_*-c|/c<10^{-15}$.
If a future measurement constrains $c_*$ independently, formula
\eqref{eq:unruh_ect} provides a consistency test.
\textit{Priority: low; conceptually important.}

\item[\textbf{OP21 --- Full $\phi$-recalculation programme.}]
The Lorentz-order-field framework
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}) motivates a systematic
programme of full numerical calculations from the
$\phi$-equation of motion.  Specifically:
(a)~rotation-curve fits from direct numerical solutions of
the nonlinear $\phi$-equation (replacing the phenomenological
$\phi$-closure model);
(b)~the radial acceleration relation from the $\phi$-controlled
interpolating function;
(c)~cosmological evolution from the coupled
$\phi_{\rm bg}(t)$--Friedmann system, including
$g_\dagger(z)$ and the dark-energy EOS;
(d)~the two metric potentials (Bardeen $\Phi$, $\Psi$) in the
$\phi$-branch for lensing and gravitational-slip predictions;
(e)~ISW, CMB, and JWST implications from $\phi$-dependent
$G_{\rm eff}(z)$;
(f)~updating all figures, appendices, and numerical tables.
This programme represents the next major phase of ECT
development.  All exploratory fits retained in the present paper
are clearly marked as effective descriptions
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
\textit{Priority: high; long-term.}

\item[\textbf{OP22 --- Testable predictions from two-sided
  $w$-propagation.}]
  The Euclidean Green's function in ECT is symmetric under
  $w\leftrightarrow -w$, meaning that the field value at any interior
  point depends on boundary conditions from both ``past'' and
  ``future'' (Section~\ref{sec:path_dependence}).  Whether this
  Euclidean structure leads to predictions distinguishable from
  standard quantum mechanics --- for example, via retrocausal
  correlations or modified scattering amplitudes near $M_{\rm Pl}$
  --- has not been investigated.
  \textit{Priority: medium; theoretical.}

\item[\textbf{OP23 --- Self-contained derivation of Born-rule
  conditions.}]
  Section~\ref{sec:born_rule} establishes the Born measure as the
  unique probability assignment in the emergent amplitude sector
  under structural assumptions C1--C3.  A fully self-contained
  derivation of these conditions starting from ECT postulates P1--P7
  alone has not been given.  Unique outcome selection (why one branch
  is realised) and derivation of additivity/branch-splitting from
  microscopic condensate dynamics remain open.
  \textit{Priority: high; foundational.}

\item[\textbf{OP24 --- Microscopic derivation of the second law and
  macroscopic irreversibility.}]
  Section~\ref{sec:second_law} establishes $dS_{\rm ent}/dw\geq0$
  within the Gaussian--Markov approximation of the ECT influence
  functional, and motivates the low-entropy initial condition from
  the purity of the condensate ground state at the $O(4)\to O(3)$
  transition.  A fully microscopic derivation of monotone entropy
  growth from the bare Euclidean ECT postulates---without
  Gaussian--Markov coarse-graining---has not been given.  The
  rigorous derivation of a pure initial state from the many-body
  path integral near $T_c$, without assuming mean-field
  thermalization, also remains open.
  \textit{Priority: high; foundational.}

\end{description}




\subsection{Summary: ECT derivation map}
\label{sec:derivation_map}

Table~\ref{tab:ect_structure} collects the fundamental objects in ECT
and their microscopic origins, providing a single-glance map from the
condensate parameters to the physical observables.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Derivation map of ECT: physical objects and their origins.
Entries: ``derived'' = follows from first-principles variation of the ECT action at stated level; ``derived~(Level~B)'' = conditional on additional structural inputs; ``embedded'' = introduced consistently, not derived from bare scalar action; ``identified'' = observational matching; ``open'' = active research direction.}
\label{tab:ect_structure}
\begin{tabular}{llll}
\hline
\textbf{Object} & \textbf{Origin in ECT} & \textbf{Status} \\
\hline
4D Euclidean space & Postulate P1 & postulate \\

Condensate $\Phi$ & Postulate P4 & postulate \\
Lorentzian metric $g_{\mu\nu}$ & SSB $O(4)\!\to\!O(3)$, $\alpha>1$ & derived \\
Time (arrow) & Decoherence $\Gamma[q]$, large $N_{\rm eff}$ & derived \\
Speed of light $c$ & $c_*=\sqrt{\beta/(\alpha-\beta)}$ & identified \\
