\bigskip
\noindent
\textbf{Transition to Part~IV.}
Parts~I--III have developed the full ECT framework from postulates to
predictions.  Part~I established the foundational results: Lorentzian geometry,
quantum mechanics, fundamental constants, gravity, and a structural
account of gauge and particle sectors---all rooted in a single
Euclidean condensate action, at varying levels of rigour.
Part~II demonstrated the macroscopic observational reach: galactic
dynamics, rotation curves, cosmology.  Part~III explored the deeper
quantum structural results: emergent principles of physics, the unified
correlator for quantum vacuum phenomena, and the black-hole sector.

Part~IV collects the overall picture.  Section~\ref{sec:discussion}
discusses the conceptual interpretation and limitations of the framework.
Section~\ref{sec:predictions} tabulates all quantitative predictions
and experimental tests, organised by observational domain.
Section~\ref{sec:comparison} places ECT in the context of existing
approaches (Einstein-aether theory, Hořava--Lifshitz gravity,
analogue gravity, causal dynamical triangulations, Barbour's
relational mechanics).  Section~\ref{sec:open_problems} states the
open problems precisely.  Section~\ref{sec:conclusion} provides
the closing summary.

%==============================================================
\part{Summary, Comparisons, and Outlook}
\label{part:summary}
%==============================================================

\section{Discussion}
\label{sec:discussion}

We now discuss the conceptual interpretation, limitations,
and future directions of the ECT framework.

\subsection{Conceptual interpretation of the framework}

ECT proposes that Lorentzian spacetime, quantum dynamics, and
gravitational interactions can all be obtained from a single
underlying structure: a scalar condensate in four-dimensional
Euclidean space with spontaneously broken $O(4)$ symmetry.
This is a working hypothesis supported by the results presented
here at varying levels of rigour, as classified in
Table~\ref{tab:ect-levels}.

This perspective inverts the conventional logic of quantum gravity.
Rather than attempting to quantise an existing spacetime geometry, ECT
starts from a fundamentally Euclidean arena where no distinction
between space and time exists, and recovers the Lorentzian structure
as an effective property of the symmetry-broken vacuum.  The
Lorentzian metric, the causal cone, and the arrow of time all arise
from the same condensate background that provides a common
parameter-matching framework for $G_N$, $\hbar$, and $c_*$
(internal consistency relations; non-circular derivation open, OP-$\Lambda$).

This framework should not be interpreted as claiming that time is
``unreal''.  Rather, it suggests that the distinction between temporal
and spatial coordinates---encoded in the metric signature---is a
collective, emergent property of the vacuum state, much as superfluidity
is a collective property of helium-4 below the $\lambda$-point.

\subsection{Emergence of physical frameworks from the condensate}
\label{subsec:emergence_chains}

A key claim of ECT is that several independently postulated
frameworks of physics \emph{emerge} as limiting cases or
sectors of a single condensate structure, rather than merely
being ``bridged'' by it.  We make this claim precise below,
distinguishing strict derivations from accommodations.

\paragraph{General Relativity.}
The linearised Einstein equations are \emph{derived} by
varying the ECT action with respect to the effective metric
(Section~\ref{sec:macroscopic}, Appendix~\ref{app:curvature_coupling}).
The nonlinear completion, including the anisotropic curvature
term, follows from a Riemann-commutator identity.
GR emerges as the deeply-Lorentzian, screened branch of the
$\phi$-dynamics: where the vacuum is strongly ordered
($\phi \gg 0$, dense environments), the order-field sector
freezes out, and the standard Einstein equations hold.
\emph{Status: Level~A (linearised); Level~A (nonlinear
anisotropic completion); the full nonminimal scalar--tensor
sector is Level~B (EFT-supported).}

\paragraph{Quantum mechanics.}
The Schr\"odinger equation is derived by analytic
continuation $w \to -ic_* t$ of the condensate equation of
motion (Section~\ref{sec:quantum}).  The uncertainty principle
follows from the Parseval inequality on minimal
loop configurations.  The Planck constant $\hbar$ is
identified with the minimal loop action $S_{\rm loop,min}$.
Quantum decoherence (the transition from quantum to classical)
follows from the growth of the decoherence functional
$\Gamma_{\rm irr}$ (effective irreversibility functional)
with the number of environmental modes (Gaussian--Markov model, Level~B).
\emph{Status: Level~A (Schr\"odinger eq.\ and CCR);
Level~A (uncertainty principle as Cauchy--Schwarz);
Level~B (decoherence structure; irreversibility is effective,
Gaussian--Markov, OP24).}

\paragraph{Thermodynamics and the arrow of time.}
An effective second law $dS_{\rm ent}/dw \geq 0$ follows for
macroscopic systems with $N_{\rm eff} \gg 1$
within the Gaussian--Markov reduction of the influence functional
(Section~\ref{sec:second_law}).  The arrow of time is not
postulated but emerges from the directionality of $\Gamma_{\rm irr}$
in the condensate background.
\emph{Status: effective (Level~B, Gaussian--Markov); full microscopic
derivation open (OP24).}

\paragraph{MOND-like dynamics.}
The baryonic Tully--Fisher relation and flat rotation curves
emerge from the critical infrared branch of the
Lorentz-order field $\phi$ in dilute environments
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).  MOND is
recovered as an excellent approximation to this branch
when $\phi_{\rm gal}$ is near-universal; ECT predicts
corrections where the ambient Lorentz-order departs
from the cosmological mean.
\emph{Status: Level~B (critical-branch hypothesis
with strong EFT support).}

\paragraph{Gauge interactions.}
$U(1)$ electrodynamics emerges from the phase symmetry
of the condensate field $\theta$.  $SU(2)_L$ is derived
from the internal structure of the condensate doublet.
$SU(3)$ is currently \emph{embedded} (accommodated),
not derived.
\emph{Status: $U(1)$, $SU(2)$~--- Level~B;
$SU(3)$~--- Level~C (open).}

\paragraph{Cosmology.}
Inflation is identified with the condensate
formation epoch ($O(4) \to O(3)$).  Dark energy is the
residual vacuum energy of the condensate potential.
The Hubble tension may be partially addressed by a
running $G_{\rm eff}(z)$ through the cosmological
Lorentz-order background $\phi_{\rm bg}(t)$.
\emph{Status: Level~B (inflation mechanism);
Level~B (dark energy); Level~C ($\phi$-cosmology).}

\medskip
The central point is that GR and quantum mechanics do not
require separate postulational bases in ECT: both emerge
from the \emph{same} condensate action, with GR governing
the macroscopic metric sector and QM governing the
microscopic loop sector.  The $\phi$-field then provides a
\emph{third} layer --- a vacuum-order variable that
organises the effective regime (quantum, Newtonian, or
MOND-like) according to the local degree of Lorentzian
ordering of the vacuum.

\subsection{Limitations of the present formulation}

Several important limitations should be noted.

(i)~The Standard Model gauge group $SU(3) \times SU(2) \times U(1)$ is
embedded within the condensate structure but not derived from it.
The colour group $SU(3)$ has no identified origin in the $O(4)$
breaking pattern.

(ii)~The galactic weak-field sector is currently implemented
through an exploratory algebraic closure of the Lorentz-order
field $\phi$, not yet through a full boundary-value solution
of the $\phi$-equation.  The deep-IR critical form
$\mathcal{F} \propto Y_\phi^{3/2}$ is a hypothesis motivated
by 3D scale invariance, not yet a full nonperturbative
derivation.  The present closure captures the screened and
deep-critical asymptotics but does not yet reproduce the
full inner morphology of all observed rotation curves.

(iii)~The critical acceleration scale $g_\dagger$ is not
treated as a universal fundamental constant in ECT.
In the current implementation it is controlled by the
ambient Lorentz-order background $\phi_{\rm env}$.
The observed galaxy-to-galaxy scatter should therefore be
interpreted as part of the physics to be explained, not
as a failure of universality.

(iv)~Three fermion generations, the Yukawa coupling hierarchy, and
the fine structure constant $\alpha_{\rm fs} = 1/137$ are not
explained.

(v)~A rigorous power-counting analysis of graviton loops on the
Euclidean background has not been performed; the claim of potential
UV safety remains a conjecture.

(vi)~The derivation of thermodynamic irreversibility required a
causal response kernel $K(\tau < 0) = 0$, which is structurally motivated
by the Lorentzian causal structure of ECT (Section~\ref{sec:second_law}).
The effective second law holds within the Gaussian--Markov approximation;
a full microscopic derivation remains open (OP24).

\subsection{Future directions}

The most important open problems for future work include:

(i)~Replacing the algebraic $\phi$-closure model by a full
spherical boundary-value solver for $\phi(r)$, with explicit
environmental boundary conditions, realistic baryonic
components (including SPARC gas profiles), and eventually
full axisymmetric disk geometry.

(ii)~A full two-loop RG analysis connecting the condensate
scales ($v_0 \sim M_{\rm Pl}$, $v_2 = 246$~GeV, galactic
$\phi$-sector) through the running of $\lambda(\mu)$.

(iii)~Numerical simulations of condensate evolution during cosmological
phase transitions, including predictions for the primordial power
spectrum beyond the slow-roll approximation.

(iv)~A systematic comparison of ECT predictions with the full SPARC
database (175 galaxies), including the $\phi_{\rm env}$--environment
correlation test.

(v)~Derivation of the Standard Model gauge structure from the internal
symmetries of the condensate, rather than embedding it by hand.

\paragraph{The Great Attractor and large-scale flows.}
The Great Attractor region (distance $\sim 60\,$Mpc,
peculiar velocity $\sim 600\,$km\,s$^{-1}$) is a
large-scale gravitational anomaly usually attributed to a
dark-matter overdensity.  In the $\phi$-framework, an
overdense supercluster region has high $\phi_{\rm env}$
(deeply Lorentzian, screened), but the surrounding
intermediate-density regions through which infalling
galaxies move have \emph{lower} $\phi_{\rm env}$ and
therefore enhanced $G_{\rm eff}$.  This amplification of
the apparent gravitational pull from the transition zone
could contribute to the observed infall pattern without
requiring a dark-matter halo as massive as the $\Lambda$CDM
estimate.  A quantitative prediction requires solving the
$\phi$-equation on Mpc scales, which is part of the
full recalculation programme (OP21).

(v)~Derivation of the Standard Model gauge structure from the internal
symmetries of the condensate, rather than embedding it by hand.

(vi)~Exploration of whether additional fundamental constants
(Boltzmann constant, fine structure constant) can be related to
condensate parameters.

\paragraph{The Lorentz-order field as an organising principle.}
A recurring theme of the present work is that the
Lorentz-order field $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$
provides a single variable that organises multiple
aspects of the theory:
the effective gravitational regime (Newtonian, MOND-like,
or quantum/Planckian) is controlled by the local value and
gradient of $\phi$;
screening in dense environments, the BTFR, environmental
modulation of $g_\dagger$, and the cosmological acceleration
scale all follow from the $\phi$-dynamics;
the transition between GR and modified gravity is not
merely a matter of curvature or distance but of the local
degree of Lorentzian ordering of the vacuum.
A central next step is to promote the galactic order field
to a cosmological background $\phi_{\rm bg}(t)$ plus
inhomogeneous perturbations, unifying late-time acceleration,
the redshift evolution of $g_\dagger$, lensing and
gravitational slip, and galactic dynamics within one
vacuum-order framework (OP-new-4, OP21).

\paragraph{Gauge interactions and the vacuum-order hierarchy.}
At present the Lorentz-order field should not be interpreted
as a derivation of the electromagnetic, weak, or strong
interactions: these emerge from the phase symmetries of the
condensate (Section~\ref{sec:gauge}), not from $\phi$.
However, $\phi$ may play an indirect role: as the order
parameter controlling the macroscopic phase of the vacuum,
it may determine \emph{in which regime} certain effective
low-energy sectors are realised.  A deeper question for
future work is whether the emergence of gauge sectors can
also be organised relative to this vacuum-order hierarchy.

\paragraph{The cleanest tests.}
The most informative empirical tests of the
Lorentz-order-field mechanism are expected not in the
highest-mass systems, but in the most weakly screened
low-density environments---void dwarfs, diffuse groups,
outer disks---where the vacuum sits closest to the critical
Lorentzian boundary.  Environment-dependent transition
morphologies (the detailed shape of the Newtonian-to-MOND
transition, not just the asymptotic $g_\dagger$) may provide
a further high-quality diagnostic.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Conclusion}
\label{sec:conclusion}

\paragraph{Overview of the framework.}

In this work we have developed the Euclidean Condensate Theory (ECT), in
which spacetime and gravitational dynamics arise from a condensate
structure of the vacuum.
The complete theoretical identity of the framework is captured by four
fundamental laws (Section~\ref{sec:laws_ect}) and six signature
equations (Section~\ref{sec:signature_eqs}).  The derivational chain
running from the postulates to the observational predictions is
summarised in Table~\ref{tab:ect_structure} (Section~\ref{sec:derivation_map}).
All phenomenological inputs are listed explicitly in
Section~\ref{sec:ssb}. Starting from a small set of basic principles
— Euclidean symmetry, spontaneous symmetry breaking, and condensate
dynamics — we have shown how several key elements of relativistic and
quantum physics can emerge within a unified framework.

The central hypothesis is that the vacuum corresponds to a condensate
field possessing an underlying $O(4)$ symmetry. A spontaneous symmetry
breaking

\[
O(4)\rightarrow O(3)
\]

selects a preferred direction which appears as the time dimension of the
emergent spacetime. Perturbations propagating in this condensate
experience an effective Lorentzian geometry while the microscopic
description remains fundamentally Euclidean.

Within this framework several fundamental physical constants acquire
candidate physical interpretations as consistency relations among
condensate parameters (not independent first-principles derivations).
The speed of light is identified with the propagation velocity of
low-energy condensate perturbations.
The gravitational constant is expressed in terms of the condensate
amplitude and the canonical normalisation parameters.
The Planck constant is identified with the minimal action of a closed
condensate loop (self-consistency relation; OP-$\Lambda$).

\paragraph{Quantum vacuum structure.}

A distinctive feature of ECT, developed in Section~\ref{sec:quantum_vacuum},
is that three quantum vacuum phenomena --- the conditional Goldstone-sector
Casimir-type vacuum shift, the Unruh temperature, and cosmological particle
production --- are all controlled
by related limits of the condensate two-point function
$G_E=(4\pi^2|X-X'|^2)^{-1}$ (organizing proposition;
each effect still requires its own boundary, detector, or
coarse-graining specification).
The Casimir pressure ratio $3/2$ is derived for condensate-reflecting
boundaries (\emph{not} predicted for standard metallic plates;
see Section~\ref{sec:casimir}).
The Unruh temperature $T_U=\hbar a/(2\pi c_* k_B)$ is derived by
continuing the $O(4)$-invariant correlator onto the Rindler trajectory.
Cosmological particle production at the $O(4)\to O(3)$ transition yields
spectral index $n_s=1-2/N_e=0.967$, matching the Planck 2018 value.

\paragraph{Observational validation.}

The galactic weak-field sector of ECT is now interpreted through
the nonlinear response of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$, not
through a kpc-scale variation of the heavy condensate amplitude.
In the present version this response is modelled by an exploratory
algebraic closure parameterised by the ambient background
$\phi_{\rm env}$, which sets the critical acceleration scale
$g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$.

Within this framework, flat rotation curves, the RAR, and the
BTFR are interpreted as manifestations of a critical $\phi$-branch
rather than as evidence for particle dark matter.  The present
exploratory fits to five SPARC galaxies and the Milky Way yield
$\chi^2/N$ values comparable to MOND (with free
$\Upsilon_\star$, one parameter each) and competitive with
$\Lambda$CDM/NFW (two halo parameters).  The key physical
observation is that the fitted $\phi_{\rm env}$ values
correlate with independently expected environmental density
(void galaxies have lower $\phi_{\rm env}$, group galaxies
higher), consistent with the theoretical prediction.
These comparisons should be viewed as proof-of-principle
tests of the $\phi$-framework rather than as final
self-consistent field solutions.

\paragraph{Emergent galactic acceleration scale.}

A central result is that the theory \emph{admits} a
characteristic acceleration scale $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$
controlled by the ambient Lorentz-order background.
This scale is not imposed as a universal constant
(as in MOND) but depends on environment through
$g_\dagger = g_{\dagger 0}\,e^{\gamma\phi_{\rm env}}$.
Observationally, $g_\dagger \approx 10^{-10}\,$m\,s$^{-2}$
governs the RAR, BTFR, and the flattening of rotation curves.

These phenomena all follow from the nonlinear response of the
Lorentz-order field $\phi$ in the critical weak-field branch,
without requiring particle dark matter.

An important aspect is that $g_\dagger$ was not
imposed by construction but emerges from the condensate
structure of the vacuum.  The characteristic galactic acceleration
scale arises as a secondary consequence of this framework. The agreement
between the predicted and observed magnitude of $g_\dagger$ therefore
provides a nontrivial consistency test of the theory.


\paragraph{Universal near-horizon critical scale.}

A noteworthy structural prediction of the ECT black-hole sector is
the universal proper-distance scale
\begin{equation}
\rho_c
\;=\;
\frac{\ell_{\rm Pl}}{\sqrt{3\pi}}
\;\approx\;
0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}
\;\approx\;
5.3\times10^{-36}\,\text{m},
\label{eq:rho_c_conclusion}
\end{equation}
at which the local Tolman temperature $T_{\rm loc}(\rho) = \hbar c/(2\pi k_B\rho)$
reaches the condensate critical temperature $T_c = v_0\sqrt{6}$.
The result is \emph{parameter-free} once $T_c$ is identified with the
Dolan--Jackiw thermal mass of the condensate: no free parameters are
adjusted to produce it.

This scale carries several layers of physical content.
First, it is \emph{universal}: $\rho_c$ does not depend on the
black-hole mass, so the same Planck-thickness critical shell appears
around stellar, intermediate, and supermassive black holes alike.
Second, the fact that $\rho_c\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$ --- rather than, say,
the Schwarzschild radius --- explains why the standard semiclassical
description works so well at low energies: all deviations from exact
Hawking thermality are confined to a region of Planck thickness,
invisible to low-frequency radiation.
Third, $\rho_c$ gives a concrete physical location for the shell
microstates required by the conditional theorem
(Section~\ref{app:conditional_theorem}): it is not the horizon itself
but the surface at proper distance $\rho_c$ where the Lorentzian
ordered phase dissolves.

The status of this result is \emph{structural}: the formula follows
from the Tolman law and the ECT critical temperature, conditional on
the physically natural assumption that local Tolman heating is the
relevant control parameter for Lorentz-order loss.
An independent derivation of this assumption from the full black-hole
branch of the condensate action remains an open problem.
Nevertheless, $\rho_c$ represents the sharpest quantitative output
of the ECT black-hole sector and is in principle testable through
universal near-horizon deviations in ringdown spectra and
effective-boundary-condition analyses of gravitational-wave data.

\paragraph{Dark-sector implications.}

An important conceptual consequence of the ECT framework is that both
phenomena commonly attributed to the cosmological dark sector are
\emph{interpretable within} the condensate structure of the vacuum
(Level~B/C; see open problems).

First, the late-time accelerated expansion can be interpreted as the
residual vacuum energy associated with the condensate background. In
this sense dark energy corresponds to the macroscopic energy density of
the condensate and does not require the introduction of a separate
fundamental cosmological constant.

Second, the gravitational phenomena usually attributed to dark matter
are reinterpreted in ECT as manifestations of the nonlinear
Lorentz-order-field branch: in dilute galactic environments the
$\phi$-sector activates a critical regime that enhances the effective
gravitational pull, reproducing flat rotation curves, the radial
acceleration relation, and the baryonic Tully--Fisher relation without
invoking collisionless particle dark matter.

In addition to this effective mechanism, the condensate sector may
support further degrees of freedom such as Goldstone-like modes or
topological configurations. These excitations could behave as extremely
weakly interacting or ultra-light components and therefore contribute to
dark-sector phenomenology. Determining whether such excitations are
observable or effectively hidden requires a detailed analysis of the
microscopic condensate dynamics.


\paragraph{Detectability of the ECT mass-discrepancy mechanism.}

In ECT, the dominant mass-discrepancy phenomenology on galactic scales is not
due to a new collisionless particle component but arises from the
nonlinear response of the Lorentz-order field $\phi$ in the
critical weak-field branch.  There is therefore \emph{no} additional
local particle flux to be detected in laboratory experiments, and
standard direct-detection strategies are not expected to observe
a signal.

Instead, the appropriate detection channel is gravitational: precision
tests of kinematics and lensing as a function of environment and scale.
In particular, ECT can be constrained by joint rotation-curve and
lensing analyses, by tests of the external-field effect in systems such
as satellites and ultra-diffuse galaxies, and by cluster-merger lensing
geometries (e.g.\ Bullet-like systems), where the condensate
redistribution can decouple the lensing potential from the gas
distribution.

If the condensate sector supports additional weakly coupled excitations
(Goldstone-like modes or topological configurations), these would behave
as an ultra-light and extremely feebly interacting component. Their most
promising observational signatures would then be astrophysical
structure effects (core sizes, interference patterns, small-scale
suppression, or characteristic oscillatory signals), rather than
terrestrial scattering events.


\paragraph{Detectability of the ECT dark-energy mechanism.}

In ECT, dark energy corresponds to residual condensate vacuum energy and
possible slow evolution of condensate parameters at late times. Unlike a
pure cosmological constant, this scenario generically allows mild
time-dependence, which is best tested through precision constraints on
the expansion history and growth of structure, e.g.\ via the
combination of BAO+SNe, weak lensing, and redshift-space distortions.
A key target is the redshift dependence of the effective equation of
state $w(z)$ and potential correlations between late-time acceleration
and quantities controlling the condensate background.

If the condensate parameters are effectively frozen on cosmological
timescales, the model becomes observationally close to $\Lambda$CDM at
the background level, and the discriminating power shifts to combined
constraints on growth, lensing, and consistency relations.


\paragraph{Observational prospects.}

The ECT framework therefore suggests two complementary observational
strategies.

The first is precision tests of the predicted modifications of gravity
on galactic and cluster scales, including the radial acceleration
relation, the external-field effect, and the baryonic Tully--Fisher
relation. These effects provide direct falsifiable predictions of the
theory.

The second is the search for additional condensate excitations. If such
modes exist, they would be expected to couple extremely weakly to
ordinary matter and could appear as ultra-light dark-sector degrees of
freedom. Conversely, it is also possible that the condensate dynamics
suppresses these excitations so strongly that they remain effectively
undetectable.

\paragraph{ECT: postulates, derived results, and phenomenological inputs.}
\label{app:constants}

For clarity we collect the logical structure of the theory.
Results fall into four categories:
(P)~\emph{Postulates};
(D)~\emph{Derived} (strict consequences of postulates);
(Ph)~\emph{Phenomenological} (free parameters matched to observations);
(O)~\emph{Open} (plausible but not yet rigorously derived).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Postulates~(P):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=P\theenumi.,leftmargin=2.2em,itemsep=1pt]
  \item 4D Euclidean manifold with metric $\delta_{AB}$; no preferred time.
  \item $O(4)$-invariant action $S_E[\Psi]$ for a scalar condensate.
  \item SSB $O(4)\to O(3)$ via gradient condensate $\langle n_A\rangle=\delta_{Aw}$.
  \item Kinetic sector: most general $O(3)$-invariant rank-$2$ tensor
        $K^{AB}=\beta\,\delta^{AB}-\alpha\,n^A n^B$.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Key derived results~(D):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=D\theenumi.,leftmargin=2.2em,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Lorentzian signature iff $\alpha>\beta>0$; Euclidean iff $\alpha<\beta$.
  \item Lorentzian phase is macroscopic only: $\beta<\alpha<4\beta$.
  \item Speed of light: $c_*=\sqrt{\beta/(\alpha-\beta)}$.
  \item Gravitational constant: $G_N=1/(8\pi v_0^2(\alpha-\beta))$.
  \item Planck constant (self-consistency): the minimal-loop action
        $S_{\rm loop,min}=2\pi\hbar$ identifies $\hbar = \beta v_0^2 m_\varphi/2$,
        where $m_\varphi=\sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0$ is the radial-mode mass.
        This is a consistency relation among $(v_0,\lambda,\beta)$,
        not an independent derivation of $\hbar$ (OP-$\Lambda$).
  \item Canonical commutation relations $[\hat x_i,\hat p_j]=i\hbar\delta_{ij}$
        derived from single-valuedness of condensate phase (not postulated).
  \item Heisenberg uncertainty principle as Cauchy--Schwarz theorem on $L^2$.
  \item Second law $dS/dt\geq0$: effective result within Gaussian--Markov
        approximation; structurally motivated low-entropy initial condition
        from condensate phase transition; full microscopic derivation open (OP24).
  \item Born measure: unique probability assignment consistent with emergent
        amplitude sector under structural assumptions C1--C3; unique outcome
        selection remains open.
  \item Structural route toward Pauli exclusion principle via $SU(2)$
        spinor representation sign structure (compatible with fermionic
        antisymmetry in the ordered sector; full PLZ theorem not obtained;
        beyond-quadratic corrections speculative).
  \item Conditional Goldstone-sector Casimir-type effect ($\times 3/2$ at condensate/superfluid boundaries only;
        not a prediction for standard metallic plates), Unruh temperature,
        and environmental decoherence as three observables controlled by
        related limits of one condensate two-point function
        $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})\propto v_0^2 C_{\rm sym}(\tau,r)$
        (organizing proposition, not theorem-level unification).
  \item Arrow of time: emergent from $dS_{\rm ent}/dw\geq0$ within
        Gaussian--Markov approximation ($\Gamma_{\rm irr}\gg1$ macroscopically);
        quantum time-reversal at $\Gamma_{\rm irr}\lesssim1$; full microscopic
        derivation open (OP24).
  \item Galactic acceleration scale: $g_\dagger \propto c^2\phi_*(\phi_{\rm gal}) \propto cH_0$
        (structural; $\mathcal{O}(1)$ coefficient undetermined).
  \item Inflation: $n_s=1-2/N_e=0.967$ at $N_e=60$.
  \item Universal near-horizon critical scale:
        $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}\approx 0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}$,
        mass-independent (conditional on Tolman control).
  \item Conditional theorem: exact Hawking thermality excluded by unitarity
        + finite shell entropy + complete evaporation.
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Phenomenological inputs~(Ph):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=Ph\theenumi.,leftmargin=2.2em,itemsep=1pt]
  \item $\beta=1$ (working convention; see Section~\ref{sec:metric_classification}).
  \item $v_0\simeq\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ (matching $G_N$).
  \item $\alpha=2\beta$ (physical constraint $c_*\equiv c=1$); canonical $\beta=1$, $\alpha=2$ --- see Section~\ref{sec:metric_classification}.
  \item $\phi_{\rm env}$: one environment parameter per galaxy.
  \item SM gauge group embedded via condensate phase symmetries (derivation: open).
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Open / conjectured~(O):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=O\theenumi.,leftmargin=2.2em,itemsep=1pt]
  \item Full renormalisability on fixed Euclidean background.
  \item Three fermion generations from condensate topology.
  \item RG connection of three condensate scales ($M_{\rm Pl}$, $246$\,GeV, kpc).
  \item Baryogenesis: $\eta_B\sim9\times10^{-10}$ (observed: $6\times10^{-10}$).
\end{enumerate}

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Condensate constants:}
\begin{align}
c_* &= \sqrt{\frac{\beta}{\alpha-\beta}}\xrightarrow{\;\alpha=2\beta,\;\beta=1\;} 1, \\[3pt]
\hbar &= \frac{\beta\,v_0^2}{2}\,m_\varphi\quad[m_\varphi\equiv\sqrt{2\lambda}\,v_0],\quad\text{(self-consistency)} \\[3pt]
G_N &= \frac{1}{8\pi v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)}\xrightarrow{\;\alpha=2\beta,\;\beta=1\;}\frac{1}{8\pi v_0^2}.
\end{align}

\paragraph{Quantum and microscopic sector.}

A major focus of the present work is the structural derivation of key
results of quantum mechanics from the condensate action.  The canonical
commutation relations and uncertainty principle are derived without
additional postulates; the second law and Born measure require Gaussian--Markov
or structural assumptions (see OP24, OP23).  The key results are as follows.

The canonical commutation relations $[\hat x_i, \hat p_j]=i\hbar\delta_{ij}$
are not postulated but emerge from the single-valuedness of the condensate
phase field on closed loops (Section~\ref{sec:CCR}).  The imaginary unit
$i$ enters through the phase factor $e^{i\theta}$ of the polar condensate,
not from the Wick rotation.  The Heisenberg uncertainty principle
$\Delta x\,\Delta p\geq\hbar/2$ then follows as a Cauchy--Schwarz
inequality in $L^2(\mathbb{R}^3)$.

The influence functional structure (Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional})
clarifies the system--environment partition of the condensate: the
symmetric correlator $N(\tau)=\langle\chi(\tau)\chi(0)\rangle_{\rm sym}$
controls decoherence, while the retarded kernel $D_R(\tau)=\Theta(\tau)
\langle[\chi(\tau),\chi(0)]\rangle$ controls dissipation.  A critical
identity is $\Gamma[q,q]\equiv 0$ (the decoherence functional vanishes on
the diagonal), which must not be confused with the entropy-production
functional $\Gamma_{\rm irr}[q]=\kappa\int\dot{q}^2\,dw\geq0$.

The quantum statistics of condensate excitations follows structurally from
$SO(4)\cong SU(2)_L\times SU(2)_R$ representation theory (tensor
representations $\to$ bosonic sectors; spinor representations $\to$
fermionic-sector compatibility, structural Level~B; not a derivation of
fermionic degrees of freedom from the bare bosonic condensate action).
This provides a \emph{structural route} to the Pauli exclusion principle;
a full Pauli--L\"{u}ders--Zumino theorem has not been obtained, and
beyond-quadratic corrections at Planck density remain speculative
(Section~\ref{sec:emergent_principles}).

The three quantum vacuum phenomena --- conditional Goldstone-sector
Casimir-type effect, Unruh temperature, and environmental decoherence ---
are three observables controlled by related limits of the condensate
two-point function $N(\tau,\mathbf{r})$,
an organizing proposition of the ECT vacuum sector
(Section~\ref{sec:unified_correlator}).  This is not a reformulation
in new notation: it is a structural unification in which all three
phenomena are controlled by the same condensate vacuum amplitude $v_0^2$.

\paragraph{Scope of ECT: what is unified and what remains open.}
\label{par:scope_ect}

ECT achieves a specific and well-defined unification: the causal structure
of spacetime, the quantum of action, and Newton's gravitational constant are
\emph{parametrically linked} within a single scalar condensate framework.
In precise terms, $c_*$, $G_N$, and $\hbar$ are related to condensate
parameters $(\alpha,\,v_0,\,\lambda)$ through \emph{internal consistency
relations} in a common field theory: once $v_0$ is calibrated from $G_N$,
both $c_*$ and $\hbar$ follow self-consistently from the same parameter set.
This is a non-trivial structural economy, though it does not yet constitute
a fully non-circular microscopic derivation of the Planck scale (OP-$\Lambda$).

At the same time, ECT is not a Theory of Everything.  The following elements
remain beyond the current framework:

\begin{itemize}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \textbf{Standard Model gauge group.}
        The gauge structure $SU(3)\times SU(2)\times U(1)$ is embedded
        into ECT as a postulate; it is not derived from the condensate action.
  \item \textbf{Fine structure constant.}
        $\alpha_{\rm fs}\approx1/137$ is not predicted; the $Z_A$-normalisation
        route (Open Problem OP11) is the most tractable avenue.
  \item \textbf{Three fermion generations.}
        ECT provides spinor representations after $O(4)\to O(3)$ SSB but does
        not explain why exactly three generations exist.
  \item \textbf{Yukawa mass hierarchy.}
        Fermion mass ratios spanning six orders of magnitude are not explained.
  \item \textbf{Quantitative RG link between scales.}
        The three condensate VEVs ($v_0\sim\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$,
        $v_2\sim246\,\mathrm{GeV}$, galactic $\phi$-sector)
        are connected qualitatively by the running coupling $\lambda(\mu)$
        but a quantitative two-loop analysis is not yet available.
\end{itemize}

We therefore describe ECT as a \emph{unified source of spacetime geometry,
quantum mechanics, and gravity} --- not a Theory of Everything.
This honest characterisation is consistent with the theory's derivational
achievements while acknowledging the substantial programme of further work
that remains.

\paragraph{Outlook.}


\paragraph{Cluster mergers.}

The $\phi$-branch was tested on four merging clusters
(Bullet~\cite{Clowe2006,Paraficz2016},
MACS~J0025~\cite{Bradac2008},
El~Gordo~\cite{Diego2023},
Abell~520~\cite{Mahdavi2007})
using a 2D projected thin-lens $\phi$-closure.
\emph{Qualitatively}, all four offset morphologies are
correctly reproduced: in Bullet, MACS~J0025, and El~Gordo
the lensing peaks follow the compact stellar component,
while in Abell~520 they follow the dense gas core ---
exactly as predicted by a $\phi$-field that responds to
local density contrast rather than to a universal
collisionless species.
This dual morphology (stellar-tracking \emph{and}
gas-tracking) is a distinctive ECT signature that neither
$\Lambda$CDM nor MOND can naturally accommodate.
\emph{Quantitatively}, the $\phi$-branch produces
15--45\% of the observed lensing mass (deficit factor
$\sim\!2$--$3$, comparable to the MOND cluster problem).
Three uncomputed effects --- environmental $g_\dagger$
modulation, gravitational slip, and non-equilibrium
merger dynamics --- may individually contribute at
order unity.
The cluster mass discrepancy remains an honest open
problem (OP22, OP23).

Several important open problems remain, including the
microscopic origin of certain effective coefficients, the
derivation of the Standard Model gauge structure, the
ultraviolet behaviour of the gravitational sector, and the
detailed dynamics of the condensate phase transition.

The framework does, however, produce falsifiable predictions
that can be confronted with current and near-future data.
The open problems listed in Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}
define concrete directions for further work.

ECT should therefore be viewed not as a complete fundamental
theory but as a testable theoretical framework at an early
stage of development.














\paragraph{Falsifiability and key tests.}
\label{par:falsifiability}

ECT makes concrete, falsifiable predictions that distinguish it from both
$\Lambda$CDM and MOND:

\begin{enumerate}[itemsep=2pt]
  \item \textbf{Environmental modulation of $g_\dagger$:}
        the Lorentz-order-field framework predicts that the effective
        acceleration scale $g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})$ varies weakly
        with galactic environment.  A positive correlation between
        the fitted $\phi_{\rm env}$ and independently measured
        local cosmic density, detectable with the full SPARC sample
        ($\sim\!175$ galaxies) cross-matched against large-scale-structure
        catalogues, would constitute direct evidence for the $\phi$-branch
        mechanism.
  \item \textbf{Gravitational-wave speed:} $\delta c_{\rm GW}/c \sim 10^{-62}$,
        consistent with GW170817 bound by 47 orders; future signals from
        BNS mergers with sub-microsecond timing will probe $\delta c/c \sim 10^{-17}$.
  \item \textbf{Fifth force:} spin precession $\omega_5 \sim 10^{-10}$~rad/s,
        E\"otv\"os parameter $\eta \sim 10^{-15}$ (MICROSCOPE-2 sensitivity).
  \item \textbf{Inflation tensor-to-scalar ratio:} leading-order prediction
        $r \approx 0.267$ (exceeds current bounds; resolved only by non-minimal
        condensate coupling or multi-field extension).
  \item \textbf{Dark energy EOS:} $w_0 \approx -0.83$, $w_a \neq 0$;
        distinguishable from $\Lambda$CDM ($w=-1$) at $>2\sigma$ with
        DESI Year-5 data.
  \item \textbf{Universal near-horizon critical scale $\rho_c$:}
        the ECT black-hole sector predicts that \emph{all} non-extremal
        black holes carry a critical shell at universal proper distance
        $\rho_c = \ell_{\rm Pl}/\sqrt{3\pi}\approx0.33\,\ell_{\rm Pl}$
        from the horizon, independent of mass.
        This scale controls corrections to quasinormal-mode spectra
        at relative order $\rho_c/r_s \sim M_{\rm Pl}^2/M^2$,
        and sets the characteristic frequency of any near-horizon
        boundary-condition deviation.
        A detection of a \emph{universal} (mass-independent) near-horizon
        scale in ringdown data from gravitational-wave events of different
        masses would constitute direct evidence for the ECT shell picture;
        conversely, a mass-dependent deviation would falsify it.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Uniqueness of the Kinetic Tensor $K^{AB}$}
\label{app:tensor_uniqueness}

\textit{Reference from main text: Theorem~\ref{thm:tensor_uniqueness}
in Section~\ref{sec:tensor_uniqueness}.}

\subsection*{Setup}

We seek the most general symmetric rank-2 tensor $K^{AB}$ satisfying:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item $K^{AB}=K^{BA}$;
  \item invariance under $O(3)$ rotations in the hyperplane $\{1,2,3\}$;
  \item built locally and algebraically from tensors
    $\{\delta^{AB}, n^A\}$, without additional derivatives,
    where $n^A=\delta^A{}_w$ is the fixed unit vector along the preferred direction.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection*{Basis decomposition}

The space of symmetric rank-2 tensors in $\mathbb{R}^4$ has dimension 10.
Under $O(3)$ the available background objects generate two $O(3)$-invariant
symmetric rank-2 structures: $\delta^{AB}$ and $n^A n^B$.
Without additional derivatives or pseudo-tensors (Levi-Civita is
antisymmetric and excluded), these two span the space of admissible tensors.
Hence the most general tensor is:
\[
  K^{AB} = a\,\delta^{AB} + b\,n^A n^B,\qquad a,b\in\mathbb{R}.
\]
Setting $a=\beta$, $b=-\alpha$ gives~\eqref{eq:K_general}.

\subsection*{Connection to the quadratic action}

The kinetic term:
\begin{align}
  \tfrac{1}{2}K^{AB}\partial_A\varphi\,\partial_B\varphi
  &= \tfrac{\beta}{2}(\partial_A\varphi)^2
     - \tfrac{\alpha}{2}(n^A\partial_A\varphi)^2,
\end{align}
which is exactly the action~\eqref{eq:quadratic_action}. $\blacksquare$

See also~\cite[Ch.~2]{Weinberg1996} and~\cite{Landau1986Elasticity}.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Background Configuration and Fluctuation Expansion}
\label{app:background_split}\label{eq:Phi_bg}

\textit{Reference from main text: Eq.~\eqref{eq:background}
and Section~\ref{sec:eft_quadratic}.}

\subsection*{Background solution}

Condition P4 requires $\langle\partial_A\Phi\rangle = u_0\delta_{Aw}$.
The simplest solution is:
\[
  \Phi_{\rm bg}(X) = u_0\,w + \Phi_*,\qquad \Phi_*=\text{const}.
\]
Check: $\partial_A\Phi_{\rm bg} = u_0\,\delta_{Aw}$ for all $X^A$. $\checkmark$

\noindent\textbf{Important note.}
This background is linear in~$w$ and therefore is not a minimum of
the potential $V(\Phi_{\rm bg})$ which grows without bound for $|w|\to\infty$.
It does not claim to be a stationary point of the bare micro-action~P3;
it defines the ordered vacuum sector postulated by~P4.
Physically this is analogous to a gradient condensate in superfluid
systems~\cite{Donnelly1991}.

\subsection*{Quadratic expansion of the broken-phase EFT}

The effective broken-phase action $S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}$
expanded around the background:
\begin{equation}
  S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}[\Phi_{\rm bg}+\varphi]
  = S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}[\Phi_{\rm bg}]
  + \underbrace{\int d^4X\,
    \frac{\delta S_{\rm eff}^{\rm broken}}{\delta\Phi}
    \bigg|_{\rm bg}\varphi}_{=\,0\text{ (stationarity by P4)}}
  + S^{(2)}[\varphi]+O(\varphi^3).
\end{equation}
The quadratic term:
\begin{equation}
  S^{(2)}[\varphi] = \int d^4X\!\left\{
    \frac{1}{2}(\partial_A\varphi)^2 + \frac{m_{\rm eff}^2}{2}\varphi^2
  \right\},
\end{equation}
where $m_{\rm eff}^2$ is the EFT mass parameter of the broken phase
(not identified a priori with $V''(\Phi_{\rm bg})$ of the bare potential).

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Derivation of the Lorentzian Window}
\label{app:lorentz_window}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:lorentz_window}.}

\subsection*{Lower bound: $\alpha>\beta$}

From the quadratic action~\eqref{eq:quadratic_action}
the dispersion relation in momentum space:
\[
  \beta\,\mathbf{k}^2 - (\alpha-\beta)\,k_w^2 + m_{\rm eff}^2 = 0.
\]
For $\alpha>\beta$ the coefficient of $k_w^2$ is negative, i.e.\
the operator is hyperbolic along~$w$---Lorentzian signature.
For $\alpha\leq\beta$ the operator is positive-definite or degenerate---Euclidean
signature or loss of causality.
The lower bound follows directly from Theorem~\ref{thm:tensor_uniqueness}
and the requirement of hyperbolicity.

\subsection*{Upper bound: $\alpha<4\beta$ (under isotropy assumption)}

Assume that at scales $L\ll\xi_{\rm cond}$ the orientation variable
is isotropically distributed over the four Euclidean directions:
$\langle n^A n^B\rangle = \delta^{AB}/4$.
The averaged kinetic tensor:
\[
  \langle K^{AB}\rangle = \left(\beta-\frac{\alpha}{4}\right)\delta^{AB}.
\]
Positive-definiteness requires $\beta-\alpha/4>0$, i.e.\ $\alpha<4\beta$.
In $d$-dimensional space this reads $\alpha<d\beta$; for $d=4$ (postulate~P1):
upper bound $\alpha<4\beta$.

\noindent\textbf{Status.}
Lower bound $\alpha>\beta$---strict consequence of
Theorem~\ref{thm:tensor_uniqueness} and Lorentzian requirement.
Upper bound $\alpha<4\beta$---requires the additional short-distance isotropy
assumption; not a strict consequence of P1--P5.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{EFT Motivation via Integrating Out the Radial Mode}
\label{app:eft_derivation}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:eft_quadratic}.}

\noindent\textbf{Status.}
This appendix provides a schematic EFT motivation within the ordered
vacuum sector selected by postulate~P4, not a strict derivation of
the broken-phase action from the bare micro-action~P3 alone.
The background $\Phi_{\rm bg}$ is not a solution of the equations
of motion of~P3; the following expansion refers to the EFT of the
broken phase.

\subsection*{Phase action and heavy-mode integration}

At $E\ll m_\sigma$ the heavy radial mode integrates out,
leaving the effective action for soft fluctuation~$\varphi$.
The isotropic kinetic term in the broken phase acquires anisotropic
$O(3)$-invariant deformation parametrised by~$(\alpha,\beta)$:
\[
  S_{\rm EFT}^{(2)}[\varphi]
  = \int d^4X\!\left\{
    \frac{1}{2}(\partial_A\varphi)^2 + \frac{m_{\rm eff}^2}{2}\varphi^2
    + O(\partial^4/m_\sigma^2)
  \right\}.
\]
The anisotropy parameters $(\alpha,\beta)$ are not fixed by this analysis
and must be determined from physical matching conditions~(OP-grad).

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Dimensions, Normalisations, and Matching Relations}
\label{app:dimensions}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:consistency_relations}.}

\subsection*{A. Dimensions in natural units ($c=\hbar=1$, provisionally)}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{ll}
\hline
Quantity & Dimension \\
\hline
$\Phi$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$u_0=|\langle\partial_A\Phi\rangle|$ & $[\text{GeV}^2]$ \\
$\mu$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$\lambda$ & dimensionless \\
$m_\sigma=\sqrt{2}\,\mu$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$m_{\rm eff}$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$M_G=\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$ & $[\text{GeV}]$ \\
$S_0$ & dimensionless in $\hbar=c=1$; status pending identification \\
$\xi_{\rm cond}$ & $[\text{GeV}^{-1}]$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent\textbf{Note.} $[\phi_0]=\text{GeV}$, $[u_0]=\text{GeV}^2$: these are different objects.

\subsection*{B. Normalisation and benchmark point}

From~\eqref{eq:c_star_def}: $c_*^2=\beta/(\alpha-\beta)$.
At $c_*=c=1$ and $\beta=1$: $\alpha=2$, $c_*=1$.

\subsection*{C. Distinction between bare and EFT masses}

\begin{align}
  m_\sigma^2 &= V''(\phi_0)=2\mu^2
  &&\text{(bare radial scale, level P3)},\\
  m_{\rm eff}^2 &\neq m_\sigma^2
  &&\text{(EFT fluctuation mass, broken-phase EFT)}.
\end{align}
Their relation appears only after explicit EFT matching through radial-mode integration.

\subsection*{D. Gravitational matching}

\[
  G_N = \frac{c_*^4}{8\pi M_G^2}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  M_G = \bar{M}_{\rm Pl} \approx 2.435\times 10^{18}\,\text{GeV}
  \quad (c=\hbar=1).
\]

\subsection*{E. Pre-quantum action scale}

From the winding condition~\eqref{eq:winding_condition}:
$S_{\rm loop,min}=2\pi S_0$.
The question of identifying $S_0$ with observable~$\hbar$
is deferred to Section~\ref{sec:quantum}, where it is
discussed and motivated in the context of the Quantum Sector.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Why the Explicit Estimate of $S_0$ Is Deferred}
\label{app:Sloop_calc}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:hbar_status}.}

To obtain~$S_0$ one needs to construct an effective 1D functional
for a loop in the coherent sector.
Starting from the 4D phase action
$S[\theta]\sim\int_{\mathcal{V}}d^4X\,f(\rho)(\partial_A\theta)^2$,
the transition from the bulk integral over~$\mathcal{V}$ to a
1D action along~$\mathcal{C}$ requires:
(i)~choice of transverse profile shape;
(ii)~integration of $f(\rho)$ over the transverse cross-section;
(iii)~introduction of an effective line tension $\mathcal{T}$
     such that $S_{\rm eff}^{\rm 1D}[\mathcal{C}]=\mathcal{T}\cdot|\mathcal{C}|$;
(iv)~minimisation over contour shape and size under the $n=1$
     winding constraint.
Each of these steps requires the nonlinear broken-phase potential
(beyond the quadratic EFT) and the choice of a vortex profile,
which are not determined at the ECT basics level.
The explicit calculation therefore belongs to Section~\ref{sec:quantum}.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Effective Action for Orientation Modes: Nonlinear Sigma-Model}
\label{app:sigma_model}

\textit{Reference from main text: Sections~\ref{sec:mode_classes}
and~\ref{sec:mode_hierarchy}.
Status: most general low-energy EFT ansatz for a unit-vector field
in the broken phase; quantisation not required.}

\subsection*{Setup}

In the ordered vacuum sector (P4) with constraint $n_A n^A=1$,
the most general local quadratic low-energy action for the orientation field:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:sigma_model}
  S_n = \frac{\kappa_n}{2}\int d^4X\,\partial_B n_A\,\partial^B n^A
  + \int d^4X\,\Lambda(X)(n_A n^A-1),
\end{equation}
where $\kappa_n>0$ is the effective stiffness of the orientation sector
and $\Lambda$ is a Lagrange multiplier.
This is a nonlinear sigma-model with target $S^3\simeq O(4)/O(3)$.

\subsection*{Linearisation around the vacuum}

Setting $n_A=\bar{n}_A+\delta n_A$, $\bar{n}_A=\delta_{Aw}$ (P4).
From $n_A n^A=1$ at first order: $\bar{n}_A\delta n^A=0\Rightarrow\delta n_w=0$.
Physical fluctuations live in three transverse components $\delta n_i$, $i=1,2,3$.
Quadratic action:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Sn2}
  S_n^{(2)}=\frac{\kappa_n}{2}\int d^4X\,\partial_B\,\delta n_i\,\partial^B\,\delta n_i.
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Equation of motion and dispersion}

\begin{equation}
  \partial_B\partial^B\,\delta n_i=0,\qquad i=1,2,3.
\end{equation}
In the Lorentzian sector ($w\to -ic_n t$):
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:eon_lorentz}
  \partial_t^2\,\delta n_i - c_n^2\nabla^2\,\delta n_i=0,\qquad
  \omega^2=c_n^2 k^2.
\end{equation}
Three massless orientation modes, consistent with the Goldstone theorem
for $O(4)/O(3)$.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Noether Currents: Translational and Rotational Sectors}
\label{app:noether_full}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:noether}.
Status: classical field theory; no quantisation required.}

\subsection*{A. Translational invariance and $T^{AB}$}

\noindent\textbf{Scalar bare sector~(P3):}
\begin{equation}
  T^{AB}_{(\Phi)}=\partial^A\Phi\,\partial^B\Phi
  -\delta^{AB}\!\left[\tfrac{1}{2}(\partial_C\Phi)^2+V(\Phi)\right],
  \qquad\partial_A T^{AB}_{(\Phi)}=0.
\end{equation}

\noindent\textbf{Orientation sigma-model~\eqref{eq:sigma_model}:}
\begin{equation}
  T^{AB}_{(n)}=\kappa_n\,\partial^A n_C\,\partial^B n^C
  -\delta^{AB}\tfrac{\kappa_n}{2}(\partial_D n_E)^2,
  \qquad\partial_A T^{AB}_{(n)}=0.
\end{equation}
Conservation $\partial_A T^{AB}=0$ follows from the homogeneity
of the arena~(P1), not from $O(4)$ rotations~(P2).

\subsection*{B. $O(4)$-invariance and angular currents}

From $O(4)$-symmetry (P2), Noether's theorem~\cite{Noether1918}
for rotations $\delta X^A=\omega^A{}_B X^B$:
\begin{equation}
  J^{C,AB}=X^A T^{CB}_{(\Phi)}-X^B T^{CA}_{(\Phi)},
  \qquad\partial_C J^{C,AB}=0.
\end{equation}
For the orientation field $n_A$ (a vector under $O(4)$),
a spin contribution is added:
\begin{equation}
  J^{C,AB}_{(n)}=X^A T^{CB}_{(n)}-X^B T^{CA}_{(n)}
  +\kappa_n(n^A\partial^C n^B-n^B\partial^C n^A).
\end{equation}

\subsection*{C. Inheritance by both branches}

Both sets of currents---translational $T^{AB}$ and rotational $J^{C,AB}$---
exist at the level of the bare~P3. Both branches of ECT inherit this
variational foundation.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Correlation Length from the Radial-Mode Propagator}
\label{app:corr_length}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:sigma_scales}.
Status: standard EFT estimate from the massive Euclidean propagator.}

\subsection*{Euclidean propagator}

Quadratic action of the radial mode:
$S_\sigma^{(2)}=\frac{1}{2}\int d^4X[(\partial_A\sigma)^2+m_\sigma^2\sigma^2]$.
Fourier propagator: $G_\sigma(k)=1/(k^2+m_\sigma^2)$.

\subsection*{Coordinate representation at large distances}

In $d=4$ Euclidean space for $r\to\infty$:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:G_coord}
  G_\sigma(r)\;\xrightarrow{r\to\infty}\;
  \frac{m_\sigma^{3/2}}{(2\pi)^{3/2}\sqrt{2}}\,
  \frac{e^{-m_\sigma r}}{r^{3/2}}.
\end{equation}
The exponential factor $e^{-m_\sigma r}$ defines the characteristic
decay length of amplitude correlations:
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\xi_{\rm cond}\sim m_\sigma^{-1}.}
\end{equation}
This is a standard EFT estimate; the identification
$\xi_{\rm cond}\sim\ell_{\rm Pl}$ is a phenomenological matching hypothesis.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Scaling Analysis of the Bath Spectral Density}
\label{app:ohmic_markov}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time},
Step~3.
Status: scaling analysis; strict derivation deferred to Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional}.}

\subsection*{Spectral density in 3D with linear dispersion}

Goldstone orientation modes with $\omega_k=c_*k$:
\begin{equation}
  J(\omega)\propto N_{\rm eff}\,\omega^2\,|g(\omega/c_*)|^2
  \quad\text{(up to powers of }c_*\text{)}.
\end{equation}
Scaling regimes:
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\hline
Coupling & $J(\omega)$ for $\omega\to 0$ & Regime \\
\hline
$|g|^2=\text{const}$ & $\propto\omega^2$ & super-ohmic \\
$|g|^2\propto k^2$ & $\propto\omega^4$ & super-ohmic \\
$|g|^2\propto k^{-1}$ & $\propto\omega$ & ohmic \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Standard 3D derivative coupling gives a \emph{super-ohmic} contribution
$J(\omega)\propto\omega^4$, not ohmic.
Ohmic behaviour requires either a non-standard coupling form,
a reduced effective bath dimensionality, or additional coarse-graining.

\subsection*{Markovian approximation: heuristics}

$\tau_{\rm env}\sim m_\sigma^{-1}$ (bath memory scale from P3 EFT cutoff).
Markovianity ($K(\tau)\approx K(0)\delta(\tau)$) requires $\tau_{\rm env}\ll\tau_{\rm dec}$
where $\tau_{\rm dec}=1/(N_{\rm eff}\gamma)$.
In the weak-coupling, large-$N_{\rm eff}$ limit this is heuristically consistent
with the EFT estimate~\eqref{eq:sigma_mass}, but not a strict derivation.

Both ohmic behaviour and Markovianity are adopted as effective phenomenological
working assumptions for the macroscopic decoherence calculation.
Strict derivation belongs to Section~\ref{sec:influence_functional}.

% ------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Retarded Causal Kernel: Proof That $K(\tau<0)=0$}
\label{app:retarded_kernel}

\textit{Reference from main text: Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time},
condition~(ii), Step~2.
Status: Level~A in the quadratic Lorentzian sector.}

\subsection*{Setup}

After passing to the effective Lorentzian description
(Section~\ref{sec:effective_metric}), small fluctuations satisfy:
\begin{equation}
  (\partial_t^2-c_*^2\nabla^2+M^2)\,\varphi(t,\mathbf{x})=J(t,\mathbf{x}).
\end{equation}
The retarded Green's function:
\begin{equation}
  (\partial_t^2-c_*^2\nabla^2+M^2)\,G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})
  =\delta(t)\,\delta^{(3)}(\mathbf{x}).
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Fourier representation and pole structure}

\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Gret_Fourier}
  G_{\rm ret}(\omega,\mathbf{k})
  =\frac{1}{(\omega+i0^+)^2-\omega_k^2},
  \qquad\omega_k=\sqrt{c_*^2k^2+M^2}.
\end{equation}
Both poles $\omega=\pm\omega_k-i0^+$ lie in the \emph{lower} half-plane.

\subsection*{Proof that $G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=0$ for $t<0$}

For $t<0$ the integrand $e^{-i\omega t}$ decays for $\text{Im}\,\omega\to+\infty$,
so the $\omega$-contour closes in the upper half-plane.
Since both poles lie in the lower half-plane, the Cauchy theorem gives:
\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:K_causal}
  \boxed{G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=0\qquad(t<0).}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Explicit form for $t>0$}

\begin{equation}
  \label{eq:Gret_explicit}
  G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=\theta(t)\int\frac{d^3k}{(2\pi)^3}\,
  \frac{\sin(\omega_k t)}{\omega_k}\,e^{i\mathbf{k}\cdot\mathbf{x}}.
\end{equation}
The factor $\theta(t)$ explicitly confirms~\eqref{eq:K_causal}.

\subsection*{What follows and what does not}

\textbf{Follows (Level~A, quadratic sector):}
retarded linear-response kernel $G_{\rm ret}(t,\mathbf{x})=0$ for $t<0$;
causality of the effective linear kernel in broken-phase EFT is strictly satisfied;
condition~(ii) in the arrow-of-time argument (Section~\ref{sec:arrow_of_time})
applies rigorously in the quadratic sector.

\textbf{Does not follow:}
retardedness of the full nonlinear causal kernel of the interacting theory~(OP5);
Markovianity, ohmicity, Born rule, Pauli principle, OS reconstruction.
