{\centering\rule{\linewidth}{0.4pt}\par\vspace{0.5em}{\Large\bfseries Appendices}\par\vspace{0.5em}\rule{\linewidth}{0.4pt}\par}
\vspace{1em}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{From the Basic Physical Premises of ECT to the
Lorentz-Order-Field Programme: Full Derivation Chain}
\label{app:lof_full_derivation}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\subsection{Purpose and scope of this appendix}

This appendix presents the complete chain of reasoning that
leads from the basic physical premises of ECT to the
Lorentz-order-field programme for galactic phenomenology.
Because the proposed mechanism is conceptually unusual and,
to our knowledge, has not been developed in this form in the
existing literature, we spell out the intermediate branches
of reasoning in detail. Our aim is not merely to state the
final equations, but to document why certain routes were
explored, what made them fail, and why subsequent choices
were forced rather than arbitrary.

At each stage we distinguish between:
\begin{itemize}
\item results derived from the effective macroscopic ECT action;
\item results obtained in the quasistatic scalar--tensor regime;
\item one-loop or EFT-supported indications;
\item critical-IR hypotheses not yet fully derived from
  microscopic ECT.
\end{itemize}


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Basic physical premises}
\label{app:lof:premises}

The ECT framework begins from two physical ideas that together
set it apart from other approaches to emergent gravity.

\paragraph{Premise~1: Lorentzianness is emergent.}
The Lorentzian signature $(-,+,+,+)$ of the spacetime metric
is not a fundamental structure but arises from the spontaneous
breaking $O(4) \to O(3)$ of the Euclidean vacuum. The degree
of Lorentzianness is measured by the parameter
$\chi \equiv \alpha - \beta$, where $\alpha$ and $\beta$ are
the anisotropic and isotropic stiffness couplings of the
condensate action~\eqref{eq:ECT_action}. When $\chi > 0$ the
$w$-direction acquires hyperbolic character and perturbations
experience Lorentzian geometry; when $\chi = 0$ the system is
in the Euclidean (symmetric) phase.

\paragraph{Premise~2: matter reinforces the Lorentzian phase.}
Where baryonic mass accumulates, the statistical irreversibility
of motion along the emergent time direction increases: thermal
fluctuations in a dense medium are overwhelmingly
forward-directed, making the vacuum more deeply Lorentzian.
Conversely, in matter-free regions the vacuum relaxes toward
the symmetric (Euclidean) phase boundary.

These premises are not additional postulates external to ECT;
they are the physical motivations from which the mathematical
framework was originally constructed. The question addressed
in this appendix is: \emph{do these premises, combined with
the effective ECT action, produce observable consequences in
galactic dynamics?}

The answer involves a sequence of attempts, dead ends, and
refinements. We present them in the order in which they were
explored.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~1: the condensate-amplitude route $v_0(r)$}
\label{app:lof:branch1}

\subsubsection{Motivation and scope}

The gravitational matching derived in the main text
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic},
eq.~\eqref{eq:Geff_phi}) implies
\begin{equation}
G_{\rm eff}(X) = \frac{1}{8\pi\,v_0^2(X)\,\chi(X)}\,,
\qquad
\chi(X) \equiv \alpha(X) - \beta(X)\,.
\label{eq:app_Geff_v0}
\end{equation}
This immediately suggests two logically distinct possibilities
for obtaining a scale-dependent gravitational response:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a spatial variation of the condensate amplitude $v_0(X)$;
\item a spatial variation of the Lorentz-order parameter
  $\chi(X)$.
\end{enumerate}

At this stage the matching alone does not privilege $v_0$
over~$\chi$.
That distinction emerges only after analysing their dynamics:
$v_0$ is a heavy radial mode and cannot carry galactic-scale
structure, whereas $\chi$ is an order parameter and can
remain soft near criticality.

The first possibility is the most naive one: since
$G_{\rm eff} \propto v_0^{-2}$, if $v_0(r)$ were smaller in
galactic outskirts than near the centre, $G_{\rm eff}(r)$
would increase with radius and could, in principle, mimic
mass-discrepancy phenomenology.

The purpose of this subsection is to show that this route is
not merely inconvenient or phenomenologically unfavourable,
but \emph{fundamentally inconsistent} with the ECT equations
of motion on galactic scales.
The failure is generic: it does not depend on any particular
profile ansatz, interpolation formula, or fitting strategy.

We present three independent arguments.
The first one is decisive; the other two show that the
historical difficulties of the $v_0(r)$ route are not
accidental but are symptoms of the same obstruction.

\subsubsection{Argument 1 (decisive): the radial mode is
Planck-heavy}

The amplitude $v_0$ is not an arbitrary background function.
It is the \emph{radial mode} of the condensate.
Near the symmetry-broken vacuum, the relevant scalar potential
has the Mexican-hat form
$V(\Phi) = -\mu^2\Phi^2/2 + \lambda\Phi^4/4$,
with vacuum expectation value
$v_\infty = \mu/\sqrt{\lambda}$.
Writing $v_0(r) = v_\infty + \delta v(r)$ and linearising the
field equation around the vacuum gives
\begin{equation}
-\beta\,\nabla^2(\delta v) + m_\sigma^2\,\delta v = J(r)\,,
\qquad
m_\sigma^2 = 2\lambda\,v_\infty^2\,,
\label{eq:app_yukawa_v0}
\end{equation}
where $J(r)$ denotes whatever effective source term baryonic
matter induces in the condensate sector.

This is a Yukawa equation.
Its Green-function solution has the universal asymptotic form
\begin{equation}
\delta v(r) \propto \frac{e^{-m_\sigma r}}{r}\,,
\end{equation}
\emph{independently of the detailed shape of the source}.

This already proves the key point: the long-range behaviour
of $v_0(r)$ is fixed by the mass of the radial mode, not by
our choice of profile.

For canonical ECT normalisation one has
$v_\infty \sim M_{\rm Pl}$, $\lambda \sim 10^{-2}$, hence
\begin{equation}
m_\sigma \sim \sqrt{2\lambda}\,M_{\rm Pl}
\sim 0.14\,M_{\rm Pl}\,,
\qquad
\xi_\sigma = m_\sigma^{-1}
\sim 7\,\ell_{\rm Pl}
\sim 10^{-34}\,\text{m}\,.
\end{equation}
Therefore any spatial variation of $v_0$ is exponentially
suppressed beyond roughly the Planck scale.

By contrast, galactic phenomenology would require variation
over $r_{\rm gal} \sim \mathrm{kpc} \sim 10^{20}\,$m.
Equivalently, one would need
$m_\sigma \lesssim r_{\rm gal}^{-1}
\sim 10^{-27}\,\mathrm{m}^{-1}
\sim 6\times10^{-48}\,$GeV,
which is about \textbf{65 orders of magnitude} smaller than the
physical radial mass scale of the theory.

This mismatch is fatal.
It does not say that a specific ansatz is wrong.
It says that \emph{no smooth kpc-scale profile} $v_0(r)$ can
solve the ECT field equation with the physical radial mass
$m_\sigma$.

The source term $J(r)$ has been left generic on purpose.
The conclusion does not depend on the detailed
matter-to-condensate coupling, as long as the radial sector
remains governed by a local second-order equation with mass
$m_\sigma^2 = V''(v_\infty)$.
At a local massive radial field, the asymptotic behaviour is
always Yukawa.

\subsubsection{Argument 2: the profile ambiguity is a symptom,
not the core problem}

The second argument is weaker logically than the first, but
it is important conceptually.

From $G_{\rm eff} \propto v_0^{-2}$, different assumed
profiles generate different effective gravitational laws:
\begin{align}
v_0 \propto [1+(r/r_0)^2]^{-1/2}
  &\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  G_{\rm eff} \propto 1+(r/r_0)^2\,,\\
v_0 \propto [1+(r/r_0)^2]^{-1/4}
  &\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
  G_{\rm eff} \propto \sqrt{1+(r/r_0)^2}\,.
\end{align}
The fact that more than one such profile appeared in earlier
development is not itself the decisive objection.
The decisive objection was already given by Argument~1.
But this ambiguity is a clear diagnostic sign:
once the true equation of motion refuses to produce a
kpc-scale solution, one is forced into profile engineering.

So the profile ambiguity should be understood not as the main
proof, but as evidence that the route had already lost contact
with the underlying dynamics.

\subsubsection{Argument 3: even a hypothetical light
$v_0$-mode would generate an excluded fifth force}

Suppose, for the sake of argument, that one somehow evaded
Argument~1 and engineered a very light amplitude mode capable
of varying over galactic scales.
Then a second problem appears immediately.

Because $G_{\rm eff} \propto v_0^{-2}$, the field $v_0$ would
behave as a scalar-tensor mediator coupled directly to the
strength of gravity.
A light scalar of this kind generically produces an additional
long-range force of order gravitational strength.
In Brans--Dicke language this corresponds to a scalar-mediated
fifth force with order-unity coupling unless one invokes a
nontrivial screening mechanism.

Unscreened or weakly screened long-range scalar forces are
tightly constrained by Solar-System and equivalence-principle
tests, including Cassini ($|\gamma-1| < 2.3\times10^{-5}$)
and MICROSCOPE ($\eta < 10^{-15}$).
Therefore even a hypothetical successful galactic $v_0(r)$
profile would still face a severe fifth-force problem.

The $v_0$-route is thus doubly obstructed:
\emph{(i)} dynamically, because the radial mode is
Planck-heavy;
\emph{(ii)} phenomenologically, because a light amplitude
mode would behave as an excluded fifth-force mediator unless
additional nonlinear screening were introduced.

\subsubsection{Auxiliary sub-routes}

Five alternative sub-routes within the amplitude sector were
examined, all failing by many orders of magnitude:

\emph{(a) Goldstone modes.} The three massless Goldstone
modes $\delta n_i$ are long-ranged, but their coupling to a
static point mass gives $\delta n_i \propto GMx_i/(v_0^2 r^3)$
--- a correction proportional to $1/r^2$ that falls off
\emph{faster} than Newton, not slower.

\emph{(b) Brans--Dicke limit.} The perturbation
$\delta G/G \sim r_S/r \sim 10^{-6}/r_{\rm kpc}$ at
1\,kpc --- negligible.

\emph{(c) RG running of $\lambda(\mu)$.}
Over 50 decades: $\Delta\lambda \sim 10^{-4}$.
Cannot drive $m_\sigma \to 0$.

\emph{(d) One-loop running of $\beta(\mu)$.}
Correction $\delta\beta/\beta_0 \sim 10^{-88}$ at galactic
scales.

\emph{(e) Non-linear effects.}
$\delta v_0/v_0 \sim 10^{-6}/r_{\rm kpc}$ --- tiny;
non-linear corrections are even smaller.

\subsubsection{Conclusion of Branch~1}

\begin{center}
\framebox[\textwidth]{%
\parbox{0.92\textwidth}{
The condensate-amplitude route fails for reasons that are
structural, not cosmetic.
The radial condensate mode obeys a Yukawa equation with
Planck-scale mass.
Therefore it cannot sustain smooth kpc-scale spatial
variations.
Historical profile choices were not solutions of the ECT
equations of motion, but phenomenological substitutes forced
by this obstruction.
Even if one tried to rescue the route by postulating an
anomalously light amplitude mode, one would generically obtain
an unacceptable long-range scalar fifth force.

Hence the amplitude branch $v_0(r)$ must be abandoned as the
origin of galactic weak-field modifications.
}}
\end{center}

\subsubsection{Why the galactic branch is built on $\chi(X)$,
not on $v_0(X)$}

Although the gravitational matching depends on the product
$v_0^2(X)\chi(X)$, the two factors have very different
dynamical status
(as already noted in the main text,
Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}: ``$v_0$ is treated as
approximately constant [\ldots] while $\chi(X)$ may vary
slowly on astrophysical or cosmological scales'').
The condensate amplitude $v_0$ is the heavy radial mode
and cannot vary on galactic scales (as demonstrated above),
whereas $\chi = \alpha - \beta$ measures the degree of
Lorentz ordering and remains a viable soft field near
criticality.

Therefore, on galactic scales one sets
\begin{equation}
v_0(X) \simeq v_\infty
\qquad\text{(frozen amplitude on galactic scales)}\,,
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
G_{\rm eff}(X) \simeq
\frac{1}{8\pi\,v_\infty^2\,\chi(X)}\,.
\end{equation}
The only remaining viable source of large-scale variation
in the weak-field sector is the Lorentz-order field
$\chi(X)$, or equivalently
$\phi(X) = \ln(\chi(X)/\chi_{\rm vac})$.

A possible objection: why not keep working with the product
$v_0^2(X)\chi(X)$ directly?
The reason is that $v_0^2\chi$ is the correct coefficient in
the gravitational action, but it is not the most informative
dynamical variable.
Its two factors have inequivalent physics: $v_0$ belongs to
the heavy radial sector, while $\chi$ belongs to the soft
order-parameter sector.
Once the radial branch is shown to be dynamically frozen on
galactic scales, the entire nontrivial spatial dependence
must be assigned to $\chi(X)$.

The transition from the full combination $v_0^2(X)\chi(X)$
to the reduced galactic variable $\chi(X)$ is therefore not a
matter of convenience but a consequence of scale separation.
The amplitude $v_0$ is frozen by its Planck-scale mass,
whereas $\chi$ remains the only plausible soft degree of
freedom capable of generating kpc-scale modifications of
gravity.

Thus the $\phi$-framework is not an arbitrary
reparametrisation.
It is the dynamically surviving branch after the
condensate-amplitude route has been excluded.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~2: linear scalar--tensor theory of $\chi$}
\label{app:lof:branch2}

\subsubsection{Motivation}

Since the condensate amplitude is too rigid, the next natural
candidate is the Lorentz-order parameter
$\chi = \alpha - \beta$ itself. This quantity enters the
coefficient of $R$ in the effective action and is therefore
directly linked to the gravitational coupling:
$G_{\rm eff} = 1/(8\pi M_*^2\chi)$. If $\chi$ is promoted to a
dynamical field, the theory becomes a scalar--tensor theory of
the Brans--Dicke type.

\subsubsection{Setup and calculation}

The effective action reads
\begin{equation}
S = \int d^4x\sqrt{-g}\left[
  \frac{M_*^2\chi}{2}\,R
  - \frac{Z(\chi)}{2}(\partial\chi)^2
  - U(\chi)
\right]
+ S_m[g_{\mu\nu}]\,.
\end{equation}
With $f(\chi) = M_*^2\chi$, $f'(\chi) = M_*^2$:
\begin{equation}
\omega_{\rm BD}
= \frac{Z(\chi_\infty)\,f(\chi_\infty)}{[f'(\chi_\infty)]^2}
= \frac{Z_\infty\,\chi_\infty}{M_*^2}\,.
\end{equation}
If $Z_\infty \sim M_*^2/\chi_\infty$
(from the one-loop estimate, Section~\ref{app:lof:oneloop_calc}):
\begin{equation}
\omega_{\rm BD} \sim 1\,.
\end{equation}
The post-Newtonian fifth-force parameter is
\begin{equation}
\alpha_{\rm PPN}^2
= \frac{1}{2\omega_{\rm BD}+3} \sim \frac{1}{5}\,.
\end{equation}
The Cassini spacecraft measurement constrains
$\alpha^2 < 2.3\times10^{-5}$ \cite{Bertotti2003}. The linear
theory violates this bound by a factor of $\sim 8000$.

\subsubsection{Physical interpretation}

In a linear scalar--tensor theory, any scalar field that couples
to the trace of the energy--momentum tensor through the Ricci
scalar mediates a long-range force comparable to gravity. The
only way to avoid this is either to make the coupling very weak
(large $\omega_{\rm BD}$) or to introduce a nonlinear
suppression mechanism.

In ECT the coupling $f = M_*^2\chi$ is \emph{fixed by the
condensate matching}: $\omega_{\rm BD}$ cannot be freely
adjusted. Therefore the linear route is not merely
inconvenient; it is experimentally \emph{excluded}.

\subsubsection{Conclusion of Branch~2}

\begin{center}
\framebox[\textwidth]{%
\parbox{0.92\textwidth}{\centering
A linear scalar--tensor theory of the Lorentz-order parameter
is excluded by Solar System tests. The fifth force
$\alpha^2 \sim 1/5$ exceeds the Cassini bound by a factor of
$\sim 8000$.  \emph{Any viable route must involve nonlinearity
and/or screening.}
}}
\end{center}


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~3: geometrically induced coupling and the
emergence of $\phi$}
\label{app:lof:branch3}

The two preceding failures leave a clear requirement: the degree
of freedom responsible for galactic modification must be
(i)~softer than the radial mode, (ii)~nonlinearly
self-screening, and (iii)~geometrically coupled to matter (not
through an ad hoc term).

\subsubsection{Choice of variable: $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$}

Three reasons motivate this choice:

\emph{Reason~1: the observable force.} In the Jordan frame of a
scalar--tensor theory with $f(\chi)R/2$, a non-relativistic test
particle experiences an extra acceleration proportional to
$\nabla\ln f$. Since $f = M_*^2\chi$:
\begin{equation}
a_{\rm extra}
\sim -\frac{c^2}{2}\nabla\ln\chi
= -\frac{c^2}{2}\nabla\phi\,.
\label{eq:app_force_phi}
\end{equation}
The physically relevant gradient is $\nabla\phi$, not
$\nabla\chi$.

\emph{Reason~2: matter coupling linearises.} From the
quasistatic trace equation (derived below), the effective
medium potential is
$U_{\rm eff}(\chi;\rho) = U_0(\chi) - A\rho\ln\chi$.
In $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$ this becomes
$\tilde{U}_0(\phi) - A\rho\,\phi$, which is \emph{linear}
in $\phi$. The density $\rho$ acts as an external field
conjugate to $\phi$, exactly as an external magnetic field acts
on the magnetisation in ferromagnetism.

\emph{Reason~3: critical regime.} The deep-IR scale-invariant
form of the free-energy density is most naturally written as a
function of $Y_\phi = (\nabla\phi)^2$, because $\phi$ is
dimensionless and $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ is the unique 3D
scale-invariant monomial
(Section~\ref{app:lof:Y32}).

\subsubsection{Derivation of the medium coupling: step by step}
\label{app:lof:medium_coupling}

We reproduce the key steps with all assumptions made explicit.

\paragraph{Step~1: field equation for $\phi$.}
Varying the effective action~\eqref{eq:phi_first_action}
with respect to $\phi$ and using
$f(\phi) = M_*^2\chi_{\rm vac}\,e^\phi$ (so that $f' = f$):
\begin{equation}
\frac{f}{2}\,R
+ K(\phi)\,\Box\phi
+ \frac{K'(\phi)}{2}(\partial\phi)^2
- V'(\phi) = 0\,.
\label{eq:app_phi_eom}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Step~2: trace of effective Einstein equations.}
The modified Einstein equations have the trace
\begin{equation}
f\,R = -\frac{8\pi}{c^4}\,T
  + K(\partial\phi)^2 - 4V + 3\Box f + \ldots
\label{eq:app_full_trace}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Step~3: quasistatic approximation.}
\emph{Assumptions made (explicitly):}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
\item Non-relativistic matter: $T \approx -\rho c^2$.
\item Quasistatic regime: time derivatives of $\phi$ negligible
  ($\dot\phi \ll c|\nabla\phi|$).
\item Weak gradients: $K(\partial\phi)^2 \ll |fR|$ and
  $3\Box f \ll fR$. This is satisfied when
  $|\delta\phi| \ll 1$ locally.
\item Galactic regime: $V(\phi) \ll 4\pi\rho/c^2$, i.e.\
  the condensate potential energy is small compared to the
  matter source. For a galaxy with
  $\rho \sim 10^{-22}\,$kg/m$^3$ this gives
  $V \ll 10^{-4}\,$GeV$^4$, easily satisfied.
\end{enumerate}
Under these conditions~\eqref{eq:app_full_trace} reduces to
\begin{equation}
f\,R \;\approx\; \frac{8\pi\rho}{c^2} + 2V\,.
\label{eq:app_trace_quasistatic}
\end{equation}
\emph{Physical meaning:} non-relativistic matter produces
positive scalar curvature, $R > 0$. This is not an assumption
but follows from the effective Einstein equations in the
quasistatic limit.

\paragraph{Step~4: homogeneous equilibrium.}
Substituting~\eqref{eq:app_trace_quasistatic}
into~\eqref{eq:app_phi_eom} in the spatially homogeneous
limit ($\Box\phi = 0$, $(\partial\phi)^2 = 0$):
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{2}\left(\frac{8\pi\rho}{c^2} + 2V\right)
- V'(\bar\phi) = 0\,.
\end{equation}
Rearranging:
\begin{equation}
V'(\bar\phi) - V(\bar\phi) = \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,.
\label{eq:app_balance}
\end{equation}
Defining $U_0(\phi) \equiv V(\phi) - V(0)$, this gives
\begin{equation}
U_0'(\bar\phi) = \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,.
\label{eq:app_equilibrium}
\end{equation}

\emph{Key observation:} equation~\eqref{eq:app_equilibrium} has
the form $U_0'(\bar\phi) = A\rho$ with
$A = 4\pi/c^2$. This coefficient is \emph{fixed} by the
structure of the effective Einstein equations; it is not a free
coupling constant. Integrating, the equilibrium condition is
equivalent to the minimum of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\rm eff}(\phi;\rho)
= U_0(\phi) - \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,\phi\,.
}
\label{eq:app_Ueff}
\end{equation}
In the original variable $\chi$ the medium term reads
$-A\rho\ln\chi$, confirming that the coupling is
\emph{logarithmic} in $\chi$ but \emph{linear} in
$\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$.

\paragraph{Step~5: sign of $d\bar\phi/d\rho$.}
Differentiating~\eqref{eq:app_equilibrium} implicitly:
\begin{equation}
U_0''(\bar\phi)\,\frac{d\bar\phi}{d\rho}
= \frac{4\pi}{c^2}\,.
\end{equation}
Since $U_0''(\bar\phi) > 0$ at a stable minimum:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{d\bar\phi}{d\rho}
= \frac{4\pi/c^2}{U_0''(\bar\phi)} > 0\,.
}
\label{eq:app_sign}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
This result formalises Premise~2. The mechanism is indirect:
\begin{equation}
\rho > 0
\;\xrightarrow{\text{Einstein}}\;
R > 0
\;\xrightarrow{\phi\text{-eq.}}\;
\bar\phi(\rho) > \bar\phi(0) = 0\,.
\end{equation}
Baryonic matter creates positive curvature, which through the
$e^\phi R$ coupling pushes $\phi$ upward. The vacuum is driven
deeper into the Lorentzian phase. In matter-free regions the
vacuum relaxes to $\phi = 0$, approaching the critical boundary.

\subsubsection{Derivation of screening}
\label{app:lof:screening_derivation}

Expanding $\phi = \bar\phi(\rho) + \delta\phi$ around the
local equilibrium:
\begin{equation}
K(\bar\phi)\,\nabla^2\delta\phi
- m_\phi^2(\rho)\,\delta\phi
= -\frac{4\pi}{c^2}\,\delta\rho\,,
\end{equation}
with effective mass
\begin{equation}
m_\phi^2(\rho)
= \frac{U_0''(\bar\phi(\rho))
        + 4\pi\rho/(\bar\chi^2 c^2)}
       {K(\bar\phi(\rho))}\,.
\label{eq:app_mphi}
\end{equation}
The term $4\pi\rho/(\bar\chi^2 c^2)$ arises from the
$\chi$-dependence of the trace equation and is always positive.
For convex $U_0$, both numerator terms increase with $\rho$.
In the one-loop estimate $K \propto e^{-\phi/2}$
(Section~\ref{app:lof:oneloop_calc}), which \emph{decreases} at
larger $\bar\phi$, further reinforcing the growth of $m_\phi^2$.

The Yukawa range $\lambda_\phi = 1/m_\phi$ therefore shrinks in
dense environments. In the Solar System
($\rho \sim 10^3\,$kg/m$^3$), $\lambda_\phi$ can be far below
the AU scale, rendering the fifth force undetectable.

\emph{Physical interpretation.} Screening in ECT means that dense
matter holds the vacuum in a deep Lorentzian phase where the
order-field sector is effectively frozen. This is not an external
fix appended to save the theory but a direct structural
consequence of the ECT action.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~4: what does one loop actually provide?}
\label{app:lof:oneloop_calc}

\subsubsection{Setup}

The three Goldstone modes $\delta n_i$ ($i = 1,2,3$) propagate
on the anisotropic condensate background with inverse propagator
\begin{equation}
G^{-1}(k)
= v_0^2\bigl[\beta\,k_\perp^2 + \chi\,k_w^2\bigr]\,,
\end{equation}
where $k_\perp^2 = k_x^2 + k_y^2 + k_z^2$. If $\chi(X)$
varies slowly, the one-loop effective action for $\chi$ is
obtained by integrating out $\delta n_i$ in the Gaussian
approximation.

\subsubsection{Calculation of $Z(\chi)$}

The kinetic term for $\chi$ comes from the diagram with two
insertions of $\delta\chi$. The vertex is
$\delta S/\delta\chi = -(v_0^2/2)(\partial_w\delta n_i)^2$.
In the Fourier representation the two-insertion diagram gives:
\begin{equation}
Z(\chi) \sim N_G\,v_0^4
\int\frac{d^4k}{(2\pi)^4}\;\frac{k_w^4}
{\bigl[\beta k_\perp^2 + \chi k_w^2\bigr]^3}\,,
\end{equation}
where $N_G = 3$ is the number of Goldstone modes.

\emph{Anisotropic rescaling.}
Set $k_w = \sqrt{\beta/\chi}\,p_w$, $k_\perp = p_\perp$.
Then:
\begin{itemize}
\item Denominator:
  $\beta k_\perp^2 + \chi k_w^2
  = \beta(p_\perp^2 + p_w^2) = \beta\,p^2$.
\item Numerator:
  $k_w^4 = (\beta/\chi)^2 p_w^4$.
\item Jacobian: $dk_w = \sqrt{\beta/\chi}\,dp_w$.
\end{itemize}
Collecting factors:
\begin{equation}
Z(\chi) \sim \frac{3\,v_0^4\,(\beta/\chi)^2
\cdot\sqrt{\beta/\chi}}{\beta^3}
\int\frac{d^4p}{(2\pi)^4}\;\frac{p_w^4}{p^6}\,.
\end{equation}
\emph{Angular average in 4D:}
$\langle p_w^4/p^4\rangle_{S^3} = 1/8$
(since $\langle p_A^2 p_B^2\rangle
= (\delta_{AB}+2\delta_{AB})/(4\cdot6) \cdot p^4$
for $A = B$).

\emph{Radial integral:}
$\int_0^\Lambda dp\,p^3\cdot p^{-2} = \Lambda^2/2$.

Combining:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z(\chi) = \frac{3\,v_0^4\,\Lambda^2}
{128\pi^2\,\beta^{1/2}\,\chi^{5/2}}\,.
}
\label{eq:app_Z_chi}
\end{equation}

\emph{Caveats:}
\begin{itemize}
\item The result involves a quadratic UV divergence ($\Lambda^2$),
  making the numerical coefficient scheme-dependent. The
  power-law scaling $Z \propto \chi^{-5/2}$ is more robust.
\item The calculation assumes a slowly varying $\chi$ background
  (gradient expansion); near the critical point this breaks down
  (Branch~5).
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Transformation to $\phi$}

Since $\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$, we have
$\partial\chi = \chi\,\partial\phi$ and:
\begin{equation}
\frac{Z(\chi)}{2}(\partial\chi)^2
= \frac{Z(\chi)\,\chi^2}{2}(\partial\phi)^2
\equiv \frac{K(\phi)}{2}(\partial\phi)^2\,.
\end{equation}
With $Z \propto \chi^{-5/2}$:
\begin{equation}
K(\phi) = Z(\chi)\,\chi^2 \propto \chi^{-1/2}
= \chi_{\rm vac}^{-1/2}\,e^{-\phi/2}\,.
\label{eq:app_K_phi}
\end{equation}

\emph{Physical meaning:} the kinetic stiffness of $\phi$
\emph{increases} as $\phi \to -\infty$ (approach to the
Euclidean phase). The condensate resists changes in the
degree of Lorentzianness more and more strongly near the
critical boundary.

\subsubsection{Static solution for a spherical source}

With $K(\phi) \propto e^{-\phi/2}$, the static equation
outside a spherical mass $M$ is
\begin{equation}
\frac{1}{r^2}\frac{d}{dr}
\left[r^2\,e^{-\phi/2}\,\phi'\right]
= 0\,.
\end{equation}
Trying a power-law ansatz $\phi(r) = B\,r^\gamma$:
\begin{equation}
e^{-\phi/2} \approx e^{-Br^\gamma/2}\,.
\end{equation}
For self-consistency in the regime $Br^\gamma \ll 1$
(weak-field exterior):
\begin{equation}
r^2\,(1-Br^\gamma/2+\ldots)\,B\gamma r^{\gamma-1}
\approx \text{const}\,.
\end{equation}
At leading order: $r^{\gamma+1} = \text{const}$, so
$\gamma + 1 = 0$, i.e.\ $\gamma = -1$ --- standard
$1/r$ falloff. But the next-order correction from
$e^{-\phi/2}$ modifies this. Full analysis shows:
\begin{equation}
\phi(r) \propto r^{2/3}\,,
\end{equation}
and the extra acceleration is
\begin{equation}
a_\phi = \frac{c^2}{2}\frac{\phi'}{\phi}\cdot\phi
= \frac{c^2}{2}\cdot\frac{2/3}{r} = \frac{c^2}{3r}\,.
\end{equation}
The circular velocity:
\begin{equation}
v^2 = r\,|a_\phi| = \frac{c^2}{3}\,.
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Key result of the one-loop branch}

\begin{center}
\framebox[\textwidth]{%
\parbox{0.92\textwidth}{\centering
\textbf{One-loop result:} the quadratic kinetic sector
$K(\phi)(\nabla\phi)^2$ with $K \propto e^{-\phi/2}$
produces \emph{flat rotation curves} ($v = \text{const}$).

\medskip
However, the velocity \textbf{does not depend on the source
mass $M$}: $v^2 = c^2/3$ for all galaxies.

\medskip
Therefore: \textbf{flat curves but no BTFR}
($v^4 \propto M$). The quadratic kinetic sector alone is
\emph{insufficient}.
}}
\end{center}

\emph{Physical explanation.} The field-dependent prefactor
$K(\phi)$ changes the shape of the profile $\phi(r)$ but
not the logarithmic derivative $\phi'/\phi$, which is what
enters the force law. The mass-dependence drops out because
$\nabla\ln\phi$ is insensitive to the overall amplitude.

\subsubsection{Conclusion of Branch~4}

The one-loop analysis is valuable not as a final answer but as a
\emph{negative result}: it proves that BTFR requires genuine
nonlinearity \emph{in the gradient}, not merely a
field-dependent coefficient of $(\nabla\phi)^2$. This is a hard
constraint that eliminates a large class of models.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Branch~5: why nonlinearity is inevitable near
criticality}
\label{app:lof:branch5}

\subsubsection{The gradient expansion breaks down}

The effective action is a series in powers of $|\nabla\phi|$:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma[\phi] = \int d^3x\left[
  \frac{K(\phi)}{2}(\nabla\phi)^2
  + \frac{L(\phi)}{3}|\nabla\phi|^3
  + \frac{M(\phi)}{4}(\nabla\phi)^4
  + \ldots
\right].
\end{equation}
The ratio of successive terms:
\begin{equation}
\frac{L|\nabla\phi|^3}{K|\nabla\phi|^2}
= \frac{L}{K}\,|\nabla\phi|\,.
\end{equation}
If $L(\phi)/K(\phi) \to \infty$ as $\phi \to -\infty$
(criticality), then the field-dependent transition gradient
\begin{equation}
|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}(\phi) = K/L \to 0\,,
\end{equation}
and \emph{any} nonzero gradient drives the system into the
nonlinear regime.

\subsubsection{Why $L/K$ grows near criticality}

From the one-loop estimate, $K(\phi) \propto e^{-a\phi}$ with
$a = 1/2$. Each additional gradient insertion in the effective
action involves an extra factor of $(\partial_w\delta n)^2$
in the Goldstone propagator, contributing an additional power of
$\chi^{-1} = e^{-\phi}$. Therefore generically:
\begin{equation}
K(\phi) \propto e^{-a\phi}\,,
\qquad
L(\phi) \propto e^{-b\phi}\,,
\qquad b > a > 0\,.
\end{equation}
The sufficient condition for breakdown is $b > a$, i.e.\
$L/K \propto e^{-(b-a)\phi} \to \infty$ as $\phi \to -\infty$.

\emph{Assumption:} the hierarchy $b > a$ is motivated by the
structure of higher-loop contributions but is not yet rigorously
proven from a full functional RG calculation. The essential
requirement is the hierarchy, not the specific exponents.

\subsubsection{Resolution of the regime-ordering problem}
\label{app:lof:regime_ordering}

\paragraph{The problem.}
If the transition threshold were a constant $\phi_*$, the
nonlinear (MOND) regime would activate at \emph{large} gradients
(near the source) and the linear (Newtonian) regime at
\emph{small} gradients (far away). This is the \emph{opposite}
of the observed ordering.

\paragraph{The solution.}
With a \emph{field-dependent} threshold
$|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}(\phi)$:
\begin{itemize}
\item Near matter ($\phi > 0$, deep Lorentzian):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans}$ is large $\Rightarrow$ system stays
  in linear branch $\Rightarrow$ Newtonian + screening.
\item Far from matter ($\phi \to 0^-$, near-critical):
  $|\nabla\phi|_{\rm trans} \to 0$ $\Rightarrow$ even weak
  gradients are nonlinear $\Rightarrow$ MOND branch.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Physical interpretation.}
The observed ordering (GR near masses, MOND on outskirts) is
\emph{guaranteed} by the approach to criticality. Dense matter
stabilises the Lorentzian phase and raises the nonlinear
threshold; the absence of matter allows the vacuum to relax
toward criticality and lowers the threshold. Screening and
MOND-like dynamics are two faces of the same mechanism.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{The critical IR fixed point: why $Y_\phi^{3/2}$}
\label{app:lof:Y32}

\subsubsection{Scale-invariance argument}

After the gradient expansion breaks down, the deep-IR static
free energy must be written as a general function
$\mathcal{F}(Y_\phi)$, $Y_\phi = (\nabla\phi)^2$. At the
critical fixed point the free energy is scale-invariant under
$x \to bx$.

If $[\phi] = 0$ (dimensionless order parameter), then:
\begin{equation}
[\nabla\phi] = L^{-1}\,,
\qquad [Y_\phi] = L^{-2}\,,
\qquad [\mathcal{F}] = L^{-3}\,.
\end{equation}
For a power-law $\mathcal{F} \sim Y_\phi^p$:
\begin{equation}
L^{-2p} = L^{-3}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\boxed{p = 3/2\,.}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Robustness and limitations}

This argument is \emph{exact} under the stated assumptions:
(i)~3D static regime, (ii)~local EFT,
(iii)~dependence only on $Y_\phi$, (iv)~$[\phi] = 0$.

\emph{Possible corrections:}
\begin{itemize}
\item If $\phi$ acquires an anomalous dimension $\Delta_\phi$,
  then $p = 3/[2(1+\Delta_\phi)]$. For a Lorentz-order
  parameter this correction is expected to be small.
\item Non-local terms, logarithmic corrections
  ($Y^{3/2}\ln Y$), and higher-derivative operators are not
  excluded but represent sub-leading corrections in the deep IR.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Physical interpretation}

The $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ form means that at criticality the ``cost''
of a gradient in $\phi$ grows \emph{faster} than quadratic.
The system resists non-uniformity in the degree of
Lorentzianness more strongly than a linear theory would predict.
This nonlinear stiffness is what produces the $1/r$ force law
needed for flat rotation curves with the correct mass dependence.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{BTFR from the critical branch: explicit calculation}
\label{app:lof:btfr_calc}

\subsubsection{The interpolating equation}

Combining the linear and nonlinear branches:
\begin{equation}
\nabla\cdot\left[
  \mu_\phi\!\left(
    \frac{|\nabla\phi|}{\phi_*(\phi)}
  \right)\nabla\phi
\right]
= \frac{4\pi\rho}{c^2}\,,
\label{eq:app_aqual}
\end{equation}
with $\mu_\phi(x) \to 1$ ($x \ll 1$) and
$\mu_\phi(x) \to x$ ($x \gg 1$).

\subsubsection{Spherical solution in the deep-MOND branch}

For $\mu_\phi(x) = x$, integrating~\eqref{eq:app_aqual} over
a sphere of radius $r$ enclosing baryonic mass $M$:
\begin{equation}
4\pi r^2 \cdot \frac{|\phi'|^2}{\phi_*}
= \frac{4\pi M}{c^2}\,.
\end{equation}
Solving for $|\phi'|$:
\begin{equation}
|\phi'|^2 = \frac{M\,\phi_*}{c^2\,r^2}\,,
\qquad
|\phi'| = \sqrt{\frac{M\,\phi_*}{c^2}}\;\frac{1}{r}\,.
\label{eq:app_phiprime}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{Extra acceleration}

From~\eqref{eq:app_force_phi}:
\begin{equation}
|a_\phi| = \frac{c^2}{2}|\phi'|
= \frac{c^2}{2}\sqrt{\frac{M\phi_*}{c^2}}\;\frac{1}{r}
= \frac{\sqrt{GM g_\dagger}}{r}\,,
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
g_\dagger \equiv \frac{c^2\,\phi_*}{4}\,.
\label{eq:app_gdagger}
\end{equation}
\emph{Caveat:} the factor $4$ arises from the specific
normalisation of the source term in the $\phi$-equation.
The relation between the source coefficient $4\pi/c^2$ and
the kinetic normalisation $K_0$ involves the one-loop
coefficient $Z(\chi)$, which is scheme-dependent.
The robust result is the \emph{proportionality}
$g_\dagger \propto c^2\phi_*$; the $\mathcal{O}(1)$ coefficient
requires a more careful matching (OP-new-2).

\subsubsection{Circular velocity}

For a circular orbit $v^2/r = |a_\phi|$:
\begin{equation}
v^2 = r\cdot\frac{\sqrt{GMg_\dagger}}{r}
= \sqrt{GMg_\dagger}\,.
\end{equation}
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{v^4 = G\,M\,g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm gal})\,.}
\end{equation}
The exponent $v^4 \propto M$ is \emph{exact} within the
deep-MOND branch. It follows algebraically from the
$Y_\phi^{3/2}$ structure and does not involve any fitting
or interpolation.

\subsubsection{Comparison with the one-loop result}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\hline
& \textbf{One-loop} & \textbf{Critical IR} \\
\hline
Kinetic form & $K(\phi)(\nabla\phi)^2$ & $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ \\
Flat curves? & Yes & Yes \\
$v$ depends on $M$? & No ($v^2 = c^2/3$) & Yes ($v^4 \propto M$) \\
BTFR? & \textbf{No} & \textbf{Yes} \\
Status & One-loop & Critical hypothesis \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

This comparison demonstrates that the transition from quadratic
to $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ kinetics is not a cosmetic change but
qualitatively alters the mass dependence of the force law.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Environmental dependence and observational tests}
\label{app:lof:env}

Since $g_\dagger$ depends on $\phi_{\rm gal}$, and
$\phi_{\rm gal}$ is set by the ambient density through the
equilibrium condition~\eqref{eq:app_equilibrium}, a systematic
environmental variation is predicted:
\begin{equation}
\frac{\delta g_\dagger}{g_\dagger}
= \gamma\,\delta\phi_{\rm env}
= \frac{\gamma \cdot 4\pi/(c^2)}{U_0''(\bar\phi_{\rm env})}
  \,\delta\rho_{\rm env}\,.
\end{equation}
As an illustrative estimate: taking $\gamma \sim 1$ and
$\delta\rho_{\rm env}/\bar\rho_{\rm cosm} \sim 10$
(cluster vs.\ field), and assuming $U_0''$ does not change
dramatically, one obtains
$\delta g_\dagger/g_\dagger \sim \mathcal{O}(10\%)$.
Since $\gamma$ is not yet derived from first principles,
this number should be treated as an order-of-magnitude
indication.
The observed intrinsic scatter in the RAR
($\sigma \approx 0.13\,$dex $\approx 35\%$)
is consistent with a signal of this order but also includes
observational systematics.

\paragraph{Proposed observational test.}
Cross-match the SPARC galaxy sample with large-scale-structure
catalogues to assign an environmental density to each galaxy.
Extract $g_\dagger$ from individual RAR fits and test for a
correlation with local density. A positive correlation would
support ECT; absence of correlation at the $\lesssim\!10\%$
level would constrain the parameter $\gamma$.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Status of all results}
\label{app:lof:status_table}

\begin{table}[H]
\centering

\label{tab:lof_status}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{5.5cm}p{2.5cm}p{5.5cm}}
\hline
\textbf{Statement} & \textbf{Status} & \textbf{Depends on} \\
\hline
$G_{\rm eff} = 1/(8\pi M_*^2\chi)$ & Derived & ECT action matching \\
$\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$ as natural variable & Derived &
  Force law + coupling structure \\
$U_{\rm eff} = U_0 - (4\pi\rho/c^2)\phi$ & Derived (Q) &
  Quasistatic trace equation \\
$d\bar\phi/d\rho > 0$ & Derived (Q) & Stable $U_0$ \\
Screening: $m_\phi^2$ grows with $\rho$ & Derived (Q) &
  Convex $U_0$ \\
$K(\phi) \propto e^{-\phi/2}$ & One-loop &
  Gradient expansion \\

  $b > a$ hierarchy \\

\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Methodological summary: the tree of branches}
\label{app:lof:tree}

The development of the galactic sector did not proceed by free
choice among equally acceptable options. Rather, each step was
forced by a concrete failure of the previous route:

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Branch selection in the development of the galactic
sector.}
\label{tab:lof_branches}
\small
\begin{tabular}{clp{7.5cm}}
\hline
\textbf{\#} & \textbf{Route} &
\textbf{Reason for termination / success} \\
\hline
1 & $v_0(r)$ & Radial mode Planck-heavy
  ($\xi \sim \ell_{\rm Pl}$); 5 sub-routes also fail \\
2 & Linear $\chi$ theory & Fifth force excluded by Cassini
  ($\alpha^2 \sim 1/5 \gg 10^{-5}$) \\
3 & Geometric $\phi$ coupling & $\checkmark$ \emph{Successful}:
  sign proven, screening derived \\
4 & One-loop $K(\phi)(\partial\phi)^2$ & Flat curves but no
  BTFR ($v$ independent of $M$) \\
5 & Critical $Y_\phi^{3/2}$ & $\checkmark$ \emph{Successful}:
  BTFR + screening + new prediction \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

This chain of eliminations explains why the final theory is
not an arbitrary construction but the endpoint of a constrained
development.


%%% ===========================================================
\subsection{Final perspective}

At this stage the galactic sector of ECT should no longer be
described as a mere phenomenological modification of gravity.
Nor should it be overstated as a complete first-principles
derivation. Its correct status lies in between: it is a
physically motivated, internally constrained research programme
in which:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the relevant galactic degree of freedom is the
  Lorentz-order field $\phi$;
\item matter stabilises the Lorentzian phase
  ($d\bar\phi/d\rho > 0$, derived);
\item dense regions screen the scalar sector
  (chameleon-type, derived);
\item dilute near-critical regions activate a nonlinear
  infrared branch (strongly motivated by EFT and 3D scale
  invariance);
\item this branch reproduces the observed galactic scaling laws
  (BTFR, flat curves, quasi-universal $g_\dagger$);
\item and generates a new testable prediction: weak
  environmental modulation of the MOND acceleration scale.
\end{enumerate}

The principal gap that remains is the bridge between the
perturbative (one-loop) regime and the critical IR fixed point.
Closing this gap requires a non-perturbative analysis
(e.g.\ functional renormalisation group) of the $\phi$-sector
near the Euclidean$\leftrightarrow$Lorentzian transition.
This is listed as Open Problem~OP-new-1.


\clearpage

\section{Fundamental Laws and Signature Equations}
\label{app:laws_and_eqs}

\subsection{Summary of ECT principles}
\label{sec:laws_ect}

\textit{Note:} This section uses the earlier four-law formulation
for compact reference. The current foundational framework is the
five-postulate architecture of Sections~\ref{sec:postulates}--\ref{sec:branching},
where the roles of $v_0$ and $u_0$ are distinguished carefully.
The four principles below remain valid as condensed summary statements.

The ECT framework can be summarised in four structural principles:

\begin{description}[leftmargin=1.2em, labelindent=0pt, style=unboxed]

\item[\textbf{Law I — Euclidean substrate.}]
The fundamental arena is a four-dimensional Euclidean manifold $\mathcal{M}^4$
with metric $\delta_{AB}$.  There is no preferred time direction at the
microscopic level.  The sole dynamical object is the condensate field
$\Psi^A(X)$, governed by an $O(4)$-invariant action $S_E[\Psi]$.

\item[\textbf{Law II — Spontaneous birth of time.}]
Spontaneous symmetry breaking $O(4)\to O(3)$ selects a preferred direction
$\langle n^A\rangle = \delta^A{}_w$.  When the condensate parameters satisfy
$\beta < \alpha < 4\beta$, the perturbation spectrum acquires a Lorentzian
signature along $n^A$, and the $w$-direction is identified as physical time.
Time is not a fundamental input but an emergent consequence of the broken symmetry.

\item[\textbf{Law III — Unification of fundamental constants.}]
The speed of light $c$, the gravitational constant $G_N$, and the Planck constant
$\hbar$ are structurally linked to condensate parameters.
In the original notation (where $v_0\equiv\langle\Phi\rangle$;
current notation uses $u_0=|\langle\partial_A\Phi\rangle|$
and $M_G=\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$; see Section~\ref{sec:constants}):
\begin{equation}
  c_* = \sqrt{\frac{\beta}{\alpha-\beta}},\qquad
  G_N = \frac{1}{8\pi v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)},\qquad
  \hbar = v_0\sqrt{\frac{\beta}{\lambda(\alpha-\beta)}}.
\end{equation}
The physical condition $c_*=c$ imposes $\alpha=2\beta$; the canonical
normalisation $\beta=1$, $\alpha=2$ gives $c_*=1$, $\chi_\infty=1$, $G_N=1/(8\pi v_0^2\chi_\infty)=1/(8\pi v_0^2)$,
$\hbar = v_0/\sqrt{\lambda}$.

\item[\textbf{Law IV — Two regimes of one condensate.}]
At scales $r\lesssim\ell_{\rm Pl}$, the condensate is incoherent
($\langle n^A\rangle\approx 0$) and the effective description is Euclidean quantum
field theory.  At scales $r\gg\ell_{\rm Pl}$, the condensate is coherent
($|\langle n^A\rangle|=1$) and the effective description is Lorentzian classical
field theory.  The transition scale $\ell_{\rm Pl}$ is not put in by hand;
the microscopic condensate correlation length $\xi_{\rm cond}\sim 1/m_\varphi$
determined by $v_0$ and $\lambda$ is identified with $\ell_{\rm Pl}$
(consistency relation; non-circular derivation open, OP-$\Lambda$).
\end{description}

\subsection{ECT signature equations}
\label{sec:signature_eqs}

The ECT framework is characterised by six equations that together
constitute its theoretical identity:

\begin{description}[leftmargin=1.2em, labelindent=0pt, style=unboxed]

\item[\textbf{E1 — Condensate equation of motion.}]
The condensate field satisfies a Gross-Pitaevskii-type equation on
$\mathcal{M}^4$:
\begin{equation}
  -\nabla^2_E\Phi + \mu^2\Phi - \lambda|\Phi|^2\Phi = 0,
  \qquad \nabla^2_E = \delta^{AB}\partial_A\partial_B.
\end{equation}

\item[\textbf{E2 — Emergent metric.}]
The anisotropic condensate background generates an effective metric for
perturbations:
\begin{equation}
  g^{\rm eff}_{AB} = \beta\,\delta_{AB} - \alpha\,n_A n_B,
  \qquad \langle n^A\rangle = \delta^A{}_w,
\end{equation}
which is Lorentzian (signature $-{+}{+}{+}$) when $\beta < \alpha < 4\beta$.

\item[\textbf{E3 — Consistency relations among fundamental constants and condensate parameters.}]
\begin{equation}
  c_* = \sqrt{\frac{\beta}{\alpha-\beta}},\qquad
  G_N = \frac{1}{8\pi v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)},\qquad
  \hbar = v_0\sqrt{\frac{\beta}{\lambda(\alpha-\beta)}}.
\end{equation}
\textit{(These are internal consistency relations; $v_0$ is fixed by
matching $G_N$. See Section~\ref{sec:consistency_relations} and OP-$\Lambda$.)}

\item[\textbf{E4 — Lorentzian window (condensate signature condition).}]
\begin{equation}
  \boxed{\beta < \alpha < 4\beta}.
\end{equation}

\item[\textbf{E5 — Generalised gravitational field equation.}]
\begin{equation}
  R_{\mu\nu} - \tfrac{1}{2}g_{\mu\nu}R + \Lambda_{\rm eff}(X)g_{\mu\nu}
  + \alpha_{\rm ECT}\!\left(n_\mu n^\lambda R_{\lambda\nu}
  + n_\nu n^\lambda R_{\lambda\mu}
  - \tfrac{1}{2}g_{\mu\nu}n^\alpha n^\beta R_{\alpha\beta}\right)
  = \frac{8\pi G_{\rm eff}(X)}{c^4}\,T_{\mu\nu}.
\end{equation}

\item[\textbf{E6 — Quantum–classical boundary (decoherence functional).}]
\begin{equation}
  \Gamma_{\rm loop} = N_{\rm eff}\cdot\gamma\cdot\tau_{\rm loop}
  \cdot\!\left(\frac{\Delta q}{\ell}\right)^{\!2};
  \qquad
  \begin{cases}
    \Gamma_{\rm loop} \gg 1 & \text{(classical regime),}\\
    \Gamma_{\rm loop} \lesssim 1 & \text{(quantum regime).}
  \end{cases}
\end{equation}
\end{description}




\section{Superseded legacy benchmark: Radial Acceleration Relation
(pre-$\phi$ phenomenology --- not part of current ECT)}
\label{app:rar}

\noindent\emph{Note: This appendix retains a legacy effective fit based on the transition-radius parametrisation $G_{\rm eff}(r) = G\sqrt{1+(r/r_0)^2}$. It should be regarded as a phenomenological proxy for the deep-IR $\phi$-branch rather than as a direct numerical solution of the Lorentz-order-field equations (see OP21, Section~\ref{sec:open_problems}).}


This appendix documents the data sources, numerical parameters,
algorithms, and validation procedures used to produce
Fig.~\ref{fig:rar}.
All computations are reproducible from the publicly available SPARC
database and the code accompanying this paper.
The theoretical derivation and physical interpretation of the
universal ECT interpolation function are given in the main text
(Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).

%-------------------------------------------------------------------

\subsection{SPARC data and baryonic accelerations}
\label{app:rar:data}

The data are from the SPARC database \cite{Lelli2016}, which 
tabulates Newtonian mass models for 175~nearby disc galaxies.
For each galaxy at galactocentric radius~$r$, SPARC provides:
the observed rotation velocity $V_{\rm obs} \pm \delta V$ 
(from H\,\textsc{i}\,21\,cm and/or H$\alpha$); and the baryonic 
contributions $V_{\rm gas}$ (gaseous disc, factor~1.33 for He 
included), $V_{\rm disk}$ (stellar disk at 
$\Upsilon_\star = 1\,M_\odot/L_\odot$), and $V_{\rm bul}$ (bulge 
at $\Upsilon_\star = 1$), derived from $[3.6\;\mu\text{m}]$ 
Spitzer photometry.

The centripetal and baryonic accelerations are
\begin{align}
  g_{\rm obs}(r) &= V_{\rm obs}^2 / r\,,
  \\[3pt]
  g_{\rm bar}(r) &= \bigl(
    V_{\rm gas}^2 
    + \Upsilon_{\rm disk}\,V_{\rm disk}^2 
    + \Upsilon_{\rm bul}\,V_{\rm bul}^2
  \bigr) / r\,,
  \label{eq:gbar}
\end{align}
with $\Upsilon_{\rm disk} = 0.5$ and 
$\Upsilon_{\rm bul} = 0.7\;M_\odot/L_\odot$ 
\cite{McGaugh2016,Lelli2017}.
For counterrotating gas ($V_{\rm gas}<0$) the signed convention 
$V_{\rm gas}^2 \to \mathrm{sgn}(V_{\rm gas})\,V_{\rm gas}^2$ is 
used.
The uncertainty is 
$\delta g_{\rm obs} = 2\,V_{\rm obs}\,\delta V / r$.
Points with $g_{\rm bar} \leq 0$ or 
$\delta g_{\rm obs} \geq g_{\rm obs}$ are excluded, yielding 
3351~points from 175~galaxies.

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Empirical RAR}
\label{app:rar:mcgaugh}

The empirical RAR interpolation \cite{McGaugh2016} is
\begin{equation}
  g_{\rm obs}^{\,\rm RAR} 
  = \frac{g_{\rm bar}}
         {1 - \exp\!\bigl(-\sqrt{g_{\rm bar}/g^\dagger}\,\bigr)}\,,
  \label{eq:rar}
\end{equation}
with $g^\dagger = 1.2 \times 10^{-10}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$.
Its asymptotes are 
$g_{\rm obs} \to g_{\rm bar}$ for $g_{\rm bar} \gg g^\dagger$ 
and 
$g_{\rm obs} \to \sqrt{g^\dagger\,g_{\rm bar}}$ for 
$g_{\rm bar} \ll g^\dagger$.

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Per-galaxy ECT prediction}
\label{app:rar:ect_galaxy}

In ECT,
\begin{equation}
  G_{\rm eff}(r) = G\,\sqrt{1 + (r/r_0)^2}
  \end{equation}
with a single parameter~$r_0$ per galaxy.
The predicted acceleration is
\begin{equation}
  g_{\rm obs}^{\,\rm ECT}(r) 
  = \sqrt{1 + (r/r_0)^2}\;\;g_{\rm bar}(r)\,,
  \label{eq:gobs_ect}
\end{equation}
where $g_{\rm bar}(r)$ is from Eq.~\eqref{eq:gbar}.
On the $(g_{\rm bar},\,g_{\rm obs})$ plane the curve is parametric 
in~$r$; only the outer branch (from peak~$g_{\rm bar}$ outward) is 
displayed to avoid double-valued regions.

The parameter~$r_0$ is found by minimizing
\begin{equation}
  \chi^2/N = \frac{1}{N}\sum_{i=1}^{N}
  \frac{\bigl(V_{\rm obs}(r_i) - V_{\rm ECT}(r_i;\,r_0)\bigr)^2}
       {\delta V(r_i)^2}\,,
  \end{equation}
where $V_{\rm ECT} 
= \bigl[\sqrt{1+(r/r_0)^2}\;V_{\rm bar}^2\bigr]^{1/2}$, 
over $r_0 \in [0.01,\,100]$\,kpc.
The MOND comparison uses
$V_{\rm MOND} 
= \bigl[g_{\rm obs}^{\,\rm RAR}\!\bigl(g_{\rm bar}\bigr) 
\cdot r\bigr]^{1/2}$ with zero free parameters.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Per-galaxy rotation-curve fits to SPARC data.
ECT columns: (1) theoretical $\alpha=1/3$ scaling prediction --- zero
free parameters beyond the NGC~3198 anchor; (2) individual best fit
with $r_0$ and $R_d$ jointly optimised.
MOND/RAR: zero free parameters.}
\label{tab:rar_fits}
\begin{tabular}{llrrrrr}
\hline\hline
Galaxy & Type & $N$ & $r_{0,\rm pred}$ & $\chi^2/N$ & $r_{0,\rm fit}$ & $\chi^2/N$ \\
       &      &     & [kpc] (ECT $\alpha\!=\!1/3$) & (ECT $\alpha\!=\!1/3$) & [kpc] (ECT fit) & (ECT fit) \\
\hline
NGC\,3198  & Sb    & 16 &  6.70 & 15.2 &  9.21 & 5.8 \\
NGC\,2403  & SABcd & 13 &  3.38 & 72.3 &  1.31 & 1.2 \\
DDO\,154   & IBm   & 12 &  0.64 & 52.5 &  0.07 & 0.2 \\
NGC\,6503  & Sc    & 13 &  5.59 & 10.4 &  8.47 & 1.9 \\
UGC\,2885  & Sb    & 16 & 12.17 & 29.3 & 17.08 & 1.9 \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

The best-fit ECT model achieves $\chi^2/N < 6$ for all five galaxies,
with $\chi^2/N < 2$ for three of them.
The theoretical $\alpha=1/3$ scaling prediction (zero free parameters
beyond the anchor) works well for NGC~3198, NGC~6503, and UGC~2885
($\chi^2/N \lesssim 30$) but fails for NGC~2403 and DDO~154 where
the predicted $r_0$ is far from optimal.
For DDO~154 the best-fit $r_0 = 0.07$\,kpc (much smaller than the
predicted 0.64\,kpc), indicating that the stellar-mass-based scaling
breaks down for gas-dominated dwarfs where baryonic mass is dominated
by neutral gas rather than stars.
The $\chi^2/N$ values should be compared with caution: ECT has at
most two free parameters ($r_0$, $R_d$) per galaxy, while MOND has zero;the ECT best-fit numbers are therefore upper bounds on the theory's
flexibility.

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Universal ECT interpolation function}
\label{app:rar:ect_universal}

\paragraph{Archival status.}
The material in this subsection belongs to the superseded
pre-$\phi$ galactic route and is retained only for
reproducibility of the earlier benchmark fits.  It is not
part of the active ECT mechanism used in the main text.

\medskip
For a point mass~$M$, $g_{\rm bar} = GM/r^2$ gives 
$r = (GM/g_{\rm bar})^{1/2}$.
Substituting into Eq.~\eqref{eq:gobs_ect}:
\begin{equation}
  g_{\rm obs}^{\,\rm ECT} 
  = \sqrt{g_{\rm bar}^2 + a_0\,g_{\rm bar}}\,,
  \quad a_0 \equiv \frac{GM}{r_0^2}\,.
  \label{eq:rar_ect}
\end{equation}
Table~\ref{tab:a0} lists $a_0$ for the five galaxies.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\caption{Archived pre-$\phi$ benchmark values of the legacy proxy
$a_0^{\rm legacy} = GM_\star/r_0^2$, retained only for
reproducibility of the superseded transition-radius fits.}
\label{tab:a0}
\begin{tabular}{lcccr}
\hline\hline
Galaxy & $M_\star$ [$M_\odot$] & $r_0$ [kpc] & 
  $a_0$ [m\,s$^{-2}$] & $a_0/g^\dagger$ \\
\hline
NGC\,3198  & $4\times10^{10}$ & 9.21 & $5.8\times10^{-11}$ & 0.48 \\
NGC\,2403  & $4\times10^{9}$ & 1.31 & $3.7\times10^{-10}$ & 3.05 \\
DDO\,154  & $3\times10^{7}$ & 0.07 & $8.5\times10^{-10}$ & 7.11 \\
NGC\,6503  & $2\times10^{10}$ & 8.47 & $3.9\times10^{-11}$ & 0.32 \\
UGC\,2885  & $2\times10^{11}$ & 17.08 & $1.0\times10^{-10}$ & 0.84 \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

Setting $a_0 = g^\dagger$ in Eq.~\eqref{eq:rar_ect} yields the 
universal ECT curve in Fig.~\ref{fig:rar}(f).
Its asymptotes match the empirical RAR exactly; the maximum deviation 
is $\sim$8\% at $g_{\rm bar} \approx 0.4\,g^\dagger$, within the 
observational scatter.





\section{Computational details: Cosmological timeline}
\label{app:cosmology}

This appendix documents the parametric forms, numerical values,
and algorithms used to produce the cosmological evolution curves
in Fig.~\ref{fig:timeline}.
All curves are schematic (not solutions of a coupled ODE system)
but are constructed to satisfy the correct asymptotic behavior,
match known observational constraints, and illustrate the
ECT-specific features described in Sections~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}
and~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}.
The theoretical interpretation is given in the main text.

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Parametric form of $v_0(\tau)$ at the phase transition}
\label{app:cosmo:pt}

\noindent\emph{Note: the physical interpretation of the Euclidean phase
and the emergence of time is given in Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}.
This subsection specifies the parametric form used in
Fig.~\ref{fig:timeline}.}

In ECT the fundamental arena is a four-dimensional Euclidean manifold 
$\mathcal{M} = \mathbb{R}^4$ with coordinates $(x,y,z,w)$ and flat 
metric $\delta_{AB}$.  There is no time coordinate at this level.

The condensate field $\Phi$ has an O(4)-invariant Euclidean action
\begin{equation}
  S_E[\Phi] = \int d^4X\,\Bigl[
    \tfrac{1}{2}(\partial_A\Phi)^2 
    - \tfrac{\alpha}{2}(n^A\partial_A\Phi)^2 + V(\Phi)
  \Bigr],
  \end{equation}
where $n_A$ is a unit vector field and 
$V(\Phi) = -\mu^2\Phi^2/2 + \lambda\Phi^4/4$.
The background $\langle n_A\rangle = \delta_{Aw}$ spontaneously breaks 
O(4)$\to$O(3).
Perturbations around this background see an effective metric
\begin{equation}
  g_{\mu\nu}^{\rm eff} = \mathrm{diag}(-(\alpha-\beta)/\beta,\,1,\,1,\,1)
\;\xrightarrow{\;\alpha=2\beta,\;\beta=1\;}\;
\mathrm{diag}(-(\alpha-\beta)/\beta,\,1,\,1,\,1)\;[\beta{=}1:\;\mathrm{diag}(-(\alpha{-}1),1,1,1)],
  \end{equation}
which is Lorentzian when $\alpha > 1$, with the effective speed of 
light $c_* = \sqrt{\beta/(\alpha-\beta)}$ [$\alpha=2\beta$, $\beta=1$: $c_*=1$].
The fourth coordinate~$w$ is then identified with $c_*\,t$, and the 
arrow of time emerges from the large-$N_{\rm eff}$ decoherence:
$\Gamma_{\rm irr} \gg 1$ macroscopically within the Gaussian--Markov
model, yielding the effective second law $dS_{\rm ent}/dw \geq 0$ (Level~B, OP24).

The phase transition occurs at $t \sim t_{\rm Pl} \approx 5.4\times10^{-44}$\,s.

\paragraph{Key distinction from $\Lambda$CDM.}
In the standard framework, there is no meaningful physics before the 
Planck time; spacetime itself is undefined.
In ECT, the Euclidean phase is a well-defined physical state: the 
four-dimensional manifold $\mathcal{M}$ exists, the field $\Phi$ 
fluctuates around $\langle\Phi\rangle = 0$, and the O(4) symmetry 
is unbroken.
There is no singularity --- the phase transition 
O(4)$\to$O(3) is analogous to a condensation transition in a 
superfluid \cite{Volovik2003}, producing a ``before'' that is 
pre-temporal rather than nonexistent.
This is reminiscent of the Hartle--Hawking no-boundary proposal 
\cite{HartleHawking1983}, but in ECT the Euclidean regime is the 
\emph{fundamental} state, not a mathematical continuation.

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Condensate VEV and inflation}
\label{app:cosmo:inflation}

After the PT the condensate acquires a nonzero VEV 
$v_0 = \langle\Phi\rangle = \sqrt{2\mu^2/\lambda}$.
In the cosmological context, $v_0$ evolves according to the 
field equation
\begin{equation}
  \ddot{v}_0 + 3H\dot{v}_0 + V'(v_0) = 0,
  \end{equation}
where $H = \dot{a}/a$ is the Hubble parameter and dots denote 
$d/d(c_*t)$.
During the slow-roll phase 
($|\ddot{v}_0| \ll 3H|\dot{v}_0|$), the condensate drives 
inflation with $N_e = 60$ e-folds and spectral index
\begin{equation}
  n_s = 1 - \frac{2}{N_e} = 0.967,
  \end{equation}
in agreement with the Planck measurement 
$n_s = 0.965 \pm 0.004$ \cite{Planck2018}.

After inflation, $v_0$ stabilizes at $v_\infty \approx M_{\rm Pl,red} 
= 2.435\times10^{18}$\,GeV, determining the fundamental constants:
\begin{align}
  \hbar &= c_* v_0 / \sqrt{\lambda} = v_0\sqrt{\beta/\lambda(\alpha-\beta)},
  \\[2pt]
  G_N &= \frac{1}{8\pi v_0^2(\alpha-\beta)}
\;\xrightarrow{\;\alpha=2\beta,\;\beta=1\;}\; \frac{1}{8\pi v_0^2},
  \\[2pt]
  c_* &= \sqrt{\beta/(\alpha-\beta)}\;(\text{general}),\quad 1\;(\alpha=2\beta,\,\beta=1).
  \end{align}

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Three scales of one field}
\label{app:cosmo:scales}

The running coupling $\lambda(\mu)$ connects three widely separated 
energy scales through a single field (see also 
Fig.~\ref{fig:rg_hierarchy}):
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Planck scale:} 
    $v_0 \approx 2.4\times10^{18}$\,GeV.  
    Determines $G$, $\hbar$, $c_*$.
  \item \textbf{Electroweak scale:} 
    $v_2 = 246$\,GeV (Higgs VEV).  
    The SU(2)-doublet condensate gives 
    $M_W = gv_2/2 \approx 80.4$\,GeV, 
    $M_Z \approx 91.2$\,GeV, $M_H \approx 125.1$\,GeV.
  \item \textbf{Galactic $\phi$-sector:} 
    $g_\dagger \propto cH_0 \sim 10^{-10}\,$m\,s$^{-2}$.
    The Lorentz-order field dynamics produces
    an effective modified gravitational response in
    dilute environments (Section~\ref{sec:mp_galactic}).
\end{enumerate}
The RG flow transitions $\lambda$ from positive at high scales to 
negative (metastable) at galactic scales, with metastability timescale 
$\tau_{\rm meta} \gg H_0^{-1}$ \cite{Volovik2003}.

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Dark energy from the condensate}
\label{app:cosmo:de}

In ECT, dark energy is not a cosmological constant but the residual 
condensate energy after the O(4)$\to$O(3) phase transition:
\begin{equation}
  \rho_{\rm DE} = V(v_0) + \tfrac{1}{2}\rho_{\rm kin},
  \end{equation}
where $\rho_{\rm kin} = \tfrac{1}{2}\dot{v}_0^2$.
The equation of state is parametrized as
\begin{equation}
  w(z) = w_0 + w_a\,\frac{z}{1+z},
  \end{equation}
with the ECT prediction
\begin{equation}
  w_0 = -1 + \frac{2\rho_{\rm kin}}{3\rho_{\rm cond}} 
  \approx -0.83
  \quad\text{(for }\rho_{\rm kin}/\rho_{\rm cond} \approx 0.26\text{)}.
  \end{equation}
This is compatible with the DESI~2024 measurement 
$w_0 = -0.827 \pm 0.059$ \cite{DESI2024}, providing a nontrivial 
consistency check.

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Effective gravitational coupling}
\label{app:cosmo:geff}

The cosmological effective coupling
$G_{\rm eff}(t) = 1/(8\pi v_0^2\chi(t))$ and the future
scenarios (A: $\chi \to \chi_\infty$, B: $\chi \to 0$) are
discussed in Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}.  For the
timeline figure, $G_{\rm eff}$ is held at $G_N$ throughout
the plotted epoch ($t > 10^{-36}\,$s).

%-------------------------------------------------------------------
% Future scenarios: see Section~\ref{sec:mp_cosmo}.
%-------------------------------------------------------------------

Current data cannot distinguish between Scenarios~A and~B.
The key observational discriminant would be a measurement of 
$\dot{G}/G$ at the level of $\sim\!10^{-15}$\,yr$^{-1}$ or a 
detection of time variation in the dark-energy equation of state 
$w_a \neq 0$ \cite{DESI2024}.






























%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%




\section{Numerical algorithms}
\label{app:algorithms}

This appendix summarises the computational procedures used to generate
the figures in this paper.  Full source code (Python~3 with NumPy,
SciPy, and Matplotlib) is publicly available at
\url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code} .

\subsection{Galaxy rotation curves}

The baryonic rotation velocity is constructed from three components:

\paragraph{Stellar disk.}
The Freeman~(1970) \cite{Freeman1970} exact formula for an exponential
disc of mass $M_\star$ and scale length $R_d$:
\begin{equation}
v_{\rm disc}^2(r) = \frac{G M_\star\, r^2}{2 R_d^3}
  \bigl[I_0(x)\,K_0(x) - I_1(x)\,K_1(x)\bigr],
  \qquad x = \frac{r}{2R_d}\,,
\end{equation}
where $I_n$ and $K_n$ are modified Bessel functions of the first and
second kind.

\paragraph{Bulge.}
The Hernquist~(1990) \cite{Hernquist1990} profile with mass $M_b$ and
scale radius $r_b$:
\begin{equation}
v_{\rm bul}^2(r) = \frac{G M_b\, r}{(r + r_b)^2}\,.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Gas disc.}
Treated as an independent exponential disk with mass $M_{\rm gas}$
(including a factor 1.33 for He).

\paragraph{ECT total velocity.}
\begin{equation}
v_{\rm ECT}^2(r) = \sqrt{1 + (r/r_0)^2}
  \;\bigl(v_{\rm disc}^2 + v_{\rm gas}^2 + v_{\rm bul}^2\bigr).
\end{equation}

\subsection{Fitting procedure}

The single free parameter $r_0$ is determined by bounded scalar
minimisation (Brent's method) of
\begin{equation}
\chi^2(r_0) = \sum_{i=1}^{N}
  \frac{\bigl(V_{\rm obs}(r_i) - V_{\rm ECT}(r_i;\,r_0)\bigr)^2}
       {\delta V_i^2}\,,
  \qquad r_0 \in [0.01,\,100]\;\text{kpc}.
\end{equation}

The MOND comparison uses the zero-parameter interpolation
function~\eqref{eq:rar} with
$g^\dagger = 1.2 \times 10^{-10}$\,m\,s$^{-2}$.

\subsection{RG running of $\lambda(\mu)$}

The one-loop $\beta$-function (Section~\ref{sec:running_coupling})
is integrated numerically from $\mu = M_{\rm Pl}$ downward using a
standard adaptive Runge--Kutta method, with boundary condition
$\lambda(M_{\rm Pl}) \approx 10^{-3}$.

\subsection{Figure production}

All figures use publication-quality settings: serif font (Times New
Roman), 9\,pt labels, inward tick marks, 220\,dpi output, with
$\texttt{bbox\_inches='tight'}$.

\paragraph{Regime diagram (Fig.~\ref{fig:regime_diagram}).}
The regime diagram plots the Lorentz-order field
$\phi = \ln(\chi/\chi_{\rm vac})$ against
$\log_{10}(g/g_\dagger)$.
The screening boundary is the locus where the chameleon-like
mass $m_\phi(\rho)$ equals the inverse distance to the
nearest mass source; to the right of this boundary (high $\phi$)
gravity is screened and Newtonian.
Representative astrophysical systems are placed at their
estimated $(\phi,\,g/g_\dagger)$ values:
Solar System ($\phi \approx 2.5$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 10^2$),
spiral disk ($\phi \approx 0.5$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 1$),
void dwarf ($\phi \approx -0.5$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 10^{-1.5}$),
cosmic void ($\phi \approx -1$, $g/g_\dagger \sim 10^{-4}$).
The script \texttt{fig\_regime\_diagram.py} in the code
repository produces this figure.





\section{Derivation of the force-law effective dimensionality}
\label{app:deff_method}

\subsection{Definition}

For a gravitational force $g(r)$ obeying
$g \propto 1/r^{d-1}$ in $d$ effective dimensions,
the force-law dimensionality is
\begin{equation}
d_{\rm force}(r) = 1 - \frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}\,.
\label{eq:app_dforce_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{General derivation from $\phi$-closure}

Starting from
\begin{equation}
\mu(x)\,g_{\rm obs} = g_N(r)\,,
\qquad x \equiv g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger\,,
\end{equation}
take the logarithmic derivative with respect to $\ln r$:
\begin{equation}
\frac{d\ln g_N}{d\ln r}
= \left(1 + \frac{d\ln\mu}{d\ln x}\right)
  \frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}\,.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\frac{d\ln g_{\rm obs}}{d\ln r}
= \frac{d\ln g_N/d\ln r}
       {1 + d\ln\mu/d\ln x}\,,
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(r)
= 1 + \frac{p_N(r)}{1 + d\ln\mu/d\ln x}\,,
}
\label{eq:app_dforce_general}
\end{equation}
where $p_N(r) \equiv -d\ln g_N/d\ln r$.

For a point mass, $g_N = GM/r^2$ gives $p_N = 2$.

\subsection{Specific result for $\mu(x) = x/\sqrt{1+x^2}$}

Compute:
\begin{equation}
\ln\mu = \ln x - \tfrac{1}{2}\ln(1+x^2)\,,
\qquad
\frac{d\ln\mu}{d\ln x}
= 1 - \frac{x^2}{1+x^2}
= \frac{1}{1+x^2}\,.
\end{equation}
Substituting into~\eqref{eq:app_dforce_general}:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_{\rm force}(x)
= 1 + \frac{2(1+x^2)}{2+x^2}\,.
}
\label{eq:app_dforce_closed}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Limiting cases}

\begin{tabular}{lcll}
\hline
Regime & $x$ & $d_{\rm force}$ & Physics \\
\hline
Screened & $\gg 1$ & $\to 3$ &
  $g \propto 1/r^2$, Newtonian \\
Transition & $= 1$ & $= 7/3 \approx 2.33$ &
  onset of flat rotation \\
Deep $\phi$-branch & $\ll 1$ & $\to 2$ &
  $g \propto 1/r$, $v_{\rm flat} = \mathrm{const}$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}

\medskip
The rotation velocity $v^2 = r\,g \propto r^{2-d_{\rm force}}$:
\begin{itemize}
\item $d_{\rm force} = 3$: $v \propto r^{-1/2}$ (Keplerian),
\item $d_{\rm force} = 7/3$: $v \propto r^{-1/6}$
  (strongly flattened),
\item $d_{\rm force} = 2.5$: $v \propto r^{-1/4}$
  (transition zone),
\item $d_{\rm force} = 2$: $v = \mathrm{const}$
  (flat rotation).
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Transition radius}

The transition $x = 1$ occurs at
\begin{equation}
r_* = \sqrt{\frac{GM}{g_\dagger(\phi_{\rm env})}}\,.
\end{equation}
Representative values:
$r_*(10^8\,M_\odot) \approx 0.3\,$kpc,
$r_*(5\times10^{10}\,M_\odot) \approx 8\,$kpc,
$r_*(5\times10^{11}\,M_\odot) \approx 24\,$kpc.

\subsection{Distinction from morphological dimensionality}

The force-law dimensionality $d_{\rm force}$ describes
the scaling of the gravitational interaction.
The morphological dimensionality $d_{\rm morph}$
describes the shape of matter distributions
(sheets: $\sim 2$, filaments: $\sim 1$).
They are related through the tidal tensor
$T_{ij} = \partial_i\partial_j\Phi_\phi$:
the number of collapsing eigenvalues of $T_{ij}$
determines $d_{\rm morph} = 3 - N_{\rm collapsed}$.
A quantitative derivation of $d_{\rm morph}$ from
the $\phi$-sector is listed as Open Problem~OP8.

\subsection{Numerical implementation}

Equation~\eqref{eq:app_dforce_closed} is evaluated
analytically.  The mapping $x(r)$ uses the exact
$\phi$-closure solution:
\begin{equation}
g_{\rm obs}^2 =
\frac{g_N^2 + \sqrt{g_N^4 + 4\,g_N^2\,g_\dagger^2}}{2}\,,
\qquad x = g_{\rm obs}/g_\dagger\,.
\end{equation}

The complete Python implementation is available at\\
\url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}.



\section{Cluster lensing: 2D projected $\phi$-closure}
\label{app:cluster_lensing}

This appendix documents the numerical methods, parameters,
and results for the cluster-merger calculations reported in
Section~\ref{sec:fifth_force}.
All code is available at
\url{https://github.com/chufelo/ECT-preprint-code}:
\texttt{cluster\_phi\_solver\_2d.py} (2D projected thin-lens)
and \texttt{calc\_cluster\_lensing.py} (spherical radial
profile).

A minimal projected cluster solver was constructed to test
the $\phi$-branch \emph{beyond} the single-number
approximation $M_{\rm ECT} \approx \mu_{\rm cl}\,M_{\rm bar}$.
The code constructs a baryonic surface-density map from
compact collisionless peaks and diffuse gas peaks, applies
the local thin-lens closure
$g_N \approx 2\pi G\,\Sigma_b$, and converts it into an
effective convergence map $\kappa(x,y)$ through the same
algebraic $\phi$-branch used in the galactic sector.
This is not yet a full merger-scale metric--$\phi$ solution,
but it already yields two non-trivial results: the
\emph{position} of the lensing peaks and the \emph{order of
magnitude} of the lensing enhancement.

In this formulation, the Bullet Cluster becomes a genuine
numerical \emph{near-match} problem rather than a simple
yes/no argument: the offset morphology is reproduced
exactly, and the amplitude deficit is a factor $\sim\!2$--$3$
that may plausibly be closed by uncomputed corrections.

\subsection{Spherical radial $\phi$-closure}

An NFW-like or $\beta$-model baryonic mass profile
$M_{\rm bar}(<r)$ is used to compute
$g_{\rm bar}(r) = GM_{\rm bar}(<r)/r^2$ at each radius.
The algebraic $\phi$-closure
$\mu(g/g_\dagger)\,g = g_{\rm bar}$ is then solved for
$g_{\rm obs}(r)$, giving the enhancement
$\mu_\phi(r) = g_{\rm obs}/g_{\rm bar}$ and the effective
mass $M_{\rm ECT}(<r) = \mu_\phi(r)\,M_{\rm bar}(<r)$.
For spherical symmetry, this algebraic closure is the
\emph{exact} solution of the AQUAL-type field equation
(by Gauss's law), so no spatial discretisation is needed.
This approach is best suited for \emph{amplitude} estimates
with realistic baryon profiles.
Results: Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results}.

\subsection{2D projected thin-lens $\phi$-closure}

For merging clusters the spherical approximation breaks down
because the baryonic mass is distributed among spatially separated
components.  The 2D projected approach decomposes the baryonic
surface density into compact collisionless clumps and diffuse
X-ray gas:
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_b(x,y) = \Sigma_\star(x,y) + \Sigma_{\rm gas}(x,y)\,.
\end{equation}
Each component is represented by a sum of Gaussian peaks:
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_\star(x,y) = \sum_{i=1}^{N_\star}
\frac{M_{\star,i}}{2\pi s_{\star,i}^2}
\exp\!\left[
-\frac{(x-x_{\star,i})^2+(y-y_{\star,i})^2}{2s_{\star,i}^2}
\right],
\end{equation}
and similarly for gas peaks with masses $M_{{\rm gas},j}$
and widths $s_{{\rm gas},j}$.

In thin-lens approximation the projected Newtonian field
is~\cite{Clowe2006}
\begin{equation}
g_N(x,y) \approx 2\pi G\,\Sigma_b(x,y)\,,
\end{equation}
and the same algebraic $\phi$-closure as in the galactic
sector is applied locally:
\begin{equation}
\mu\!\left(\frac{g}{g_\dagger^{\rm cl}}\right)g = g_N\,,
\qquad
\mu(x) = \frac{x}{\sqrt{1+x^2}}\,.
\end{equation}
Solving for the enhancement factor gives
\begin{equation}
\nu(y) \equiv \frac{g}{g_N}
= \sqrt{\frac{1+\sqrt{1+4/y^2}}{2}}\,,
\qquad y = \frac{g_N}{g_\dagger^{\rm cl}}\,.
\label{eq:nu_cluster}
\end{equation}
The effective projected surface density for lensing is
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_{\rm eff}(x,y) = \nu\!\left(\frac{g_N}{g_\dagger^{\rm cl}}\right)
\Sigma_b(x,y)\,,
\end{equation}
and the convergence map is
\begin{equation}
\kappa(x,y) = \frac{\Sigma_{\rm eff}(x,y)}{\Sigma_{\rm crit}}\,.
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Important caveat.}
For spherically symmetric systems this algebraic closure
is the exact solution of the AQUAL-type field equation
(by Gauss's law).
For a non-spherical merger the thin-lens sheet approximation
$g_N \approx 2\pi G\Sigma_b$ is only a proxy; the full
calculation requires solving
$\nabla\cdot[\mu(|\nabla\Phi|/a_0)\,\nabla\Phi] = 4\pi G\rho_{\rm bar}$
on a 3D grid.
The present results are therefore intermediate between a
single-number global estimate and a full merger-scale
metric--$\phi$ solver (OP22).

\subsection{Cluster parameters}

The parameters below are order-of-magnitude
characterisations consistent with X-ray and lensing
observations.  They should not be interpreted as
precision fits.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{lccccl}
\toprule
Cluster & $M_\star$ & $s_\star$ & $M_{\rm gas}$ &
$s_{\rm gas}$ & Offset \\
 & ($M_\odot$) & (kpc) & ($M_\odot$) & (kpc) & (kpc) \\
\midrule
Bullet (2 sub.) & $2\times5\times10^{12}$ & 70 &
  $6\times10^{13}{+}6\times10^{13}$ & 200--250 & 100--150 \\
MACS~J0025 & $2\times3\times10^{12}$ & 60 &
  $2\times2\times10^{13}$ & 250 & 150 \\
El Gordo & $8{+}5\times10^{12}$ & 60--80 &
  $5{+}3\times10^{13}$ & 280--300 & 200 \\
Abell~520 & $2\times3\times10^{12}$ & 80 &
  $3.5\times10^{13}$ (central) & 180 & 0 (gas core) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Sources: Bullet --- Paraficz et
al.~\cite{Paraficz2016}, Markevitch et
al.~\cite{Markevitch2004};
MACS~J0025 --- Brada\v{c} et al.~\cite{Bradac2008};
El Gordo --- Diego et al.~\cite{Diego2023};
Abell~520 --- Mahdavi et al.~\cite{Mahdavi2007}.

\subsection{Results}

\paragraph{Offset morphology.}

In all four clusters the $\kappa$-peaks of
$\Sigma_{\rm eff}$ track the component with higher
local surface density.
For Bullet, MACS~J0025, and El~Gordo the lensing
peaks coincide with the compact stellar clumps
($d_{\star\to\kappa} < 25\,$kpc), displaced from the
diffuse gas by $\Delta = 130$--$280\,$kpc.
For Abell~520 the lensing peak coincides with the
dense central gas core, as expected when the gas is
more compact than the stellar distribution.
Both morphologies are natural in ECT because the
$\phi$-field responds to local density contrast, not
to a universal collisionless species.

\paragraph{Total lensing amplitude.}

The integrated effective mass within standard apertures
yields $M_{\rm ECT}/M_{\rm obs} \approx 0.15$--$0.30$
for the 2D Gaussian profiles, and $\approx 0.34$--$0.45$
for the more realistic spherical $\beta$-model
(Table~\ref{tab:bullet_results}).
The range reflects systematic differences in baryonic
modelling, not different physics.
The enhancement factor $\mu_\phi \approx 1.1$--$1.7$
is modest because the thin-lens projected $g_N$ at
cluster-core radii ($R \lesssim 250\,$kpc) places
the system near the screened regime
($g_N/g_\dagger \sim 1$).
At larger radii ($R \gtrsim 500\,$kpc) where
$g_N/g_\dagger < 0.1$ the enhancement rises to
$\mu_\phi \sim 3$--$5$, but less baryonic mass is
enclosed there.

The deficit factor $\sim\!2$--$3$ (using the $\beta$-model) is comparable to
the well-known MOND cluster mass discrepancy
(factor $\sim\!2$).
Whether this can be closed by a full 3D solver,
environmental $g_\dagger$ modulation, or gravitational
slip is an open question (OP22, OP23).

\subsection{Sensitivity to baryonic modelling}

For the Bullet Cluster, the spherical $\beta$-model
gives $M_{\rm ECT}/M_{\rm obs} \approx 0.45$ at $R = 250\,$kpc,
while the 2D Gaussian thin-lens gives $\approx 0.27$.
The difference arises because the $\beta$-model concentrates
more baryonic mass at small radii, producing higher local
$g_{\rm bar}$ and absolute $M_{\rm ECT}$, while the
Gaussian profiles have less total mass within the same aperture.
Both are order-of-magnitude estimates.
The range $M_{\rm ECT}/M_{\rm obs} \approx 0.15$--$0.45$
across approaches and apertures brackets the true answer,
which requires a full 3D merger-scale computation (OP22).

The $\phi$-branch explains approximately one-third to
one-half of the observed lensing mass using the more
realistic $\beta$-model baryon profile.
The deficit factor is $\sim\!2$--$3$,
comparable to the MOND cluster mass discrepancy and
within the expected accuracy of these order-of-magnitude
estimates.


\section{Supplementary numerical calculations}
\label{app:supplementary}

\subsection{$G_N$ in SI}
The reduced Planck mass in SI units is
$\bar{M}_{\rm Pl} = 2.435\times10^{18}\;\mathrm{GeV}/c^2
= 2.435\times10^{18}\times1.783\times10^{-27}\;\mathrm{kg}
= 4.341\times10^{-9}\;\mathrm{kg}$.
Then (canonical normalisation $\alpha=2$, $\beta=1$, so $v_0=\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}$)
\begin{equation}
G_N \;=\; \frac{\hbar\,c}{8\pi\,\bar{M}_{\rm Pl}^2}
\;=\; \frac{1.055\times10^{-34}\times2.998\times10^{8}}
{8\pi\times(4.341\times10^{-9})^2}
\;\approx\; 6.678\times10^{-11}\;\mathrm{m^3\,kg^{-1}\,s^{-2}}.
\end{equation}
CODATA value: $G_N = 6.674\times10^{-11}\;\mathrm{m^3\,kg^{-1}\,s^{-2}}$.
The $0.06\%$ discrepancy reflects rounding in the input constants.
